Cancelling a Lease Mid-Month: When Does It Take Effect?
Ruling on effective timing of lease cancellation when declared mid-month.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on cancelling an ijarah contract mid-month and explain the difference between the majority view and the view of Muhammad Abu Nasir.

Core Idea
A lease cancellation declared mid-month does not end the lease immediately; it takes effect at month's end according to one opinion.

When a lessor cancels an ijarah (lease) partway through a month, the timing of the cancellation's effectiveness is critical. This passage from al-Zayla'i's Tabyin al-Haqa'iq presents the primary ruling that the contract continues, with a notable exception attributed to Muhammad Abu Nasir ibn Yahya ibn Salam.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act
The lessor cancels the lease during the month (fi athna' al-shahr). Recognize that this is a unilateral cancellation (faskh).
2
State the primary ruling
According to the majority, 'lam yanfasikh' – it does not cancel. The contract remains in effect.
This is the mufta bihi position.
3
Note the alternative view
There is a view (qil) that the cancellation takes effect when the month ends, because it can be aligned to a time when the lessor has the right to cancel.
This was the fatwa of Muhammad Abu Nasir ibn Yahya ibn Salam.
4
Understand the reasoning
The cancellation can be attached (yattasilu) to a future time, analogous to the contract itself being valid when attached to a future time.
The word 'mudafan' (attached) is key.
5
Consider explicit wording
If the lessor expressly says 'I cancelled at the beginning of the month', the cancellation takes effect at the beginning immediately, because the contract can be attached to the past? Actually it says 'yansakh idha ahalla al-shahr' meaning it cancels when the month begins, i.e., it is attached to the beginning.
This shows that the cancellation can be made effective from an earlier point by explicit wording.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولو فسخ في أثناء الشهر لم ينفسخ، وقيل : ينفسخ به إذا خرج الشهر؛ لأنه أمكن توفيقه إلى وقت يملك فيه الفسخ، وبه كان يفتي محمد أبو نصير بن يحيى بن سلام. ولو قال : في أثناء الشهرِ فسخت رأس الشهر ينفسخ إذا أهل الشهر بلا شبهة، فيكون فسخاً مضافاً إلى رأس الشهر، وعقد الإجارة، ويصح مضافاً، فكذا فسخه. كذا في «تبيين الحقائق للعلامة الزيلعي».
And if he cancels during the month, it does not cancel, and it is said: it cancels when the month ends, because it is possible to align it to a time when he has the right to cancel, and this was the fatwa of Muhammad Abu Nasir ibn Yahya ibn Salam. And if he says: during the month I have cancelled at the beginning of the month, it cancels when the month begins without doubt, so it becomes a cancellation attached to the beginning of the month, and the lease contract is valid as attached, so similarly its cancellation. Thus in 'Tabyin al-Haqa'iq' by al-Zayla'i.
Source pages p. 548

Commentary
This passage deals with the effect of cancelling an ijarah contract mid-month. The primary ruling is that cancellation during the month does not take effect immediately; the contract remains. However, there is a view (qil) that it does take effect when the month ends. This view was followed by Muhammad Abu Nasir ibn Yahya ibn Salam in his fatwa. The reasoning is that the cancellation can be aligned to a time when the lessor has the right to cancel (i.e., at month's end). Additionally, if the lessor explicitly says 'I have cancelled at the beginning of the month' while still in mid-month, it effectively cancels at the beginning since the contract can be attached to a future time. This is analogous to the contract itself being valid when attached to a future time.

Key Terms
فسخ (faskh): Cancellation or rescission of a contract unilaterally.
مضافاً (mudafan): Attached or appended to a specific time.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a lessor says 'I cancel the lease' on the 15th of the month, when does the cancellation take effect according to the primary Hanafi ruling?
A) Immediately.
B) At the end of the current month.
C) At the end of the lease term.
D) It does not take effect at all.

Key Takeaway
The effectiveness of a mid-term lease cancellation is delayed under Hanafi law, with the primary view holding that the contract remains until the agreed period ends.

Calculating Lease Months When Ijarah Begins Mid-Month
Intra-Hanafi dispute on lease term calculation mid-month.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the two Hanafi positions on calculating months in ijarah when the contract starts mid-month and apply the mufta bihi position to a given scenario.

Core Idea
When an ijarah starts mid-month, the first month is counted as 30 days, then actual lunar months follow – the Sahibayn's view prevails.

This passage from 'Umdat al-Ri'aya addresses a practical problem in ijarah: how to count months when the lease begins in the middle of a lunar month. The Hanafi school has two positions on this issue: one from Imam Abu Hanifa and another from the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Imam Muhammad). In this lesson, we will trace the dispute, its proof, and the operative ruling for fatwa.

Guided Path
1
State the scenario and the issue
Identify that the lease begins mid-month, so the first month is incomplete. The question is how to count the entire lease term.
The passage distinguishes between contracts made at the beginning of a month (use lunar months) and mid-month (use days for first month).
2
Identify the Hanafi position
Abu Hanifa holds that all months are counted as 30 days each, making a year 360 days.
This view is also reported from Abu Yusuf, and from al-Shafi'i and Ahmad.
3
Identify the Sahibayn's position
Abu Yusuf and Muhammad hold that only the first month is counted as 30 days (by days), and the remaining months are counted by actual lunar months.
This is also reported from Abu Yusuf and Muhammad, and from al-Shafi'i and Ahmad.
4
Compare the proofs
Abu Hanifa's proof relies on convenience and uniformity. The Sahibayn rely on Quran 2:189, which makes lunar months the original standard.
The commentator notes that days are resorted to only out of necessity for the incomplete first month.
5
Apply the mufta bihi
The relied-upon position is that of the Sahibayn. Use this to calculate the end date of a lease.
Example: lease on 10th Dhu al-Hijjah for one year ends on the 10th of Dhu al-Hijjah next year if the month has 30 days, or on the 9th if it has 29 days.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فإن كان حين يهل اعتبر الأهلة، وإلا فالأيام كالعدة (١) : أي إن كان عقد الإجارة عند الإهلال تعتبر الأهلة، وإن كان في أثناء الشهر فعند أبي حنيفة يعتبر الكل بالأيام، كل شهر ثلاثون، وعندهما يعتبر الأول بالأيام والباقي بالأهلة، فإن أَجْرَ في عاشر ذي الحجةِ سنةً، فعند أبي حنيفة له يقع على ثلاثمئة وستين يوماً. وعندهما الشهر الأوَّلُ يعتبر بالأيام، وهو ثلاثون يوماً، فذو الحجة إن تم على ثلاثين يوماً فالسِّنةُ تتم على عاشر ذي الحجة، وإن تم على تسعة وعشرين، [١] قوله : حين يهل؛ ليس المراد بقولهم حين يهلّ الهلال في هذه المسألة معناه الحقيقي، وهو أول الليلة من الشهر، بل المراد معناه العرقي وهو اليوم الأول من أشهر. كذا في «النتائج»). [٢] قوله : تعتبر الأهلة في شهور السنة كلّها؛ لأنها هي الأصل في الشهور العربية، قال الله : يَسْتَلُونَكَ عَنِ الْأَهِلَّةِ قُلْ هِيَ مَوَاقِيتُ لِلنَّاسِ وَالْحَج (٣) ، فلا يعدل عن الأصل بقدر الإمكان. [٣]قوله : فعند أبي حنيفة له، وهو رواية عن أبي يوسف، وقول للشافعي، ورواية عن أحمد الله ذكره العلامة السُّمُنِّي [٤] قوله : وعندهما؛ وذكر السمني ) : إنه قول محمد، ورواية عن أبي يوسف، وقول الشافعي، ورواية عن أحمد . [٠]قوله : يعتبر...الخ؛ لأن الأصل في اعتبار الشهر الأهلة والأيام، يصار إليها ضرورة، ألا ترى ما قال : «صوموا لرؤيته وأفطروا لرؤيته، فإن غم عليكم فاقدروا له».
If it is at the time of the new moon, the lunar months are considered, otherwise the days are like the count (of thirty). (Explanation:) That is, if the lease contract is at the appearance of the new moon, the lunar months are considered; if it is mid-month, then according to Abu Hanifa the whole is considered by days, each month thirty days, and according to them (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) the first month is considered by days, and the rest by lunar months. So if he leases on the 10th of Dhu al-Hijjah for a year, according to Abu Hanifa it falls on 360 days. According to them, the first month is considered by days, which is thirty days, so if Dhu al-Hijjah completes thirty days, the year completes on the 10th of Dhu al-Hijjah, and if it completes twenty-nine days, ... [1] His saying: 'when he sees the new moon' – the intended meaning is not the literal meaning of the first night of the month, but rather the customary meaning, which is the first day of the months. Thus in 'al-Nata'ij'. [2] His saying: 'The lunar months are considered in all the months of the year' because they are the basis for the Arabic months. Allah said: 'They ask you about the new moons. Say: They are timings for people and for Hajj' (Quran 2:189). So one does not deviate from the origin as much as possible. [3] His saying: 'According to Abu Hanifa' – it is a narration from Abu Yusuf, and a saying of al-Shafi'i, and a narration from Ahmad. al-Samunni mentioned it. [4] His saying: 'According to them' – al-Samunni said: It is the saying of Muhammad, and a narration from Abu Yusuf, and a saying of al-Shafi'i, and a narration from Ahmad. [0] His saying: '... is considered' – because the origin for considering the month is lunar months and days, but days are resorted to out of necessity. Do you not see that he said: 'Fast at its sighting and break the fast at its sighting, and if it is cloudy, then estimate it.'
Source pages p. 549

Commentary
This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the calculation of months in an ijarah contract when the lease begins mid-month. The matn states: if the contract is made at the time of the new moon (i.e., at the beginning of a lunar month), the months are counted by the actual lunar months. If it is made mid-month, then the ruling differs: Imam Abu Hanifa holds that all months are counted as thirty days each, making a year 360 days. The Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Imam Muhammad) hold that only the first month is counted as thirty days (since it is incomplete), and the subsequent months are counted by the actual lunar months. The commentator clarifies that 'halla' here means the first day of the month, not the actual sighting. The justification for the Sahibayn's view is that the lunar months are the original standard (as indicated by Quran 2:189), and resorting to days is only due to necessity. The commentator also notes that Abu Hanifa's view is also reported from Abu Yusuf, and is the view of al-Shafi'i and Ahmad, while the Sahibayn's view is reported from Muhammad and also from Abu Yusuf, and is the view of al-Shafi'i and Ahmad as well. The practical example: if someone leases on the 10th of Dhu al-Hijjah for one year, according to Abu Hanifa the term ends after 360 days. According to the Sahibayn, the first month (the remainder of Dhu al-Hijjah) is counted as 30 days, then the next 11 months are lunar months, so the term ends on the 10th of Dhu al-Hijjah of the next year if Dhu al-Hijjah has 30 days, or if it has 29 days, the term ends on the 9th? The text is cut but likely it ends on the 9th. The relied-upon position (mufta bihi) in the Hanafi school is the view of the Sahibayn, as it aligns with the original lunar standard.

Key Terms
إهلال (ihlal): The appearance of the new moon; in this context, it refers to the first day of the lunar month.
أهلة (ahilla): Plural of hilal; new moons, used to denote lunar months.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Sahibayn, when a lease begins mid-month, the first month is counted as:
A) the actual remaining days in that month.
B) a full 30-day period.
C) the next lunar month.
D) 29 days.

Key Takeaway
When an ijarah begins mid-month, the Hanafi mufta bihi calculates the first month as 30 days and the rest by actual lunar months.

Counting Months in Ijarah When Contract Begins Mid-Month
Ruling on counting months in ijarah when contract is made during a month.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi positions on counting months in ijarah when the contract begins mid-month and evaluate the proof for Abu Hanifa's view.

Core Idea
If ijarah starts mid-month, Abu Hanifa counts all months as 30 days; the two companions only the first month by days.

This passage from 'Umdat al-Ri'ayah explains how to determine the lease period when an ijarah contract is signed in the middle of a lunar month. The matn gives a concise rule, and the commentator expands on the intra-Hanafi dispute between Abu Hanifa and his two companions, with proofs from Quran, hadith, and qiyas on 'iddah. Understanding this ikhtilaf is essential for correctly fixing the end date of a lease.

Guided Path
1
Identify the matn's ruling
The matn states: 'If at the appearance of the crescent, crescents are considered; otherwise, days are like the 'iddah.' This means if the contract is at month-start, use actual lunar months; if mid-month, use days.
The 'otherwise' triggers the ikhtilaf.
2
State the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf
Abu Hanifa counts all months by days (30 each = 360 days for a year). Abu Yusuf and Muhammad count only the first incomplete month by days, then actual crescents for the rest.
The dispute is about how far necessity extends.
3
Examine the proof for the two companions
They cite Quran 2:189 making crescents the primary time markers, and the hadith 'complete Sha'ban' showing that months are normally by crescents. Days are only for necessity, limited to the first month.
The hadith is used to support the rule.
4
Examine the proof for Abu Hanifa
He uses qiyas on 'iddah: if divorce is mid-month, the waiting period is counted by days throughout. Similarly, once days are used for the first month, the remainder is also by days for consistency (each month 30 days).
This analogy makes the calculation fixed and predictable.
5
Identify the mufta bihi position
The commentator marks Abu Hanifa's view as 'al-mukhtar' (the chosen one). It is also reported from Abu Yusuf and adopted by al-Shafi'i and Ahmad.
So the relied-upon fatwa is that the total is 360 days for a one-year lease.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الإجارة باب الإجارة الفاسدة
فإن كان حين يهل اعتبر الأهلة، وإلا فالأيام كالعدة
فإن كان حين يهل اعتبر الأهلة ، وإلا فالأيام كالعدة) : أي إن كان عقد الإجارة عند الإهلال تعتبر الأهلة ، وإن كان في أثناء الشهر فعند أبي حنيفة " يعتبر الكل بالأيام ، كل شهر ثلاثون، وعندهما يعتبر الأول بالأيام والباقي بالأهلة ، فإن أَجْرَ في عاشر ذي الحجَّةِ سنةً، فعند أبي حنيفة له يقع على ثلاثمئة وستين يوماً.
وعندهما الشهر الأوَّلُ يعتبر بالأيام ، وهو ثلاثون يوماً، فذو الحجة إن تم على ثلاثين يوماً فالسِّنةُ تتم على عاشر ذي الحجة، وإن تم على تسعة وعشرين، قوله : حين يهل ؛ ليس المراد بقولهم حين يهلّ الهلال في هذه المسألة معناه الحقيقي، وهو أول الليلة من الشهر، بل المراد معناه العرقي وهو اليوم الأول من أشهر. كذا في «النتائج»). قوله : تعتبر الأهلة في شهور السنة كلّها ؛ لأنها هي الأصل في الشهور العربية، قال الله : يَسْتَلُونَكَ عَنِ الْأَهِلَّةِ قُلْ هِيَ مَوَاقِيتُ لِلنَّاسِ وَالْحَج، فلا يعدل عن الأصل بقدر الإمكان. قوله : فعند أبي حنيفة له ، وهو رواية عن أبي يوسف، وقول للشافعي، ورواية عن أحمد ذكره العلامة السُّمُنِّي قوله : وعندهما ؛ وذكر السمني : إنه قول محمد، ورواية عن أبي يوسف، وقول الشافعي، ورواية عن أحمد .
قوله : يعتبر...الخ ؛ لأن الأصل في اعتبار الشهر الأهلة والأيام، يصار إليها ضرورة، ألا ترى ما قال : «صوموا لرؤيته وأفطروا لرؤيته ، فإن غم عليكم فأكملوا عدة شعبان (حديث) ، رواه البخاري ومسلم ، ولا تعذر إلا في الشهر الواحد، وهو الشهر الأول، وقد أمكن تكميله من الأخير، فيكمل، وبقي غيره على الأصل. ولأبي حنيفة : إن الشهر الأول يتم بأيامه وبليله من الشهر المتصل به، فيبتدأ الشهر الثاني بالأيام ضرورة، وهكذا إلى آخر المدة كل شهر ثلاثون يوماً، والسنة ثلاثمئة وستون يوماً. وهذا نظير ما في العدة، فإن الطلاق إن كان في أوّل الشهر يعتبر الشهور بالأهلة، وإن كان في الوسط فبالأيام في حق التفريق، وفي حق العدة أيضاً كذلك عند الإمام ، وعندهما يكمل الأوّل بالآخر، والمتوسطات بالأهلة.
Book of Ijarah, Chapter of Void Ijarah. If (the contract is made) at the time when the crescent appears, the crescents are considered; otherwise, the days are like the 'iddah (waiting period). That is, if the ijarah contract is at the appearance of the crescent, the crescents are considered; and if during the month, then according to Abu Hanifa the entire period is considered by days, each month thirty days; and according to the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), the first month is considered by days and the rest by crescents. If he rents in the tenth of Dhul-Hijjah for a year, then according to Abu Hanifa it falls on 360 days. And according to the two, the first month is considered by days, and it is thirty days; so if Dhul-Hijjah completes thirty days, the year ends on the tenth of Dhul-Hijjah; and if it completes twenty-nine... His saying: 'when the crescent appears' does not mean the literal meaning of the crescent appearing, which is the first night of the month, but rather the customary meaning, which is the first day of the months. This is in Al-Nata'ij. His saying: 'the crescents are considered in all months of the year' because they are the basis in the Arabic months, Allah said: 'They ask you about the crescents. Say: They are time markers for people and for Hajj' (2:189), so one should not deviate from the basis as much as possible. His saying: 'according to Abu Hanifa' is a narration from Abu Yusuf, and a saying of al-Shafi'i, and a narration from Ahmad, mentioned by al-Samani. His saying: 'according to the two' and al-Samani mentioned that it is the saying of Muhammad, and a narration from Abu Yusuf, and a saying of al-Shafi'i, and a narration from Ahmad. His saying: 'he considers... etc.' because the basis in considering the month is the crescents, and days are resorted to by necessity. Do you not see what he said: 'Fast on its sighting and break fast on its sighting, and if it is obscured, then complete the count of Sha'ban' narrated by Bukhari and Muslim, and it is not excused except in one month, which is the first month, and it can be completed from the last, so it is completed, and the rest remain on the basis. And according to Abu Hanifa: the first month is completed by its days and its night from the month connected to it, so the second month begins with days by necessity, and so on until the end of the period, each month thirty days, and the year 360 days. And this is similar to what is in 'iddah: if divorce is at the beginning of the month, the months are considered by crescents; if in the middle, then by days regarding separation, and in the case of 'iddah also similarly according to the Imam, and according to the two, the first is completed by the last, and the middle ones by crescents.
Source pages p. 549

Commentary
This passage from the commentary on Al-Wiqayah explains a ruling on void ijarah (leasing) regarding the counting of months when the contract's start falls in the middle of a month. The matn states: 'If (the contract is made) at the time when the crescent appears, the crescents are considered; otherwise, the days are like the 'iddah (waiting period).' The commentator clarifies that if the ijarah contract is concluded at the start of a month (i.e., when the crescent appears), then the lease period is calculated by actual lunar months. If it is concluded in the middle of a month, then there is a dispute within the Hanafi school: Abu Hanifa counts the entire period by days, each month being 30 days, effectively making the lease term 360 days for a year. The two companions (Abu Yusuf and Imam Muhammad) hold that only the first incomplete month is counted by days, and the remaining months are counted by actual lunar months. For example, if a lease begins on the 10th of Dhul-Hijjah, Abu Hanifa would fix the end at 360 days later, while the companions would consider the first month as 30 days (starting from the 10th), and then count subsequent months by lunar sightings, with the year ending on the 10th of Dhul-Hijjah if that month completes 30 days, or on the 11th if it completes 29 days (thus avoiding a repeat of Eid al-Adha). The commentator then provides the proof: the Quranic verse (2:189) establishes crescents as time markers, so lunar months are the basis. However, necessity requires resorting to days when the starting point is in the middle of a month. The hadith about completing Sha'ban's count when the crescent is obscured supports the use of days for one month when needed. Abu Hanifa's view is analogized to the 'iddah (waiting period) of divorce: if the divorce occurs at the beginning of a month, lunar months are used; if in the middle, days are used. The relied-upon position (al-mukhtar) is that of Abu Hanifa, as indicated in the commentary. The passage also notes that Abu Hanifa's view here is also narrated from Abu Yusuf and is the position of al-Shafi'i and Ahmad.

Key Terms
يهل (yuhill): Here it means 'when the crescent appears' as a time indicator for the beginning of a lunar month.
العدة (al-ʿiddah): The waiting period for a divorced or widowed woman, used here as an analogy for the method of counting months when the start is mid-month.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the relied-upon view (mufta bihi) in the Hanafi school, how are months counted if an ijarah contract begins mid-month?
A) All months are counted by actual lunar crescents.
B) Only the first month is counted by days; the rest by crescents.
C) All months are counted by days (30 days each).
D) The counting depends on the mutual agreement of the parties.

Key Takeaway
When an ijarah contract begins mid-month, the Hanafi mufta bihi (Abu Hanifa) counts all months as 30 days, making the lease period a fixed number of days (e.g., 360 for a year), while the two companions only do so for the first month.

The Permissibility of Hiring a Bathhouse and Cupper
Ruling on permissibility with evidence and objections

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on hiring a bathhouse and cupper, explain the primary evidence, and evaluate objections based on uncertainty.

Core Idea
What Muslims customarily deem good is legally permissible, overriding contractual uncertainty.

This lesson explores why the Hanafi school permits hiring a bathhouse (hammam) and a cupper (hajjam) despite apparent uncertainty in the contract. You'll see how the principle of 'urf (custom) and necessity overcomes the objection of jahalah, supported by a key hadith about communal consensus.

Guided Path
1
Identify the primary ruling
State that hiring a bathhouse and cupper is permissible (mubah) in the Hanafi school. The text begins: 'And the hiring of the bathhouse and the cupper... their hiring is valid.'
This is the mufta bihi position from later Hanafi authorities.
2
Examine the primary evidence
The key dalil is the hadith of Ibn Mas'ud (mauquf) that 'what the Muslims see as good is good in the sight of Allah'. This supports the validity of hiring based on the widespread custom of Muslims.
The hadith is cited from Ahmad, al-Bazzar, al-Tayalisi, and al-Tabarani.
3
Address the objection of jahalah
Some argue that the bathhouse contract involves ignorance (jahalah) about the amount of water used or time, which normally invalidates ijara. The author responds that such uncertainty is overlooked due to necessity (darurah) and the established custom (urf).
The text explicitly refutes the objection: 'It is not considered due to necessity and the custom of the Muslims.'
4
Consider differing opinions
Some scholars disliked (kariha) hiring bathhouses, especially for women, citing reports from Uthman and Aisha. The author rebuts by interpreting those as concerns about exposure of 'awrah, not a prohibition of the contract itself.
The correct view permits both men and women due to equal or greater need for women (e.g., menstruation, postpartum).
5
Conclude the mufta bihi
The relied-upon position (mufta bihi) is that there is no harm in hiring bathhouses for both sexes, and the practice is permissible (mubah). This is the view of the later Hanafi masters (mutakhkhirin).
Authority weight: fatawa_mutakhkhirin; tarjih by the author of the commentary.

وإجارة الحمام والحجام
[1]قوله : وإجارة الحمام والحجام ؛ أي وصحٌ إجارتهما، أما إجارة الحمام فلتعارف الناس. وروی أحمد في كتاب السنة من حديث أبي وائل عن ابن مسعود صلى الله عليه وسلم قال : «الله نظر إلى قلوب العباد فاختار له أصحاباً ، فجعلهم أنصار دينه، ووزراء نبيه، فما رآه المسلمون حسناً فهو عند الله حسن، وما رآه المسلمون قبيحاً فهو عند الله قبيح) وهو موقوف حسن لا مفرع، كما وقع من أكثر المصنفين، وأخرجه البزار والطيالسي ، والطَّبَرَانِي ، في ترجمة ابن مسعود ه من «الحلية». و التفصيلُ في المقاصد الحسنة) (3)
و ما استدلوا به من أنه دخل حمام الجحفة، ففيه كلام ؛ لأنه صرّح في مبحث الشمائل الشريفة من «المواهب» أن حديث دخوله حمام الجحفة موضوع. فإن قلت : إن في إجارة الحمام جهالة موجبة ؛ لعدم جوازها. قلت : هي لم تعتبر لمكان الضرورة مع اصطلاح المسلمين. ومن العلماء من كره أخذ أجرة الحمّام، لما روي عن عمارة بن عقبة له أنه قال : قدمت على عثمان بن عفان الله ، فسألني عن حالي فأخبرته أن لي غلاماً وحماماً له غلة، فكرة لي غلّة الحجامين وغلّة الحمام ، وقالوا : إنه بيت الشيطان، وسماه رسول الله : شربيت، فإنّه تكشفُ فيه العورات، وتصبّ فيه الغسالات والنجاسات». ومنهم : من فصل بين حمام الرجال وحمام النساء، وقالوا : يكره إيجار حمام النساء ؛ لأنهن ممنوعات من الخروج، وقد أمرنَ بالقرار في البيوت، فاجتماعهن قل ما يخلو عن الفتن. وقد روي أن نساء دخلن على أم المؤمنين عائشة الصديقة رضي الله عنها ، فقالت: «أنتن من اللاتي يدخلن الحمامات ، وأمرت بإخراجهنّ)) والصحيح أنه لا بأس بنباء الحمامات للرجال والنساء جميعاً للحاجة إليه ؛ لأن النساء يحتجن إليه للاغتسال مثل الرجال ، بل حاجتهن أكثر ؛ لكثرة أسباب الاغتسال في حقهن من الحيض والنفاس والجنابة، واستعمال الماء البارد قد يضر، وقد لا يتمكن من الاستيعاب به ، وإزالة الوسخ مقصود ، وذلك يحصل بدخول الحمام. وكراهة عثمان بن عفان الا الله محمول على أنه كان يؤدّي إلى كشف العورة. ذكره ، وغيره من الكبار.
And the hiring of the bathhouse and the cupper. He said: 'And the hiring of the bathhouse and the cupper' means that their hiring is valid. As for hiring the bathhouse, it is due to the common practice of the people. And Ahmad narrated in the book of Sunnah from the hadith of Abu Wa'il from Ibn Mas'ud (may Allah be pleased with him) that the Prophet (peace be upon him) said: 'Allah looked at the hearts of the servants and chose for Himself companions, making them supporters of His religion and ministers of His Prophet. So what the Muslims see as good is good in the sight of Allah, and what they see as bad is bad in the sight of Allah.' This is a mauquf hadith, hasan, not marfu', as many authors have stated. And it was also narrated by al-Bazzar, al-Tayalisi, and al-Tabarani in the biography of Ibn Mas'ud from al-Hilya. And the detail is in al-Maqasid al-Hasana. And what they adduced from the fact that he (the Prophet) entered the bathhouse of al-Juhfah is subject to discussion, because he explicitly stated in the discussion of the noble characteristics in al-Mawahib that the hadith of his entering the bathhouse of al-Juhfah is fabricated. If you say: In hiring the bathhouse there is an ignorance (jahalah) that necessitates its impermissibility. I say: It is not considered due to necessity and the custom of the Muslims. And among the scholars, some disliked taking the wage of the bathhouse, based on what was narrated from 'Amarah ibn 'Uqbah that he said: 'I came to 'Uthman ibn 'Affan, and he asked about my situation. I informed him that I had a young slave and a bathhouse that produced income, and he disliked for me the income of the cupper and the income of the bathhouse.' And they said: 'It is the house of the devil, and the Messenger of Allah called it a bad place, because private parts are exposed in it, and water from washing and impurities are poured in it.' And among them are those who distinguished between the bathhouse for men and the bathhouse for women, and they said: 'Hiring the bathhouse for women is disliked, because women are forbidden from going out, and they are commanded to stay in their homes, so their gatherings are rarely free from fitnah.' And it has been narrated that some women entered upon the Mother of the Believers, 'A'ishah (may Allah be pleased with her), and she said: 'Are you among those who enter bathhouses?' and ordered them to be expelled. The correct view is that there is no harm in building bathhouses for both men and women due to the need for them, because women need to bathe just like men, indeed their need is greater due to the many causes of bathing in their case from menstruation, postpartum bleeding, and janabah. Using cold water may be harmful, and they may not be able to achieve complete purification with it, and removing dirt is intended, and that is achieved by entering the bathhouse. And the disapproval of 'Uthman ibn 'Affan is interpreted as being due to the exposure of private parts, as mentioned by him and other major scholars.
Source pages p. 550

Commentary
This passage discusses the permissibility of hiring a bathhouse (hamam) and a cupper (hajjam). The author begins by stating that both are valid. For the bathhouse, the basis is the common practice of the Muslims, supported by a hadith that what Muslims deem good is good before Allah. Some critics object that the Prophet entering a bathhouse is fabricated, so that argument fails. Another objection is that hiring a bathhouse involves jahalah (uncertainty) which should render the contract invalid. The author responds that such uncertainty is overlooked due to necessity and the prevailing custom ('urf) of the Muslims. The passage then presents various scholarly opinions: some dislike taking wages from a bathhouse, citing reports from Uthman and others; some differentiate between men's and women's bathhouses, considering women's bathhouses makruh; and others allow both due to need. The author concludes that the correct view is permissibility for both sexes, as women have greater need for bathing. The disapproval of Uthman is interpreted as being due to fear of exposure of 'awrah, not a prohibition of the hiring itself. This ruling is from the mutakhkhirin (later scholars) as it relies on custom and necessity.

Key Terms
الحمام (al-hammam): A public bathhouse where people go to wash with hot water.
الحجام (al-hajjam): A cupper, a practitioner of cupping therapy.
جهالة (jahalah): Ignorance or uncertainty about essential terms of a contract.

Key Terms from Source Passage

D) Ijma of the Companions.

Key Takeaway
Hiring a bathhouse is permissible in the Hanafi school due to necessity and custom, overriding the usual objection of contractual uncertainty.

Renting a Bathhouse (Hammam): Overcoming Uncertainty by Necessity and Custom
Ruling with proof on renting a bathhouse

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on renting a bathhouse, identify the proofs cited, and explain how necessity and custom override the defect of uncertainty (jahalah).

Core Idea
Necessity and custom allow what is normally impermissible: the bathhouse lease overcomes jahalah by urf.

In Hanafi fiqh, a lease contract must have a known benefit and duration. Renting a bathhouse (hammam) seems to involve uncertainty (jahalah) because the amount of water, time, and usage are unspecified. Yet classical Hanafi jurists permitted it, citing the pressing need and the customary practice of Muslims. This lesson unpacks the ruling, its proof, and the scholarly debate, culminating in the detailed fatwa that depends on guarding one's gaze and covering private parts.

Guided Path
1
Identify the core ruling and initial objection
The author begins by stating that renting a bathhouse is permissible despite a potential objection: the contract contains jahalah (uncertainty) which normally makes it invalid.
Jahalah here refers to the unknown quantity of water, time, and usage by customers.
2
Understand the Hanafi response: necessity and custom override jahalah
The author responds: 'It is not considered because of necessity (darurah) and the custom of Muslims (urf).' This is a key Hanafi principle—custom that does not contradict a clear text can remove uncertainty.
This is an application of istihsan (juristic preference) over strict qiyas.
3
Analyze the counter-evidence: hadith and opinions of the Companions
The passage cites a hadith from Aisha (ra) warning against undressing outside the husband's home, and the opinion of Uthman ibn Affan (ra) who disliked bathhouse earnings. These are presented as objections.
The author later interprets these as conditional upon the exposure of private parts, not absolute prohibition.
4
Distinguish between men's and women's bathhouses
Some scholars differentiated: renting a women's bathhouse is more disliked due to greater risk of fitnah. The author notes the correct view is no harm for either gender due to need, especially for women's ghusl obligations.
This shows the Hanafi attention to the specific cause (illah) of prohibition.
5
Synthesize the later detailed opinion (Ibn Abidin)
Ibn Abidin resolves the later absolute dislike by detailing: if one guards his gaze and covers his own private parts, there is no dislike; otherwise, it is disliked for both men and women. This becomes the mufta bihi.
This reflects the evolution of fatwa in changing times (later authorities acknowledging increased moral decay).

The section on Ijarah / Chapter on Invalid Ijarah. Al-Juhfa: there is discussion regarding it because he stated in the chapter on noble characteristics from al-Mawahib that the hadith of entering the bathhouse of al-Juhfa is fabricated. If you say: The leasing of a bathhouse involves uncertainty (jahalah) necessitating its impermissibility. I say: It is not considered due to necessity and the custom of Muslims. Some scholars disliked taking rent for the bathhouse, based on what was narrated from ʿUmarah ibn ʿUqbah: he said, 'I came to ʿUthman ibn ʿAffan, and he asked about my situation; I informed him that I have a slave and a bathhouse with profit, so he disliked for me the profit of the bathhouse. And they said: It is the house of Shaytan, and the Messenger of Allah called it a 'sharbit' (or 'house of evil') because private parts are exposed in it, and washings and impurities are poured in it.' Among them are those who differentiated between a men's bathhouse and a women's bathhouse, saying: It is disliked to lease a women's bathhouse because women are prohibited from going out and have been commanded to stay in their homes, so their gathering is rarely free from temptation. It has been narrated that some women entered upon the Mother of the Believers ʿAishah as-Siddiqah (may Allah be pleased with her), and she said: 'Are you among those who enter bathhouses?' and she ordered them to be expelled. The correct view is that there is no harm in building bathhouses for both men and women due to the need for them, because women need them for bathing like men, rather their need is greater due to many reasons for bathing in their case such as menstruation, postpartum, and janabah. Using cold water may be harmful, and they may not be able to achieve complete cleansing with it, and removal of filth is intended, and that is achieved by entering the bathhouse. The dislike expressed by ʿUthman ibn ʿAffan is interpreted as due to it leading to exposure of the private parts. He mentioned it, along with other great scholars. (Footnote 1: from Abul-Malih al-Hudhali: some women from Homs sought permission to enter upon ʿAishah, and she said: 'Are you among those who enter bathhouses? I heard the Messenger of Allah say: Any woman who removes her clothes in other than her husband's house has torn the veil between her and Allah.' in Sunan Ibn Majah (2:1234), Sunan ad-Darimi (2:365), Musnad Ahmad (6:267), authenticated by our teacher al-Arna'ut. Footnote 2: in at-Tabyin (5:123-124).) Zubdat an-Nihayah li ʿUmdat ar-Riʿayah. He said in al-Ashbah: It is disliked for her to enter the bathhouse according to one opinion, and it is said: except if she is ill or postpartum, and the relied-upon is that there is no dislike absolutely. End quote. He said in ad-Durr al-Mukhtar: In our time there is no doubt about the dislike absolutely due to the realization of exposing the private parts. End quote. ʿAllamah ash-Shami said in his gloss on ad-Durr al-Mukhtar: The author of this is Ibn al-Humam. I say: This is not specific to women's bathhouses, for in our lands the exposure of real and gross private parts is realized from the sinful common men, so what is appropriate is detail: if the one entering lowers his gaze such that he does not see anyone's private parts and does not expose his own private parts to anyone, then there is no dislike absolutely. Otherwise, there is dislike for entering both groups, as the cause is what was mentioned. End quote.

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof discussing the permissibility of renting a bathhouse (hammam). The author begins by addressing a potential objection: the lease of a bathhouse contains uncertainty (jahalah) due to unknown usage, which normally renders the contract invalid. He responds that this uncertainty is overlooked due to necessity (darurah) and customary practice (urf) of Muslims. He then presents the views of scholars who disliked taking rent for a bathhouse, citing a narration from Uthman ibn Affan (ra) who disliked the earnings of a cupper and a bathhouse. They also quote that the Prophet (saw) called it a 'house of evil' due to exposure of private parts and presence of impurities. Some scholars differentiate between men's and women's bathhouses, deeming it disliked to lease women's bathhouses due to fear of fitnah. A hadith from Aisha (ra) is mentioned where she expelled women who entered bathhouses. The author then states the correct view: there is no harm in building bathhouses for both genders due to need, especially for women who require them for ghusl (menstruation, postpartum, janabah). The dislike expressed by Uthman is interpreted as applying to cases where it leads to exposure of private parts. Later, the passage cites al-Ashbah, ad-Durr al-Mukhtar, and Ibn Abidin's commentary on the ruling for women. The relied-upon view is no absolute dislike, but due to widespread exposure of private parts in later times, dislike is reinforced. Ibn Abidin resolves by detailing that if one guards his gaze and covers his own private parts, there is no dislike; otherwise, it is disliked for both men and women.

Key Terms
الحمام (al-hammam): A public bathhouse where people bathe using hot water and steam.
الإجارة الفاسدة (al-ijarah al-fasidah): An invalid lease contract due to a defect such as uncertainty (jahalah) or prohibited element.
جهالة (jahalah): Uncertainty or ambiguity in the contract terms that can cause invalidity.

Key Takeaway
Renting a bathhouse is permissible in the Hanafi school despite jahalah, because necessity and custom override the defect, but the actual use must guard against exposure of private parts.

Hiring a Cupper: Abrogation of the Prohibition
Proves permissibility of hiring a cupper despite hadith calling its earnings evil

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi position on hiring a cupper and evaluate the Zahiri objection using the concept of abrogation.

Core Idea
The Prophet's own payment to the cupper abrogates any prior prohibition on his earnings.

The Hanafi school permits hiring a cupper (hajjam) despite a hadith that calls his earnings 'khabith' (evil). This lesson unpacks the evidence: the Prophet himself was cupped and paid the cupper, and a later hadith explicitly allows feeding one's family from such earnings. The apparent contradiction is resolved through the principle of abrogation (naskh), a key tool in Hanafi usul.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify the ruling: hiring a cupper is permissible (ja'iz) and the contract is valid.
This is the mufta bihi position in the Hanafi school.
2
Identify the opponent and their proof
The Zahiriyyah (literalist school) argue it is impermissible, citing the hadith from Rafi' ibn Khadij: 'Kash al-hajjam khabith' (the earnings of the cupper are evil).
They also cite prohibitions on stud fees and miller's measures.
3
Follow the opponent's proof
Examine the proof: the hadith explicitly uses the word 'khabith' (impure, forbidden). How does this lead to impermissibility?
Zahiriyyah take the literal meaning without considering context or later evidence.
4
Analyze the Hanafi response
The Hanafi response is that the prohibition hadith is abrogated (mansukh) by a later hadith where the Prophet (saw) permitted a man to feed his family from his cupper slave's earnings.
Also, the Prophet's own act of paying the cupper is cited as evidence that he would not pay for something forbidden.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical difference: Hanafis allow ijarah (hire) of a cupper; Zahiriyyah consider the contract invalid and the earnings unlawful.
This affects daily transactions for medical cupping.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأما إجارة الحجام فلما رواه البخاري له مسنداً إلى ابن عباس : «إنه احجتمَ وأعطى الحجام أجرة » ) ، ولو علم كراهة لم يعطه، وفي رواية «السنن»: ولو علمه خبيثاً لم يعطه ؛ لأنه كما لا يحلّ لأحدٍ أكل الحرام لا يحل له دفعه إلى غيره ليأكله. وقالت الظاهرية : لا تجوز هذه الإجارة ؛ لأنه نهـي عـن عـسـب التيس ، وكسب الحجام، وقفيز الطحان ، وروي عن رافع بن خديج له أن رسول الله ، قال : «كسب الحجّام خبيث ، وثمن الكلب خبيث ، ومهر البغي خبيث . والجواب : إن حديث النهي منسوخ بما روي أنه قال له رجل: «إن لي عيالاً وغلاماً حجاماً ، فأطعم عيالي من كسبه ، قال : نعم ، ذكر الزيلعي في «شرح الكنز» هذا الحديث.
As for hiring the cupper (hajjam), it is based on what al-Bukhari narrated with chain to Ibn ʿAbbas: 'He had himself cupped and gave the cupper his fee.' Had he known it was disliked, he would not have given it. In another narration of as-Sunan: 'Had he known it was evil, he would not have given it, because just as it is not permissible for anyone to eat the forbidden, it is not permissible for him to give it to another to eat.' The Zahiriyyah say: This hiring is not permissible because of the prohibition against the stud fee of a goat, the earnings of a cupper, and the measure of a miller. It is narrated from Rafiʿ ibn Khadij that the Messenger of Allah said: 'The earnings of the cupper are evil, the price of a dog is evil, and the dowry of a prostitute is evil.' The answer: The hadith of prohibition is abrogated by what is narrated that a man said to him: 'I have dependents and a slave who is a cupper; shall I feed my family from his earnings?' He said: 'Yes.' az-Zaylaʿi mentioned this hadith in Sharh al-Kanz.
Source pages p. 552

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof and an inter-madhhab dispute concerning the permissibility of hiring a cupper (hajjam). The author first presents the Hanafi evidence: the hadith from Ibn Abbas (ra) that the Prophet (saw) himself was cupped and paid the cupper, indicating the permissibility. If cupping earnings were forbidden, the Prophet would not have paid him. The Zahiri school (dhahiriyyah) objects, citing the hadith that prohibits the earnings of a cupper, along with other prohibited earnings like stud fees and miller's measures. They consider this hiring invalid. The Hanafi response is that the prohibition hadith is abrogated (mansukh) by a later hadith where the Prophet (saw) permitted feeding one's family from a cupper's earnings. This ruling is supported by az-Zaylaʿi in his commentary on al-Kanz. Thus, the Hanafi position is that hiring a cupper is permissible, and the contract is valid.

Key Terms
الحجام (al-hajjam): A person who performs cupping (hijamah), a therapeutic bloodletting procedure.
كسب خبيث (kash khabith): Evil or impure earnings; specifically used in hadith to describe income from cupping, dog sale, and prostitution.
منسوخ (mansukh): Abrogated; a ruling that is superseded by a later revelation or hadith.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the Hanafi response to the hadith that says 'Kash al-hajjam khabith'?
A) They accept it and prohibit hiring a cupper
B) They consider it a weak hadith
C) They argue it is abrogated by a later permission
D) They say it only applies to non-Muslim cuppers

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school permits hiring a cupper because the prohibitory hadith is abrogated by the Prophet's own action and a later explicit permission.

Hiring a Wet Nurse: Istihsan Over Qiyas
Istihsan for hiring a wet nurse despite qiyas

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on hiring a wet nurse and explain why istihsan overrides the apparent qiyas.

Core Idea
Hiring a wet nurse is valid because the contract is for service, not milk consumption.

This lesson examines a classic Hanafi example of istihsan: the permissibility of hiring a wet nurse despite a strong analogy that would suggest invalidity. The passage from 'Umdat al-Ri'ayah explains why the school adopts istihsan based on Quranic text, consensus, need, and the proper characterization of the contract's object. By the end, you will understand how Hanafi jurists prioritize normative evidence over strict analogy.

Guided Path
1
Identify the apparent qiyas
Read the text's statement of qiyas: hiring a wet nurse involves consuming milk, like hiring a cow for milk or a garden for fruit. Recognize why this analogy would make the contract invalid (consumption of the substance itself).
Qiyas would treat the milk as the primary object of the contract.
2
Recognize the grounds for istihsan
The text lists four grounds: (1) Quranic command in Surah al-Talaq 65:6 to pay wages to wet nurses, (2) practice of earlier communities confirmed by the Prophet, (3) ijma' (consensus), and (4) necessity because mothers may be unable to nurse.
Istihsan is not arbitrary; it is based on stronger evidence or need.
3
Understand the recharacterization of the contract object
The text states that the contracted object (al-ma'qud 'alayhi) is the benefit (manfa'ah) of service—caring for the child. The milk is subsidiary (taba'), like dye in cloth-dyeing. This resolves the qiyas objection.
This is a key Hanafi legal technique: identifying the primary subject matter.
4
Note the authoritative basis
The passage ends by noting that this is the choice of the author of al-Dhakhirah, a major Hanafi reference. Understand that the ruling is mufta bihi in the school.
Authority weight: Zahir al-Riwayah.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : والظئر...الخ ; - بهمزة ساكنة - ، ويجوز تخفيفها : ناقة تعطف على ولد غيرها، ومنه قيل للمرأة الأجنبية تحضنُ ولد غيرها ظئر، وللرجل الحاضن : ظئر أيضاً، والجمع أظار، مثل حمل وأحمال ، وربّما جمعت المرأة على ظئار بكسر الظاء وضمها. كذا في «المصباح المنير»). وقال في منتهى الأرب» : ظئر بالكسر : شیرده بجيه اغير. انتهى. أي وصح إجارة الظئر بأجر معيّن، والقياس أن لا تصح ؛ لأنـهـا تـرد علـى استهلاك العين، وهو اللبن، فصار كاستئجار البقرة أو الشاه ليشرب لبنهما ، أو البستان ليأكل ثمره. ووجه الاستحسان قوله : فإن أَرْضَعْنَ لَكُمْ فَاتُوهُنَّ أُجُورَهُنَّ ) (٢) ، والمراد الإرضاع بعد الطلاق، فمعناه إن أرضعن أولادكم لأجلكم فأعطوهن أجورهن، أمر بإتيان أجورهنّ، فيكون دليلاً على جواز إجارة الظئر. وإن ذلك كان قبل النبي فأقرهم عليه ، وإجماع الأمة وإنَّ الحاجة ماسة إليه ؛ إذ الأم قد تعجز عن الإرضاع لمرض أو موت أو حبل، ولا يحصل الإرضاع لولدها إلا بالاستئجار. ثم قيل : المعقود عليه المنفعة، وهو القيام بخدمة الولد، وما يحتاج إليه، واللبنُ مستحق بطريق التبع، كالصبغ في صبغ الثوب ، وهو اختيار صاحب «الذخيرة»
His saying: And the wet nurse with a specified wage... with a hamza and a sukun, and it is permissible to pronounce it lightly: a she-camel that shows affection to the offspring of another. Hence an unrelated woman who suckles another's child is called a zi'r, and the man who does the same is also called a zi'r. The plural is aẓār like ḥaml and aḥmāl, and sometimes the female plural is ẓiār with kasr or ḍamm of the ẓā'. So in al-Miṣbāḥ al-Munīr. And in Muntahā al-Arab: zi'r with kasr: a child's nurse. End quote. Meaning: The hiring of a wet nurse with a specified wage is valid. By analogy (qiyas) it would not be valid because it involves consumption of the substance (the milk), so it is like hiring a cow or sheep to drink their milk, or a garden to eat its fruit. The ground for istiḥsān is His statement: 'If they suckle for you, then give them their wages' (Quran 65:6). The reference is to suckling after divorce, so the meaning is: if they suckle your children for your sake, then give them their wages. The command to give them their wages indicates the permissibility of hiring a wet nurse. And that practice existed before the Prophet and he confirmed it, and there is consensus of the ummah, and there is a pressing need for it, since the mother may be unable to suckle due to illness, death, or pregnancy, and the child's suckling cannot be obtained except by hiring. Then it is said: The object of the contract is the benefit (manfa'ah), i.e., the service of caring for the child and what is needed, and the milk is due as a subsidiary, like dye in dyeing cloth. This is the choice of the author of al-Dhakhīrah.
Source pages p. 553

Commentary
This passage establishes the Hanafi ruling that hiring a wet nurse (zi'r) with a specified wage is valid. The qiyas (analogy) to hiring an animal for its milk would suggest invalidity because the contract involves consuming the substance (milk). However, istihsan (juristic preference) overrides the qiyas based on: (1) the Quranic command in Surah al-Talaq (65:6) to pay wages to wet nurses; (2) the practice of earlier communities confirmed by the Prophet; (3) ijma' (consensus); and (4) dire need since mothers may be unable to nurse. The contract is structured as a hire of service (manfa'ah) for child care, with the milk being a subsidiary right, like dye in cloth-dyeing. This is the chosen view according to the author of al-Dhakhirah. The mufta bihi in the Hanafi school is thus the permissibility of such a contract.

Key Terms
ظئر (ẓi'r): A wet nurse; originally a she-camel that suckles another's calf, then applied to a woman who suckles another's child.
استحسان (istiḥsān): Juristic preference that sets aside a strict analogy (qiyas) in favor of a more suitable ruling based on stronger evidence or need.
منفعة (manfa'ah): Benefit or service; the lawful subject matter of a hire contract.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the primary object of the contract (al-ma'qud 'alayhi) when hiring a wet nurse according to the Hanafi school?
A) The milk itself (al-laban)
B) The benefit of service (al-manfa'ah), i.e., nursing and care
C) The child's ownership
D) The duration of the contract

Key Takeaway
Hiring a wet nurse is valid in the Hanafi school because the contract is for service, not milk, and istihsan overrides the contrary qiyas.

Husband's Rights Over Hired Wet Nurse: Intercourse and Contract Cancellation
Rulings on husband's right to intercourse and cancellation of wet nurse contract

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the husband's right to intercourse with a hired wet nurse and explain the Hanafi position on contract cancellation.

Core Idea
A husband's prior marital right overrides a subsequent hire contract.

When a woman is hired as a wet nurse, her husband retains his marital rights, including the right to intercourse and the ability to cancel the hire contract under certain conditions. This lesson examines the Hanafi position on these rights, contrasting it with the Maliki view, and explores the reasoning behind the Hanafi ruling.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Three Rulings
The passage addresses three distinct rulings: (1) husband's right to intercourse, (2) restriction on where intercourse can occur, (3) husband's right to cancel the hire contract. State each clearly.
These rulings are interconnected through the principle of preserving the husband's prior rights.
2
State the Hanafi Position on Intercourse
The Hanafi school holds that the husband may have intercourse with the wet nurse without the employer's consent. Explain the basis: the right predates the contract and cannot be nullified by a doubtful harm.
This is supported by al-Shafi'i and Ahmad; Malik disagrees.
3
Analyze the Maliki Objection
Malik argues that intercourse may reduce or cut off milk, harming the employer. Identify the weak point in this argument from the Hanafi perspective.
The harm is speculative, and a prior right is not lost on mere speculation.
4
Understand the Location Restriction
The husband may not have intercourse in the employer's house without permission because the house is the employer's property. This shows respect for the employer's rights.
The restriction is a compromise between conflicting rights.
5
Apply the Ruling on Contract Cancellation
If the marriage is publicly known (nikah zahir) and the husband did not permit the hire, he may cancel the contract. The reason: breastfeeding and night duties weaken the wife and impair her beauty, analogous to voluntary fasting.
The marriage must be proven by witnesses or notoriety, not just confession.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وللزوج وطؤها إلا في بيت المستأجر ، وله في نكاح ظاهر فسخها إن لم يأذن لها فإن أقرت بنكاحه لا
[١] قوله : وللزوج ... الخ ؛ أي لزوج الظئر وطؤها إذا أراد، وهو قول الشافعي له وأحمد ه ، وقال مالك : ليس له ذلك إلا برضاء المستأجر ؛ لأنه قد ينقص اللبن ، وقد يقطعه بالحبل.
ولنا : إنّ الوطء حق للزوج قبل عقد الإجارة ، فلا يتمكن المستأجر من إسقاطه ، ولا يسقط لأمر مشكوك فيه، ألا ترى أن للزوج أن يفسخ عقد الإجارة إذا لم يعلم به صيانة لحقه
[٢] قوله : لا في بيت المستأجر ؛ يعني ليس لزوج الظئر وطؤها في بيت المستأجر، إذا لم يرض به ؛ لأنَّ بيته حقه فليس للزوج فعل ذلك إلا بإذنه.
[٣] قوله : وله...الخ ؛ ولزوج الظئر سواء كان ممن يشينه أن يكون امرأته ظئراً أو لا. في نكاح ظاهر ؛ أي معلوم من غير الإقرار فسخها : أي فسخ الإجارة. إن لم يأذن الزوج لها ؛ أي للظئر في الإجار؛ لما أنَّ له أن يمنعها من الخروج ؛ ولأنَّ الإرضاع والسهر بالليل يضعفها ويذهب جمالها، فكان له المنع منه، كما يمنعها من الصيام تطوعاً.
And the husband has the right to intercourse with her except in the employer's house, and he has in a known marriage the right to annul the contract if he did not permit her, but if she acknowledges his marriage then no. [1] His saying: 'And the husband...' meaning the husband of the wet nurse may have intercourse with her if he wishes, and this is the saying of al-Shafi'i and Ahmad, and Malik said he does not have that except with the consent of the employer because it may reduce the milk or cut it off by pregnancy. And our proof: intercourse is the husband's right before the hire contract, so the employer cannot nullify it, and it is not lost due to a doubtful matter; do you not see that the husband may annul the hire contract if he was not aware of it to protect his right? [2] His saying: 'Except in the employer's house' means the husband of the wet nurse may not have intercourse with her in the employer's house without his consent because the house is the employer's right, so the husband may only do so with permission. [3] His saying: 'and he has...' and for the husband of the wet nurse, whether or not he is among those who would be dishonored by his wife being a wet nurse, in a known marriage, i.e., known without confession, he may annul it, i.e., annul the hire contract, if the husband did not permit her, i.e., the wet nurse, in the hire; because he has the right to prevent her from going out, and because breastfeeding and staying up at night weaken her and remove her beauty, so he may prevent it, just as he prevents her from voluntary fasting.
Source pages p. 555

Commentary
This passage addresses the husband's rights over the hired wet nurse. First, the husband retains the right to intercourse, as this right predates the contract and cannot be nullified by the employer. This is the Hanafi view, supported by al-Shafi'i and Ahmad, while Malik requires the employer's consent due to potential harm to the milk. The Hanafi argument is that the husband's right is established and cannot be lost on a mere speculation; indeed, the husband may cancel the contract if he was unaware of it to protect his right. Second, the husband may not exercise this right in the employer's house without permission, as the house is the employer's property. Third, if the marriage is publicly known (ظاهر), the husband may cancel the hire contract to protect his rights, especially if he did not permit his wife to be hired, as breastfeeding and night duty weaken her and impair her beauty. This is analogized to preventing voluntary fasting. The cancellation is not allowed if she merely confesses the marriage without evidence.

Key Terms
ظئر (dha'ir): A wet nurse hired to breastfeed and care for a child.
نكاح ظاهر (nikah zahir): A marriage that is publicly known, proven by witnesses or notoriety, not just confession.
فسخ (faskh): Rescission or annulment of a contract by one party due to a valid reason.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Under Hanafi law, when can the husband of a hired wet nurse cancel the hire contract?
A) Only if the employer agrees.
B) Only if the marriage is publicly known and he did not permit her hire.
C) At any time without reason.
D) Only if the wet nurse confesses the marriage.

Key Takeaway
The husband's prior marital right is not overridden by a subsequent hire contract; he may have intercourse and cancel the contract if necessary to protect his rights.

Husband's Right to Intercourse with Wet Nurse
Dispute with Maliki school over husband's right to intercourse

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on the husband's right to intercourse with his wet nurse wife and evaluate the Maliki counter-argument.

Core Idea
A husband's prior conjugal right cannot be voided by a lessee's uncertain fear of harm.

When a married woman is hired as a wet nurse, a conflict may arise between the husband's right to marital intimacy and the lessee's interest in uninterrupted breastfeeding. The Hanafi school rules that the husband may have intercourse except in the lessee's house, while Imam Malik requires the lessee's consent. This lesson unpacks the legal reasoning behind each position and the practical consequences.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify the exact ruling from the passage: the husband may have intercourse except in the lessee's house. Note the exception is based on property rights, not on the breastfeeding contract.
2
Identify the opposing school and its dalil
Imam Malik argues that intercourse may reduce milk or cut it off due to pregnancy, harming the lessee's benefit.
3
Analyze the Hanafi response
The Hanafi response has two prongs: (1) the husband's right predates the lease and cannot be voided by uncertain harm; (2) the husband may annul the lease if unaware, showing the strength of his right.
Note the use of 'mashkuk fih' (doubtful matter) as a key concept.
4
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical difference: under Hanafi, the lessee cannot prevent intercourse (except in his own house); under Maliki, the lessee's consent is required, giving them leverage.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وللزوج وطؤها إلا في بيت المستأجر. [١]قوله : وللزوج ... الخ ؛ أي لزوج الظئر وطؤها إذا أراد، وهو قول الشافعي له وأحمد ه ، وقال مالك : ليس له ذلك إلا برضاء المستأجر ؛ لأنه قد ينقص اللبن ، وقد يقطعه بالحبل. ولنا : إنّ الوطء حق للزوج قبل عقد الإجارة ، فلا يتمكن المستأجر من إسقاطه ، ولا يسقط لأمر مشكوك فيه، ألا ترى أن للزوج أن يفسخ عقد الإجارة إذا لم يعلم به صيانة لحقه. [٢] قوله : لا في بيت المستأجر ؛ يعني ليس لزوج الظئر وطؤها في بيت المستأجر، إذا لم يرض به ؛ لأنَّ بيته حقه فليس للزوج فعل ذلك إلا بإذنه.
And for the husband is intercourse with her except in the lessee's house. [1] His statement: 'And for the husband... etc.' meaning: for the husband of the wet nurse [it is permissible] to have intercourse with her if he wishes, and this is the statement of al-Shafi'i and Ahmad. Malik said: He does not have that except with the lessee's consent, because it may reduce the milk and may cut it off by pregnancy. And our proof: Intercourse is a right of the husband before the contract of lease, so the lessee cannot nullify it, and it is not voided due to a doubtful matter. Do you not see that the husband may annul the contract of lease if he was not aware of it? To protect his right. [2] His statement: 'not in the lessee's house' means: it is not for the husband of the wet nurse to have intercourse with her in the lessee's house if he does not consent, because his house is his right, so the husband may not do that except with his permission.
Source pages p. 555

Commentary
This passage addresses the husband's right to have marital relations with his wife who is serving as a wet nurse (ظئر) under a lease contract (إجارة). The primary ruling states that the husband may have intercourse with her, but not in the lessee's house. The commentator explains that this right is established before the lease contract, so the lessee cannot deny it. The dispute is with Imam Malik, who requires the lessee's consent due to potential harm to the milk. The Hanafi response argues that the harm is uncertain and established rights are not voided by uncertainty. The exception (not in the lessee's house) is because the lessee's house is his private property; the husband may not enter without permission.

Key Terms
ظئر (ẓaʼ): Wet nurse; a woman hired to breastfeed an infant.
إجارة (ijārah): Lease contract; in this context, hiring a wet nurse.
وطء (waṭʼ): Sexual intercourse.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school upholds the husband's prior right to intercourse, limiting it only by the lessee's property rights in his own house.

Conditions for Payment in Fungible Commodities in Ijara
Ruling on validity of hiring wet nurse with mithli payment

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the conditions for valid payment with fungible commodities in a lease contract and explain Abu Hanifa's additional requirement for specifying the place of delivery.

Core Idea
A lease with payment in fungible goods is valid if the goods are specified like a salam contract, but payment need not be deferred; place of delivery must be specified if transport costs apply.

When hiring a wet nurse (or any worker) with payment in clothes or other fungible goods, the contract resembles a salam sale in certain respects. This passage from Al-Shumnunī clarifies which conditions of salam apply and which do not, and highlights Abu Hanifa's concern for specifying the place of delivery when transport is involved.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is hiring a wet nurse with payment in clothes (or other mithli commodities). The ruling is that the contract is valid (sahih) provided certain conditions are met.
2
Locate the conditions from salam
All conditions of a salam contract are required: specification of term (ajal), quantity (qadr), and type (jins). This ensures the commodity is precisely defined.
The classic salam conditions are: full specification of the subject matter (quantity, quality, delivery date).
3
Understand why deferment is not required
The payment (thaman) is a fungible commodity that is described and not individually identified. It is established as a debt in the liability (dhimma). Therefore, it acts as a price, and deferring payment beyond the contract is not necessary.
In salam, the price is paid at the session. Here, since the commodity itself is the price, the same logic applies to the payment being immediate.
4
Note Abu Hanifa's additional condition on place
Abu Hanifa requires specification of the place of delivery if the commodity involves transport and expense. This prevents future dispute over where delivery must occur.
The text says 'if it has load and expense', meaning if moving the goods is burdensome.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال الشمني في «كمال الدراية» (۱) : لو استأجرها بثياب يشترط جميع شرائط السلم من الأجل وبيان القدر والجنس ولو سمّى مكيلاً أو موزوناً وبين قدره وصفته لا يشترط تأجيله؛ لأنَّ المكيل والموزون إذا كان موصوفاً غير مشار إليه ثمن، بدليل ثبوته في الذمة، لكن يشترط بيان مكان الإيفاء عند أبي حنيفة له إذا كان له حمل ومؤنة. انتهى.
Al-Shumnunī said in 'Kamal al-Diraya': If he hires her with clothes, all the conditions of salam (advance sale) are required, such as the term and specification of quantity and type. Even if he specifies a measurable or weighable commodity and specifies its quantity and description, deferment of the term is not required, because a measurable or weighable commodity, when described and not specifically identified, is a price, as evidenced by its being established in the liability. However, specification of the place of delivery is required according to Abu Hanifa if it has transport and expense. End quote.
Source pages p. 555

Commentary
This passage from Al-Shumnunī discusses the payment terms when hiring a wet nurse with clothes (or similar items). The key point is that if the payment is a mithli (fungible) commodity like food grains, it must meet the conditions of a salam contract (an advance sale with deferred delivery) regarding the specification of quantity, quality, and term. However, deferment of the payment itself is not required because the mithli commodity acts as a price (thaman) that is established in the liability. As per Abu Hanifa, the place of delivery must be specified if the commodity requires transportation and expense.

Key Terms
مكيل (makīl): A commodity measured by volume (e.g., grain).
موزون (mawzūn): A commodity weighed (e.g., gold, silver).
سلم (salam): An advance sale where price is paid upfront for deferred delivery of a specified commodity.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, if a wet nurse is hired with payment in wheat (a measurable commodity), what additional condition does Abu Hanifa require beyond the standard salam conditions?
A) Deferment of the payment
B) Specification of the place of delivery
C) Both deferment and place
D) Nothing extra

Key Takeaway
A lease with payment in fungible commodities is valid if the commodity is specified as in a salam contract, but payment deferment is not required; Abu Hanifa adds place specification when transport costs apply.

Husband's Right to Annul the Lease of a Wet Nurse: The Apparent Marriage Condition
Intra-Hanafi dispute over husband's annulment right

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the conditions under which a husband can annul his wife's lease as a wet nurse and distinguish between marriage established by appearance vs. acknowledgment.

Core Idea
A husband can annul a wet nurse's lease only if the marriage is 'apparent' and he did not permit her; her mere acknowledgment does not bind the lessee.

The passage from 'Umdat al-Ri'aya discusses a nuanced ruling: when a married woman is hired as a wet nurse, her husband may annul the lease if the marriage is publicly known. But if the marriage is only known through her own admission, the husband cannot annul because acknowledgment (iqrar) is a limited proof. An intra-Hanafi difference exists about whether the husband can annul if the marriage occurred after the lease or without his permission.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and ruling
The act is the husband's annulment of the wet nurse's lease. The ruling: he may annul if the marriage is 'apparent' and he did not permit her.
2
Distinguish 'apparent' vs. acknowledged marriage
'Apparent' (nikah zahir) means publicly witnessed or widely known, not established by the wife's own acknowledgment or that of her husband.
3
Analyze the intra-Hanafi dispute
The dominant view (الأصح) allows annulment even if the marriage occurred after the lease or without the husband's permission. Al-Maqdisi argues that if he permitted her, he cannot annul; so if he married after the contract, he a fortiori should not be able to annul.
The text does not give a direct response to al-Maqdisi but declares the first view as الأصح.
4
Apply the principle of iqrar
Acknowledgment (iqrar) is a limited proof (hujja qasira) that only binds the declarant, not third parties. Thus, if the marriage is known only through the wet nurse's acknowledgment, the husband cannot annul the lease against the lessee.
This protects the lessee's rights.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وله في نكاح ظاهر فسخها إن لم يأذن لها فإن أقرت بنكاحه لا. [٣]قوله : وله...الخ ؛ ولزوج الظئر سواء كان ممن يشينه أن يكون امرأته ظئراً أو لا. في نكاح ظاهر ؛ أي معلوم من غير الإقرار فسخها : أي فسخ الإجارة. إن لم يأذن الزوج لها ؛ أي للظئر في الإجار؛ لما أنَّ له أن يمنعها من الخروج ؛ ولأنَّ الإرضاع والسهر بالليل يضعفها ويذهب جمالها، فكان له المنع منه، كما يمنعها من الصيام تطوعاً. وقيل : له فسخها سواءً كان التزوج بعد الإجارة أو حدثت بعده بغير إذنه في الأصح ، قال المقدسي : فيه تأمل ؛ لأنه إذا كان أذن لها ليس له الفسخ ، فإذا تزوج بعد العقدِ ينبغي أن لا يكون له ذلك بالطريق الأولى. أمَّا إِن عَلِمَ النِّكَاحَ بإقرارها لا. [١] قوله : أما إن علم ... الخ ؛ يعني أمّا إن علم النكاح بإقرار الظئر أو بإقرار زوجها فليس له أن يفسخها ؛ لأنَّ الإقرار حجّةٌ قاصرة غير مقبولة في حق الغير، وهـو المستأجر، كما إذا أقرت المنكوحة المجهولة بالرق لإنسان تصير رقيقاً ولا تصدق في حق بطلان النكاح كما صرحوا به.
And for him, in an apparent marriage, to annul it if he did not permit her, and if she acknowledges her marriage, he cannot. [3] His statement: 'And for him... etc.': meaning for the husband of the wet nurse, whether he is one whom it shames that his wife is a wet nurse or not. 'In an apparent marriage' i.e., known without acknowledgment. 'Annul it' i.e., annul the lease. 'If the husband did not permit her' i.e., did not permit the wet nurse to enter the lease, because he has the right to prevent her from going out, and because breastfeeding and night waking weaken her and remove her beauty, so he may prevent her, just as he prevents her from voluntary fasting. And it was said: He may annul it whether the marriage occurred after the lease or after it without his permission, according to the more correct view. Al-Maqdisi said: There is consideration in this, because if he permitted her, he cannot annul, so if he married after the contract, it should be that he does not have that right as a primary course. Further: 'If he knows of the marriage by her acknowledgment, he cannot annul'. [1] His statement: 'As for if he knows... etc.': meaning if he knows of the marriage by the acknowledgment of the wet nurse or her husband, then he may not annul it, because acknowledgment is a limited proof not accepted against a third party, i.e., the lessee, just as when an unknown married woman acknowledges slavery to someone, she becomes a slave but her acknowledgment is not believed to invalidate the marriage, as they have explained.
Source pages p. 555

Commentary
This passage discusses the husband's right to annul the lease of his wife as a wet nurse. The key condition is that the marriage must be 'apparent' (visible to people or witnessed), not merely known through her own acknowledgment. If the husband did not permit her to enter the lease, he has the right to annul it to protect his marital interests (weakening, loss of beauty). There is an intra-Hanafi difference: some say he may annul even if the marriage occurred after the lease or without his permission (the more correct view), but al-Maqdisi finds this problematic. If the marriage is established only by the wife's or her husband's acknowledgment, the husband cannot annul the lease because acknowledgment (iqrar) is a limited proof that does not bind third parties (the lessee). Thus, the lessee can insist on the lease.

Key Terms
نكاح ظاهر (nikāḥ ẓāhir): A marriage that is publicly known, either by witnesses or widespread knowledge, as opposed to being established only by the parties' acknowledgment.
إقرار (iqrār): Acknowledgment or confession; a limited proof that only binds the declarant, not binding on others.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a wet nurse's marriage is only known through her own acknowledgment, can her husband annul the lease?
A) Yes, because the marriage is proven
B) No, because acknowledgment does not bind the lessee
C) Yes, if he did not permit her
D) No, unless the lessee agrees

Key Takeaway
A husband can only annul his wife's wet-nurse lease if the marriage is apparent (not merely acknowledged) and he did not permit her.

Grounds for Annulling Wet Nurse's Lease by Infant's Family
Ruling on family's right to annul lease due to wet nurse's defects

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to list the valid grounds for the infant's family to annul a wet nurse's lease and distinguish between actual harm and suspected harm according to the Hanafi school.

Core Idea
The infant's family may annul only for actual harm, not mere suspicion or harm to character alone.

This passage from 'Umdat al-Ri'aya discusses the rights of the infant's guardians to annul the lease of a wet nurse when certain defects arise. The key principle is that the lease can be annulled due to excuses (al-ijarah tufsakh bi al-a'dhar). The text enumerates specific grounds and clarifies that only actual harm, not mere worry, justifies annulment. A later view from al-Khaniyya and al-Nihaya expands the grounds to include disbelief and insanity.

Guided Path
1
Identify the primary grounds
The passage begins with illness and pregnancy as clear grounds. Understand why: the milk becomes harmful, and nursing harms the ill/pregnant woman herself.
2
Identify additional grounds
Curdled milk, theft, open promiscuity, and prolonged absence are listed. The common thread is actual harm (darar) to the infant or family.
3
Distinguish suspicion from certainty
The text explicitly states that mere suspicion (what only suggests harm) is not enough. Only definite harm qualifies.
This is a key fiqh principle: harm must be certain, not conjectural.
4
Note the intra-school difference
Disbelief alone is not considered harmful in the main view, but al-Khaniyya and al-Nihaya allow annulment for disbelief, insanity, foolishness, and promiscuity. Al-Nihaya argues promiscuity is worse than disbelief.
This reflects a later, more cautious trend in the madhhab.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولأهل الصبي فسخها إن مرضت أو حبلت. [٢] قوله : ولأهل الصبي.. الخ ; أي ولأهل الصبي الرضيع فسخ الإجارة إن مرضت المرضعة أو حبلت ; لأنَّ لبن الحبلى والمريضة يضرّ بالولد، وهي أيضا يضرها الرضاع، فكان لها ولهم الخيار دفعاً للضرر عنها وعن الصبي؛ وهذا لأنَّ الإجارة تفسخ بالأعذار. وكذا لو تقيأ لبنها لأهله الفسخ ; لأنَّ ذلك يضر بالصبي ، وكذا إذا كانت سارقة ; لأنهم يخافون على متاعهم وعلى حلي الصبي، وكذا إذا كانت فاجرة بائناً فجورها ; لأنها تشتغل عنه بالفجور، وكذا كل ما يضرُّ بالصبي نحو الخروج من منزلِ الصبي زماناً كثيراً أو ما أشبه ذلك ، فلهم أن يمنعوها عنه. وأما ما كان يوهم الضرر فليس لهم أن يمنعوها عنه، وكذا فيما إذا لا يضر بالصبي مثل كفرها فإنّه لا يضر بالصبى، لكن قال في «الخانية» : إذا ظهر الظئر كافرة أو مجنونة أو زانية أو حمقاء فلهم فسخ الإجارة. انتهى. وقال في «النهاية»: ولا يبعد أن يقال : عيب الفجور في هذا فوق عيب الكفر، ألا ترى أنه كان في نساء بعض الرسل كامرأتي نوح ا ولوط ال وما بغت امرأة نبي قط، هكذا قال رسول الله له ، وكذا إذا كان الصبي لا يأخذ ثديها كان لهم أن يفسخوا الإجارة، وللظئر أيضاً أن تفسخ الإجارة إذا كان يحصل لها الإذاء منهم
And for the family of the infant to annul it if she becomes ill or becomes pregnant. [2] His statement: 'And for the family of the infant... etc.': meaning for the family of the nursing infant to annul the lease if the wet nurse becomes ill or pregnant, because the milk of the pregnant and the ill harms the child, and breastfeeding also harms her, so she and they have the option to avoid harm to her and the child. This is because the lease is annulled due to excuses. Similarly, if her milk curdles, her family may annul because that harms the child. Similarly, if she is a thief, because they fear for their belongings and the infant's jewelry. Similarly, if she is openly promiscuous, because she will be occupied with fornication. Similarly, anything that harms the child, such as leaving the child's home for a long time or the like, they may prevent her from it. As for what only suggests harm, they may not prevent her from it. Similarly, if it does not harm the child, like her disbelief, it does not harm the child. However, it says in al-Khaniyya: If the wet nurse appears to be a disbeliever, insane, adulteress, or foolish, they may annul the lease. End quote. And it says in al-Nihaya: It is not far to say that the defect of promiscuity is above the defect of disbelief. Do you not see that among the wives of some messengers, like the two wives of Nuh and Lut, and no wife of a prophet ever committed adultery? Thus said the Messenger of Allah peace be upon him. Similarly, if the infant does not take her breast, they may annul the lease, and the wet nurse may also annul the lease if she is harmed by them.
Source pages p. 556

Commentary
This passage lists the valid reasons for the infant's family (أهل الصبي) to annul the lease of a wet nurse. The primary two reasons are illness and pregnancy because the milk becomes harmful. Other defects include: curdling of milk, theft (fear for belongings), open promiscuity (she will be distracted), any harm like prolonged absence. Mere suspicion of harm is not enough. Disbelief alone is not considered harmful according to the main view, but al-Khaniyya allows annulment for disbelief, insanity, adultery, or foolishness. Al-Nihaya argues that promiscuity is a worse defect than disbelief, citing the example of the wives of prophets. Also if the infant refuses the breast, the family may annul, and the wet nurse may also annul if she is harmed.

Key Terms
فسخ الإجارة (faskh al-ijārah): Annulment of the lease contract due to an excuse or defect.
أهل الصبي (ahl al-ṣabī): The guardians or family of the infant who arranged the lease.
ضرر (ḍarar): Actual harm that justifies annulment; contrasted with mere suspicion (توهم الضرر).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Illness of the wet nurse
B) Pregnancy of the wet nurse
C) Disbelief of the wet nurse
D) Theft by the wet nurse

Key Takeaway
Annulment of a wet nurse's lease is allowed only for actual harm to the infant or family; character defects alone are insufficient in the main view, but later scholarship expands the grounds.
