Rescinding the Wet Nurse's Ijarah: Grounds and Intra-Hanafi Dispute
Explaining grounds and intra-Hanafi dispute on faskh of ijarah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the valid grounds for rescinding a wet nurse's ijarah contract in Hanafi law and evaluate the intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the effect of marriage.

Core Idea
Harm to the child or wet nurse justifies rescinding; mere suspicion or non-harmful characteristics do not.

The hiring of a wet nurse (ijarah al-dha'r) is a contract with specific rules. This passage explains when the guardians of the infant can terminate the contract. While sickness and pregnancy are clearly harmful, the text also explores other defects like theft, immorality, and even disbelief. An intra-Hanafi dispute arises regarding the effect of the wet nurse's marriage after the contract: does it give the guardian an automatic right to rescind?

Guided Path
1
State the basic Hanafi position
Identify the clear grounds for faskh given in the matn: sickness, pregnancy, and the rationale of harm (ضرر).
The commentary expands this to include theft, open immorality, leaving the child, etc.
2
Identify the intra-Hanafi dispute
The dispute concerns whether marriage after the contract (with or without the guardian's permission) allows faskh. Contrast the 'asahh' view with al-Maqdisi's critique.
3
Follow the opposing proof
Al-Maqdisi argues that if the guardian permits the marriage, he waives his right to rescind; marriage without permission would then be even clearer grounds, but he questions the logic.
4
Analyse the Hanafi response
The majority view assesses harm objectively: marriage without permission is likely harmful and allows rescission; with permission, the guardian accepts the risk.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical difference: if the wet nurse marries with permission, the guardian cannot rescind; if without permission, some allow rescission, others do not.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولأهل الصبي فسخها إن مرضت أو حبلت
أما إن علم النكاح بإقرارها لا، (ولأهل الصبي فسخها إن مرضت أو حبلت)؛ لأن لبنها يضر بالولد.
وقيل: له فسخها سواء كان التزوج بعد الإجارة أو حدثت بعده بغير إذنه في الأصح، قال المقدسي: فيه تأمل؛ لأنه إذا كان أذن لها ليس له الفسخ، فإذا تزوج بعد العقد ينبغي أن لا يكون له ذلك بالطريق الأولى.
(١) قوله: أما إن علم ... الخ؛ يعني أما إن علم النكاح بإقرار الظئر أو بإقرار زوجها فليس له أن يفسخها؛ لأن الإقرار حجة قاصرة غير مقبولة في حق الغير، وهو المستأجر، كما إذا أقرت المنكوحة المجهولة بالرق لإنسان تصير رقيقاً ولا تصدق في حق بطلان النكاح كما صرحوا به.
(٢) قوله: ولأهل الصبي.. الخ؛ أي ولأهل الصبي الرضيع فسخ الإجارة إن مرضت المرضعة أو حبلت؛ لأن لبن الحبلى والمريضة يضر بالولد، وهي أيضا يضرها الرضاع، فكان لها ولهم الخيار دفعاً للضرر عنها وعن الصبي؛ وهذا لأن الإجارة تفسخ بالأعذار. وكذا لو تقيأ لبنها لأهله الفسخ؛ لأن ذلك يضر بالصبي، وكذا إذا كانت سارقة؛ لأنهم يخافون على متاعهم وعلى حلي الصبي، وكذا إذا كانت فاجرة بائناً فجورها؛ لأنها تشتغل عنه بالفجور، وكذا كل ما يضر بالصبي نحو الخروج من منزل الصبي زماناً كثيراً أو ما أشبه ذلك، فلهم أن يمنعوها عنه. وأما ما كان يوهم الضرر فليس لهم أن يمنعوها عنه، وكذا فيما إذا لا يضر بالصبي مثل كفرها فإنه لا يضر بالصبي، لكن قال في «الخانية»: إذا ظهر الظئر كافرة أو مجنونة أو زانية أو حمقاء فلهم فسخ الإجارة. انتهى. وقال في «النهاية»: ولا يبعد أن يقال: عيب الفجور في هذا فوق عيب الكفر، ألا ترى أنه كان في نساء بعض الرسل كامرأتي نوح ولوط وما بغت امرأة نبي قط، هكذا قال رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم، وكذا إذا كان الصبي لا يأخذ ثديها كان لهم أن يفسخوا الإجارة، وللظئر أيضاً أن تفسخ الإجارة إذا كان يحصل لها الإذاء منهم
And the guardians of the infant have the right to rescind it if she becomes sick or pregnant. As for if he knows of the marriage by her confession, then no. (And the guardians of the infant have the right to rescind it if she becomes sick or pregnant) because her milk harms the child. And it is said: He has the right to rescind it whether the marriage occurred after the ijarah or happened after it without his permission, according to the more correct view. Al-Maqdisi said: There is consideration in this; because if he permitted her, he does not have the right to rescind, so if she married after the contract, it is even more apt that he should not have that right. (1) His saying: As for if he knows... etc.: meaning that if he knows of the marriage by the confession of the wet nurse or by the confession of her husband, he cannot rescind it, because a confession is a limited proof not accepted against a third party, who is the hirer, just as if the unknown married woman confesses to being slave to someone, she becomes a slave but is not believed regarding the invalidity of the marriage, as they have explicitly stated. (2) His saying: And the guardians of the infant... etc.: meaning that the guardians of the nursing infant have the right to rescind the ijarah if the wet nurse becomes sick or pregnant, because the milk of the pregnant and sick woman harms the child, and breastfeeding also harms her, so she and they have the option to prevent harm to her and the child, and this is because the ijarah is rescinded due to excuses. Likewise, if her milk curdles, they have the right to rescind, because that harms the child; likewise if she is a thief, because they fear for their goods and the child's jewelry; likewise if she is an openly immoral woman, because she will be preoccupied with immorality; likewise everything that harms the child, such as leaving the child's home for a long time or similar, they can prevent her from that. As for what suggests harm, they cannot prevent her, and likewise if it does not harm the child, such as her disbelief, for it does not harm the child; but in al-Khaniyya it is stated: If the wet nurse appears to be a disbeliever, or insane, or adulteress, or foolish, they have the right to rescind the ijarah. End quote. And in al-Nihaya: It is not far to say that the defect of immorality in this respect outweighs the defect of disbelief; do you not see that among the wives of some messengers were the wives of Nuh and Lut, and no prophet's wife ever committed adultery, thus said the Messenger of Allah, peace be upon him; likewise if the child does not take her breast, they have the right to rescind the ijarah; and the wet nurse also has the right to rescind the ijarah if she suffers harm from them.
Source pages p. 556

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the grounds for rescinding the ijarah contract with a wet nurse. The matn states that the guardians of the infant can rescind if the wet nurse becomes sick or pregnant, because her milk harms the child. The commentary then addresses a subtle point: if the hirer knows of the wet nurse's marriage through her own confession or her husband's, he cannot use that as grounds to rescind, because a confession is not binding against third parties. Then it introduces a differing opinion (qila): the guardian can rescind regardless of whether the marriage occurred with permission or not, but al-Maqdisi finds this problematic, reasoning that if he permitted her to marry, he waives his right to rescind. The commentary then expands on the ruling, listing other valid grounds for rescission: sour milk, thievery, open immorality, leaving the child for long periods, etc. It also distinguishes between actual harm and hypothetical harm (e.g., disbelief alone is not harmful, but according to al-Khaniyya, if she is a disbeliever, insane, adulteress, or foolish, they can rescind). The passage then quotes al-Nihaya prioritizing immorality over disbelief, and adds that if the child refuses the breast, or if the wet nurse suffers harm from the guardians, she also has the right to rescind.

Key Terms
فسخ (faskh): Rescission or termination of a contract; here, the right to end the ijarah with the wet nurse.
ظئر (dha'r): Wet nurse; the woman hired to breastfeed an infant.
إجارة (ijarah): A contract of hire or lease; here, hiring a wet nurse for breastfeeding.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) The wet nurse becomes pregnant.
B) The wet nurse is a thief.
C) The wet nurse is a disbeliever (according to the primary text).
D) The wet nurse's milk becomes sour.

Key Takeaway
The guardians of the infant can rescind the wet nurse's ijarah when harm to the child is actual and proven; mere suspicion or non-harmful characteristics are insufficient, but the list of harms is broad and includes sickness, pregnancy, theft, and open immorality.

Duties of the Wet Nurse and Effect of Substitute Feeding
Defining the wet nurse's obligations and the consequence of alternative feeding

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the duties of a wet nurse under a Hanafi ijarah contract and determine when she forfeits her wage.

Core Idea
Custom (urf) defines the wet nurse's duties; failure to breastfeed forfeits her wage entirely.

In this lesson, we examine the obligations of a wet nurse hired to breastfeed an infant. The matn and its commentary clarify what services she must provide and what happens if she substitutes breastfeeding with other feeding. Understanding this ruling illustrates how custom (urf) determines the scope of work in ijarah contracts.

Guided Path
1
Identify the wet nurse's duties
From the matn, list the specific services: washing the child, washing his clothes, preparing food and oil. Note that these are derived from custom (urf).
The commentary emphasizes that these are considered tofi' (consequences) of the contracted work.
2
Determine who bears the costs
The father is responsible for the price of food, oil, soap, etc. The wet nurse provides labour only, not materials.
This is consistent with the general ijarah principle that the hirer pays for consumables.
3
Understand the consequence of substitute feeding
If the wet nurse feeds the infant with sheep's milk or solid food instead of breastfeeding, she forfeits her entire wage for the period.
The three imams (Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, Muhammad) agree — she failed to perform the contracted work.
4
Analyze the role of custom (urf)
The commentary explains that when a contract specifies a general work (like 'service of the child'), the specific duties are determined by local custom.
Custom may vary; e.g., whether oiling or perfume is required depends on the custom of the locality.
5
Note the intra-Hanafi agreement
There is no dispute among the three main Hanafi imams on this ruling; it is a unanimous position.
This strengthens the weight of the ruling as mufta bihi.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وعليها غسل الصبي، وغسل ثيابه، وإصلاح طعامه ودهنه، لا ثمن شيء منها، وهو وأجره واجب على أبيه، فإن أرضعته بلبن شاة، أو غذته بطعام، ومضت المدة فلا أجر لها
[1] قوله: وعليها... الخ؛ الأصل أن الإجارة إذا وقعت على عمل فكل ما كان من توابع ذلك العمل، ولم يشترط ذلك على الأجير في الإجارة، فيرجع فيه إلى العرف. ولما كانت خدمة الصبي واجبة عليها، وكل ما ذكر من الغسل وإصلاح الطعام ونحوهما كان منه عرفاً، فيجب عليها قطعاً، فما ذكره محمد رحمه الله من أن الدهن والريحان على الظئر فهو محمول على عادة أهل الكوفة، فاستقم.
[2] قوله: وغسل ثيابه؛ أي من البول ونحوه من النجاسات؛ لتصريحهم أن غسل ثيابه من الوسخ والدرن لا يكون عليها.
[3] قوله: وإصلاح طعامه؛ بأن تمضغه له ولا تأكل شيئاً يفسد لبنها ويضر به، وعليها أيضاً طبخ طعامه. كذا في «الهندية» نقلاً عن «السراج».
[4] قوله: ودهنه؛ أي إصلاح دهنه، فهو مجرور معطوف على طعامه، ويحتمل أن يكون بفتح الدال المهملة، مرفوعاً معطوفاً على قوله: إصلاح طعامه؛ أي لطخه ودلكه، فإنه أيضاً من خدمة الصبي عرفاً.
[5] قوله: ولا ثمن شيء...الخ؛ أي ولا يجب على الظئر ثمن شيء من طعامه ودهنه، وما غسل به ثيابه من الصابون ونحوه، بل ثمن كل من هذه المذكورات واجب على أب الصبي أو على من تجب نفقتُهُ عليه غير الأب إن لم يكن للصبي مال، ولا خفي ماله كالنفقة.
[6] قوله: فلا أجر لها؛ وبه قالت الثلاثة؛ لأنها لم تأتِ بالعمل المستحق عليها
And it is incumbent upon her to wash the child, and wash his clothes, and prepare his food and oil; she is not responsible for the price of any of that; that and its wage are obligatory upon his father. If she breastfeeds him with sheep's milk, or feeds him with food, and the period passes, then she has no wage.
[1] His saying: And it is incumbent upon her... etc.; the principle is that when the ijarah is contracted for a work, everything that is a necessary consequence of that work, even if not stipulated upon the hired worker in the ijarah, is referred to custom. Since the service of the child is obligatory upon her, and everything mentioned like washing and preparing food etc. is customarily part of that, it becomes obligatory upon her absolutely. What Muhammad, may Allah have mercy on him, mentioned that oil and perfume are upon the wet nurse is to be understood according to the custom of the people of Kufa, so be upright.
[2] His saying: And wash his clothes; i.e., from urine and similar impurities; because they explicitly state that washing his clothes from dirt and grime is not upon her.
[3] His saying: And prepare his food; i.e., she should chew it for him and not eat anything that spoils her milk and harms him, and she must also cook his food. Likewise in al-Hindiyya quoting from al-Siraj.
[4] His saying: And his oil; i.e., preparing his oil, it is in the genitive case as a conjunction to 'his food', and it is possible that it is with fatha on the dal, in the nominative as a conjunction to 'prepare his food'; meaning anointing and rubbing him, for that is also customarily part of the service of the child.
[5] His saying: And no price of anything... etc.; i.e., the wet nurse is not obliged to pay the price of anything, of his food and oil, and what is used to wash his clothes like soap etc. Rather, the price of all these mentioned items is obligatory upon the child's father or upon the one who is obliged to provide for him other than the father, if the child has no wealth and his wealth is not hidden, like maintenance.
[6] His saying: Then she has no wage; and the three (imams) said this, because she did not perform the work that was due upon her.
Source pages p. 557

Commentary
This passage is a ruling statement about the duties of a wet nurse under an ijarah contract. The matn specifies that she must wash the child and his clothes, prepare his food and oil, but is not liable for the cost of these items (the father must pay). If she substitutes breastfeeding with sheep's milk or feeding with food, after the contracted period passes, she is not entitled to any wage. The commentary explains that the duties are determined by custom (urf): whatever is customarily part of child service is obligatory on her. It also clarifies that washing from dirt (not just impurities) is not required of her, and that the ruling about oil and perfume depends on local custom (Kufa). The commentary further notes that the three imams (Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, Muhammad) agree that she gets no wage if she provides substitute feeding, because she failed to perform the contracted work (breastfeeding).

Key Terms
غسل (ghusl): Washing the child and his clothes; part of the wet nurse's duties.
إصلاح الطعام (islah al-ta'am): Preparing the child's food by chewing or cooking.
ثمن (thaman): Price or cost; here, the cost of food, oil, soap, etc. is not the wet nurse's responsibility.
أجر (ajr): Wage or fee; the wet nurse forfeits her wage if she does not breastfeed.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What determines the specific duties of a wet nurse in Hanafi law?
A) The contract terms alone
B) Local custom (urf)
C) Analogy to other contracts
D) Explicit stipulation in the Quran

Key Takeaway
A wet nurse's duties are defined by custom; failure to perform the contracted breastfeeding forfeits her wage even if she provides alternative feeding.

Duties of the Wet Nurse: Customary Services in Ijarah
Explains obligations via custom and substitution penalty

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the obligations of a wet nurse under a valid hire contract and apply the Hanafi principle of custom (urf) to determine included duties.

Core Idea
Customary services are included in a hire contract without extra pay; the wet nurse must wash, feed, and oil the child.

This lesson examines the obligations of a wet nurse beyond suckling. The question arises: if a wet nurse is hired to suckle a child, must she also wash, feed, and care for the child without extra compensation? The Hanafi school, relying on custom (urf) as a legal principle, holds that customary services are included. We will analyze the passage from 'Umdat al-Ri'ayah and understand how custom defines the scope of a hire contract.

Guided Path
1
Identify the issue
What are the stated duties of the wet nurse according to the matn? List them: washing the child, washing his clothes, preparing his food and oil.
2
Understand the principle
The commentator explains that when a hire contract does not specify all duties, custom (urf) determines what is included. This is a key Hanafi principle: al-urf muhakkam (custom is authoritative).
3
Apply the principle
Which duties are considered customary for a wet nurse? The text mentions washing from impurities (not dirt), preparing food by chewing, and applying oil (either preparing oil or rubbing the child). These are obligatory without extra pay.
Custom may vary by region; the example of oil and perfume being on the wet nurse in Kufa shows regional variation.
4
Identify exceptions
Not everything is included. For example, washing clothes from dirt and grime is not required. Also, the wet nurse is not liable for the cost of supplies (soap, oil, food); the father must pay.
5
Analyze the consequence
If the wet nurse substitutes suckling with goat's milk or food, she forfeits her wage because she did not perform the agreed service. This is agreed upon by the three imams.
A nuance: if her milk was stipulated and she hires another, there is a difference of opinion on whether she deserves wage.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الإجارة باب الإجارة الفاسدة
وعليها غسل الصبي ، وغسل ثيابه، وإصلاح طعامه ودهنه، لا ثمن شيء منها ، وهو وأجره واجب على أبيه ، فإن أرضعته بلبن شاة، أو غدته بطعام، ومضت المدة فلا أجر لها
قوله : وعليها ... الخ ; الأصلُ أنّ الإجارة إذا وقعت على عمل فكل ما كان من توابع ذلك العمل، ولم يشترط ذلك على الأجير في الإجارة، فيرجع فيه إلى العرف. ولما كانت خدمة الصبي واجبة عليها، وكلُّ ما ذكر من الغسل وإصلاح الطعام ونحوهما كان منه عرفاً، فيجب عليها قطعاً، فما ذكره محمد الله من أنَّ الدهن والريحان على الظئر فهو محمول على عادة أهل الكوفة ، فاستقم). قوله : وغسل ثيابه ؛ أي من البول ونحوه من النجاسات ؛ لتصريحهم أنَّ غسل ثيابه من الوسخ والدرن لا يكون عليها. قوله : وإصلاح طعامه ؛ بأن تمضغه له ولا تأكل شيئاً يفسد لبنها ويضر به، وعليها أيضاً طبخ طعامه. كذا في «الهندية» نقلاً عن «السراج». قوله : ودهنه ؛ أي اصلاح دهنه، فهو مجرور معطوف على طعامه، ويحتمل أن يكون بفتح الدال المهملة، مرفوعاً معطوفاً على قوله : اصلاح طعامه ؛ أي لطخه ودلكه، فإنّه أيضاً من خدمة الصبي عرفاً. قوله : ولا ثمن شيء...الخ ؛ أي ولا يجب على الظئر ثمن شيء من طعامه ودهنه، وما غسل به ثيابه من الصابون ونحوه، بل ثمن كلّ من هذه المذكورات واجب على أب الصبي أو على من تجب نفقتُهُ عليه غير الأب إن لم يكن للصبي مال ، ولا خفي ماله كالنفقة. قوله : فلا أجر لها ؛ وبه قالت الثلاثة ؛ لأنها لم تأتِ بالعمل المستحق عليها وهو الإرضاع ؛ لأن الأوّل إيجار والثاني تغذية، وذكر الشمني نقلاً عن «المحيط» : لو كان إرضاعها مشروطاً فاستأجرت ظئراً فأرضعته لا يستحق الأجر ؛ لأنَّ لبنها ربّما يكون أجود ، وقيل : يستحق لأنَّ التفاوت بين اللبنين يسير. انتهى.
Book of Ijarah, Chapter of Invalid Ijarah. And upon her (the wet nurse) is washing the boy, washing his clothes, preparing his food and oil; she is not liable for the price of any of this, rather it is obligatory upon the father. And if she suckles him with the milk of a goat or feeds him with food and the period passes, she has no wage. His saying: 'And upon her...' etc. The principle is that when a hire contract is made for a certain work, everything that is a consequence of that work and was not stipulated upon the hired worker in the contract, then reference is made to custom. Since the service of the boy is obligatory upon her, and everything mentioned (washing, food preparation, etc.) is customarily part of that, it is definitely obligatory upon her. So what Muhammad said about oil and perfume being upon the wet nurse is based on the custom of the people of Kufa, so be straight. His saying: 'And washing his clothes' i.e. from urine and similar impurities; because they explicitly state that washing his clothes from dirt and grime is not upon her. His saying: 'And preparing his food' i.e. by chewing it for him and not eating anything that spoils her milk and harms him; also cooking his food is upon her. Thus in al-Hindiyya quoting al-Siraj. His saying: 'And his oil' i.e. preparing his oil, so it is genitive connected to 'his food', and it is possible that it is with fatha on the dal, nominative, connected to his saying: 'preparing his food', i.e. smearing and rubbing him, for that is also customarily part of the service of the boy. His saying: 'And not the price of anything...' etc. i.e. the wet nurse is not liable for the price of anything from his food, oil, or soap for washing his clothes; rather the price of all these mentioned things is obligatory upon the boy's father or upon the one whose maintenance is obligatory upon him other than the father if the boy has no wealth, and his wealth is not hidden like maintenance. His saying: 'So she has no wage'; and with it said the three (Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, Muhammad); because she did not perform the work that was due upon her, which is suckling; because the first is suckling and the second is feeding. And al-Shamni narrated from al-Muhit: If her suckling was stipulated and she hired a wet nurse who suckled him, she does not deserve the wage; because her milk might be better, and it is said: she deserves because the difference between the two milks is slight. End.
Source pages p. 557

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof, specifically a commentary (sharh) on the matn of al-Hidayah. The matn states that a wet nurse (ظئر) must wash the child, wash his clothes, prepare his food and oil, and these are not paid separately; the father bears the cost. The commentator explains that the basis is custom (urf): whatever is customarily part of the service is included in the hire without extra payment. Thus washing the child and clothes (from impurities like urine), preparing food by chewing it, and applying oil (either preparing oil or rubbing) are all obligatory on the wet nurse as part of her job. However, washing clothes from dirt is not required. The wet nurse is not required to pay for any supplies; the father must pay. If she substitutes suckling with goat's milk or food, she forfeits her wage because she did not perform the agreed service—suckling. The three imams (Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, Muhammad) agree on this. A nuance: if her milk was stipulated, and she hired another, neither deserves wages due to potential quality difference, though some say she does if difference is slight.

Key Terms
ظئر (ẓi'r): A wet nurse hired to suckle a child.
إجارة فاسدة (ijāra fāsida): A hire contract that is invalid due to a defect, yet may still give rights/obligations if performed.
العرف (al-ʿurf): Customary practice used to determine unstated terms of a contract.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what happens if a wet nurse feeds the child solid food instead of breast milk during the contract period?
A) She is still entitled to her wage because feeding is part of child care.
B) She loses her wage because she did not perform the agreed suckling.
C) She gets half the wage because she performed part of the duty.
D) She must compensate the father for the milk's cost.

Key Takeaway
The wet nurse must perform customary services (washing, feeding, oiling) without extra pay; if she fails to suckle, she forfeits her wage.

Hiring for Acts of Worship: The Hanafi Position and Its Proofs
Presents the Hanafi ruling and inter-madhhab dispute on hiring for acts of worship

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi ruling that hiring for adhan and imamah is invalid, identify the opposing school's proofs, and apply the Hanafi textual evidence to evaluate the qiyas arguments.

Core Idea
You cannot take wages for worship—explicit hadith override analogy.

This lesson examines a classic fiqh dispute: may one hire someone to give the adhan or lead prayers? The Hanafi school, relying on explicit prophetic prohibitions, declares such contracts invalid. The Shafi'i, Maliki, and some Hanbali scholars permit it using qiyas from marriage, ruqyah, and public treasury. We will analyse the evidence and understand why the Hanafi ruling prevails.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify the specific ruling: hiring for adhan and imamah is invalid (لم تصح). Note that this applies to all acts of worship that are not purely worldly services.
The Hanafi view is supported by the hadith of Abd al-Rahman ibn Shibl and Ubada ibn al-Samit.
2
Identify the opposing school and their proofs
al-Shafi'i, Malik, and Ahmad (in one narration) permit hiring for acts that are not personally obligatory (fard 'ayn). Their proof uses qiyas: marriage for teaching Quran, Abu Sa'id's ruqyah for sheep, and salary from Bait al-Mal.
They argue that if compensation is allowed in one context (marriage, ruqyah, treasury), it should be allowed in ijarah.
3
Analyse the Hanafi textual evidence
Examine the hadith of Abd al-Rahman ibn Shibl: 'Recite the Quran and do not eat from it...' – this is a direct prohibition of taking wages for recitation/teaching. Also the hadith of Ubada ibn al-Samit where the Prophet disapproved of taking a bow for teaching Quran.
The Hanafis argue these texts are explicit and override any analogy.
4
Evaluate the qiyas and the tarjih
The Hanafi response: marriage compensation is not ijarah (it is mahr), ruqyah was a specific permission, and Bait al-Mal is a public trust, not a private contract. Since worship acts are devotional, they cannot be subject to hire. The Hanafi position is adopted as mufta bihi.
The thamarah al-khilaf: in Hanafi law, paying for adhan/imamah is haram and the contract is fasid; in Shafi'i law it is permissible.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولم تصح للأذان ، والإمامة
قوله : ولم تصح للأذان؛ إلى قوله والفقه، وهو نص أحمد، وقول عطاء والضحاك والزهري والحسن وابن سيرين وطاوس والنخعي والشعبي. وقال الشافعي ومالك وأحمد في رواية: تصح في كل ما لا يتعين على الأجير حتى لو تعين الإفتاء أو الإمامة على واحد لا تصح إجارته؛ لأن النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم زوج رجلاً بما معه من القرآن، وإذا جاز تعليم القرآن عوضاً في باب النكاح جاز في باب الإجارة. ولأن أبا سعيد الخدري رقى بفاتحة الكتاب، وأخذ قطيعاً من الغنم واقتسمه هو وأصحابه بأمر النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم وقال له: «إن أحق ما أخذتم عليه أجراً كتاب الله»؛ ولأنه يجوز أخذ الرزق عليه من بيت المال، فيجوز أخذ الأجر عليه؛ لأنه بمعناه؛ ولأنه قد يحتاج إلى الاستنابة في الحج عمن وجب عليه وعجز عن فعله، ولا يوجد متبرع به. ولنا: ما رواه أحمد واسحاق بن راهويه وابن شيبة وعبد الرزاق له من حديث عبد الرحمن بن شبل قال: سمعت رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم يقول: «اقرؤوا القرآن ولا تأكلوا به، ولا تحضوا عنه، ولا تغلوا فيه، ولا تستكثروا به» وما رواه أبو داود وابن ماجه عن عبادة بن الصامت له قال: علمت ناساً من أهل الصفة القرآن، وأهدى إلي رجل منهم قوساً، فقلت: ليست بمال وأرمي بها في...
And it (the hire) is not valid for the adhan and the imamah. His saying: 'And it is not valid for the adhan' up to his saying 'and fiqh'—that is the text of Ahmad, and the saying of Ata, al-Dahhak, al-Zuhri, al-Hasan, Ibn Sirin, Tawus, al-Nakhai, and al-Sha'bi. And al-Shafi'i, Malik, and Ahmad in one narration said: It is valid for everything that is not specific to the hired person, such that if fatwa or imamah is specific to one person, his hiring is not valid; because the Prophet (peace be upon him) married a man with what he had of Quran, and if teaching Quran is permissible for compensation in the chapter of marriage, it is permissible in the chapter of ijarah. And because Abu Sa'id al-Khudri performed ruqyah with the Fatiha and took a flock of sheep and divided it among him and his companions by order of the Prophet (peace be upon him), and he said to him: 'The most worthy thing for which you take a wage is the Book of God.' And because it is permissible to take sustenance from the treasury for it, so it is permissible to take wages for it; because it is in the same meaning. And because there may be need for hiring for Hajj on behalf of one who is obligated but unable, and there is no volunteer. And our (Hanafi) proof: what Ahmad, Ishaq ibn Rahawayh, Ibn Shayba, and Abd al-Razzaq narrated from Abd al-Rahman ibn Shibl who said: I heard the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) say: 'Recite the Quran and do not eat from it, and do not make it a means to gain, and do not exaggerate in it, and do not seek to increase through it.' And what Abu Dawud and Ibn Majah narrated from Ubada ibn al-Samit who said: I taught the people of al-Suffa the Quran, and a man among them gave me a bow, so I said: It is not wealth and I shoot with it...
Source pages p. 558

Commentary
This passage is an inter-madhhab dispute (inter_madhhab_dispute). The Hanafi school (with a group of early scholars) rules that hiring for adhan, imamah, and similar acts of worship is invalid (batil). The opposing view (Imam al-Shafi'i, Imam Malik, and Ahmad in one narration) holds that hiring for such acts is valid unless the act is personally obligatory for the hired person (like if fatwa or imamah is specifically required of him). The opponent argues with three proofs: 1) The Prophet married a man with what he knew of Quran, teaching for compensation is allowed in marriage, so analogy with ijarah applies. 2) The hadith of Abu Sa'id al-Khudri who performed ruqyah with Fatiha and accepted a sheep as payment; the Prophet approved. 3) Taking salary from Bait al-Mal for these acts is allowed, so private hiring is similar. The Hanafi response (Lana) cites explicit prohibitions: the hadith of Abd al-Rahman ibn Shibl forbids eating from Quran (taking wages for recitation/teaching). The text begins also citing a hadith from Ubada ibn al-Samit which continues with the same prohibition. The Hanafi school relies on these explicit texts and considers qiyas invalid in worship (ibadat) since it contradicts the primary prohibition.

Key Terms
أذان (adhān): The call to prayer, an act of worship.
إمامة (imāma): Leading congregational prayer, an act of worship.
إجارة (ijāra): A contract of hire or lease where one party pays for a service or usufruct.
تعين (ta'ayyun): Personal specificity; when an act becomes obligatory on a particular individual.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the ruling on hiring someone to give the adhan for a specific prayer?
A) Valid, because it is a needed service.
B) Invalid, because adhan is an act of worship and cannot be hired.
C) Permissible if the payer is wealthy.
D) Makruh tanzihi, disliked but not haram.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school prohibits hiring for adhan and imamah based on explicit prophetic hadith, and this prohibition overrides analogical reasoning from other permissible compensations.

Hiring a Wet Nurse When Mother's Milk is Stipulated
Ruling on hire of wet nurse when mother's milk condition

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on hiring a wet nurse when the mother's milk is stipulated and explain the basis for the difference of opinion.

Core Idea
Stipulating the mother's milk can void the wet nurse's wage entitlement.

This passage addresses a specific scenario in contracts of hire (ijara): when a mother has agreed to breastfeed her child but hires another woman to do so. The central question is whether the wet nurse deserves her wage. The text presents two opinions within the Hanafi school, with the primary view cautioning against automatic entitlement due to the potential superiority of the mother's milk. Understanding this ruling helps clarify how conditions in marriage contracts affect subsequent hire agreements.

Guided Path
1
Identify the contractual condition
The mother's milk is stipulated in the marriage contract. This means the mother is obliged to breastfeed the child herself.
2
State the primary ruling
According to al-Muhit, if the mother hires a wet nurse, the wet nurse does not deserve the wage because the mother's milk might be of superior quality, thus the stipulated condition is not fulfilled.
This view is attributed to the more cautious approach.
3
State the counter-opinion
Some scholars hold that the wet nurse does deserve the wage because the difference between the two milks is negligible, so the condition is effectively met.
This opinion is introduced with 'قيل' (it is said), indicating a weaker transmission.
4
Evaluate the tarjih
The passage does not explicitly choose, but the phrase 'قيل' suggests the first opinion is more relied upon. Later Hanafi works may give preference to one view.
A mufti would need to check later fatwa collections for the mufta bihi position.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وهو الإرضاع؛ لأن الأوّل إيجار والثاني تغذية، وذكر الشمني نقلاً عن «المحيط» : لو كان إرضاعها مشروطاً فاستأجرت ظئراً فأرضعته لا يستحق الأجر؛ لأنَّ لبنها ربّما يكون أجود، وقيل : يستحق لأنَّ التفاوت بين اللبنين يسير. انتهى.
And it is breastfeeding; because the first is hire and the second is feeding. And al-Shumni mentioned, quoting from al-Muhit: If her breastfeeding is stipulated, and she hired a wet nurse and the wet nurse breastfed the child, she does not deserve the wage, because her own milk might be superior. And it is said: she deserves, because the difference between the two milks is slight. End.
Source pages p. 558

Commentary
This passage is a ruling statement regarding the validity of hiring a wet nurse when the mother's milk has been stipulated in the marriage contract. The author clarifies that the issue falls under breastfeeding (rida'). The first (the mother's own breastfeeding) is a contractual obligation (ijar) while the second (hiring another) is merely nourishment. Al-Shumni reports from al-Muhit a difference: If the mother's milk is stipulated and she hires another woman to breastfeed, the hired woman does not deserve the wage because the mother's milk might be of better quality. However, there is a counter-opinion that she does deserve it because the difference between the two milks is negligible. This reflects a nuanced approach: the Hanafi school considers the potential qualitative difference. The relied-upon position is not explicitly stated here, but the text gives both views.

Key Terms
الإرضاع (al-irda'): Breastfeeding; here specifically the act of nursing a child by the mother or a hired wet nurse.
ظئر (zir (pl. zu'ur)): A wet nurse hired to breastfeed a child.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Because the wet nurse's milk is inferior
B) Because the mother's milk might be superior
C) Because the wet nurse is not a professional
D) Because the contract is void

Key Takeaway
When mother's milk is stipulated, hiring a wet nurse may not fulfill the condition, affecting her entitlement to wage.

Prohibition of Wages for Acts of Worship (Qurbah)
Ruling with proof from Sunnah on wages for qurbah acts

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on wages for adhan and explain why it is prohibited using the hadith and qiyas reasoning.

Core Idea
Taking wages for pure acts of worship (qurbah) is prohibited because the act is attributed to the doer, nullifying the wage contract.

This lesson explains the Hanafi position on receiving wages for rituals like adhan. The source passage presents a hadith from Uthman ibn Abi al-As and a legal argument based on qiyas. By understanding the ruling and its rationale, you will be able to distinguish between permissible and impermissible compensation for religious services.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What exactly is being ruled upon? The act is taking a wage for performing adhan. The ruling is haram (prohibited).
2
Locate the dalil
Find the primary evidence. The hadith: Uthman ibn Abi al-As was commanded to appoint a mu'adhdhin who does not take a wage for his adhan.
Hadith narrated by Tirmidhi and others.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
How does the dalil prove the ruling? The explicit command 'لا يأخذ على أذانه أجراً' (does not take a wage for his adhan) indicates prohibition.
4
Apply qiyas
Extend the ruling to all pure qurbah acts. Since the act is attributed to the doer, the hired person's action is for himself, not the employer, so taking a wage is invalid.
Qiyas with fasting and prayer is mentioned in the text.
5
Address counterarguments
Examine the hadith 'The most worthy thing for which you take wages is the Book of Allah'. This is interpreted as a ja'ala (reward) for ruqya, not a hire for recitation. Ruqya is not a pure qurbah, so ja'ala is permissible.
This addresses a potential objection.

Source Text

كتاب الإجارة باب الإجارة الفاسدة
٥٥٩
سبيل الله ، فسألت النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم عن ذلك فقال : «إن أردت أن يطوقك الله طوقاً من نار
فاقبلها»(۱).
وما رواه أصحاب السنن الأربعة بطرق مختلفة عن عثمان بن أبي العاص ، قال : قلت : « يا رسول الله اجعلني إمام قومي ، قال : أنت إمامهم، واتخذ مؤذناً لا يأخذ على أذانه أجراً» (٢).
(۲)
وما رواه الترمذي في «جامعه» مسنداً إلى الحسن عن عثمان بن أبي العاص قال: «إن آخر ما عهد إلي رسول الله أن أتخذ مؤذناً لا يأخذ على أذانه أجراً (۳). ولأن القربة متى حصلت وقعت عن فاعلها ؛ ولهذا تعتبر أهليته ونيته لا نية الأمر وأهليته إن أوقعت على الآمر بشرط نيّة الآمر وأهليته كما في الزكاة، وإذا وقعت عن فاعلها كان عمل الأجير لنفسه لا للمستأجر ، فلا يجوز له أخذ الأجرة عليه كما في
الصوم والصلاة. وحديث التزويج ليس فيه تصريح بأن التعليم صداق، فلعله زوجها إياه بغير صداق إكراماً له، كما زوج أبا طلحة أم سليم على إسلامه، فإنّ النكاح يصح بدونِ ذكر المهر، ومع ذلك يجب مهر المثل، وتكون الباء مكان اللام : أي لما معك من القرآن أو لعل المرأة وهبت مهرها له باعتبار ذلك.
ومعنى: «أحق ما أخذتُم عليه أجراً كتاب الله الجعالة في الرقية ؛ لأنّ ذلك في سياق خير الرقية، ودائرة الجعالة أوسعُ من دائرة الإجارة ؛ ولهذا يجوز الجعالة مع جهالة العمل والمدة دون الإجارة، أو إنّ المأخوذ منه قطع من الغنم كان كافراً غير مستأمن ، فجار أخذ ماله أو إن حق الضيف واجب ولم يضيفوهم، أو إن الرقية ليست بقربة محضة، فجاز أخذ الإجارة عليه. وأما الرزق من بيت المال فيجوز على من يتعدى نفعه ؛ لأن بيت المال لمصالح المسلمين فجرى مجرى الوقف عليهم، بخلاف الأجرة.
وأما الاستنابة عن الحج، فللآمر ثواب الإنفاق، وبه يسقط القرض عنه، فيكون الأجرة للخدمة، أو لقطع المسافة، وعلى تقدير أنّ الأفعال تقع عن الأمر يكون إجارة عن الحج ، بل اتفاقاً على الغائب. كذا في «كمال الدراية»)، وغيرها.
The Book of Ijarah. Chapter on Invalid Ijarah. 559 ... (hadith) "If you want Allah to put a collar of fire around you, then accept it." And what was narrated by the authors of the four Sunan with various chains from Uthman ibn Abi al-As: He said: I said: O Messenger of Allah, appoint me as imam of my people. He said: You are their imam, and appoint a mu'adhdhin who does not take a wage for his adhan. And what was narrated by al-Tirmidhi in his Jami' from al-Hasan from Uthman ibn Abi al-As: He said: Indeed, the last thing that the Messenger of Allah enjoined upon me was that I appoint a mu'adhdhin who does not take a wage for his adhan. And because whenever a qurbah (act of worship) occurs, it is attributed to its doer; hence his eligibility and intention are considered, not the intention and eligibility of the employer, if it is carried out on behalf of the employer with the condition of the employer's intention and eligibility, as in zakat. And when it is attributed to its doer, the work of the hired person is for himself, not for the employer, so it is not permissible for him to take wages for it, as in fasting and prayer. And the hadith of marriage does not explicitly state that teaching was the dowry; perhaps he married her to him without a dowry as an honor, just as he married Abu Talha to Umm Sulaym on his embracing Islam. Indeed, marriage is valid without mention of the dowry, and nevertheless the dowry of the like is obligatory, and the ba is in place of lam: meaning for what you have of the Quran, or perhaps the woman waived her dowry to him in consideration of that. And the meaning of "The most worthy thing for which you take wages is the Book of Allah" is a ja'ala (reward) for ruqya (incantation); because that is in the context of "the best of ruqya", and the scope of ja'ala is wider than the scope of ijarah; hence ja'ala is permissible with ignorance of the work and duration, unlike ijarah. Or that the one from whom the sheep was taken was a disbeliever not under protection, so he took his wealth wrongfully, or the right of the guest is obligatory and they did not host them, or that ruqya is not a pure act of worship, so taking wages for it became permissible. As for the allowance from the treasury (bayt al-mal), it is permissible for one whose benefit extends to others; because the treasury is for the interests of the Muslims, so it runs like a waqf upon them, unlike the wage. As for deputizing for Hajj, the employer gets the reward of spending, and by it the debt is discharged from him, so the wage is for service or for covering the distance, and on the assumption that the actions occur on behalf of the employer, it becomes a hire for Hajj, rather it is agreed upon for the absentee. Thus in Kamil al-Dirayah and others.
Source pages p. 559

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof from the Sunnah. It opens with two hadith prohibiting taking wages for the adhan (call to prayer). The first hadith warns of a collar of fire, and the second commands Uthman ibn Abi al-As to appoint a mu'adhdhin who does not take wages. The legal reasoning follows: acts of worship (qurbah) are attributed to the doer; therefore, the hired person's action is for himself, not for the employer, so receiving wages is invalid. The principle is applied to fasting and prayer. The passage then addresses counterarguments: the hadith about teaching Quran as a dowry is explained as a gift or waiver of dowry, not a wage for teaching. The hadith 'The most worthy thing for which you take wages is the Book of Allah' is interpreted as a reward (ja'ala) for ruqya, not a hire contract for recitation, distinguishing ja'ala from ijarah. The discussion also covers permissibility of wages for ruqya (as it is not a pure qurbah), rizq from bayt al-mal (which is like a stipend, not wages), and the case of deputizing for Hajj, where the wage is for service or travel, not for the Hajj itself, and if treated as hiring, it would be invalid. The overall ruling is that taking wages for pure acts of worship is prohibited in the Hanafi madhhab.

Key Terms
قربة (qurbah): An act of worship that brings one closer to Allah, such as prayer, fasting, adhan, etc.
إجارة (ijarah): A contract of hire or lease where wages are paid for a known benefit.
جعالة (ja'ala): A reward or commission for a specific result, such as ruqya, where work and duration may be unknown.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why is it not permissible to take wages for the adhan according to the Hanafi madhhab?
A) Because the mu'adhdhin must be a volunteer.
B) Because acts of worship (qurbah) are attributed to the doer, so the hired person's action is for himself.
C) Because the salary from the mosque endowment covers it.
D) Because the Prophet (saw) prohibited it only for the companion Uthman.

Key Takeaway
Taking wages for pure acts of worship is prohibited because the act is attributed to the doer, making the contract invalid.

Wages for Teaching Quran: Permissible by Istihsan
Intra-Hanafi dispute on wages for Quran teaching vs recitation

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish the Hanafi positions on taking wages for Quran teaching versus recitation, and apply the mufta bihi ruling.

Core Idea
Teaching Quran for a fee is permissible by istihsan; mere recitation for money is not.

This passage presents an important intra-Hanafi refinement. While early authorities like Taj al-Shari'a and al-Ayni strongly prohibited any wage for Quran-related acts, later Hanafi fatwa – by istihsan – permits payment for teaching the Quran. The key distinction lies in the nature of the service: teaching involves effort and benefit, while mere recitation for money corrupts intention. Let's trace the arguments.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two positions
Recognize that there are two views within the Hanafi school: (1) absolute prohibition of any wage for Quran-related acts, and (2) permissibility by istihsan for teaching but not for mere recitation.
The prohibition view is held by Taj al-Shari'a and al-Ayni; the permissibility view is the mufta bihi by Khayr al-Din al-Ramli.
2
Examine the reasoning for prohibition
Taj al-Shari'a and al-Ayni argue that taking wages for Quran eliminates reward (thawab) because the intention becomes worldly. Both the reciter and the giver become sinful. Thus, the common practice of reciting ajza' for wages is impermissible.
The core argument is that the Quran should not be a means of worldly gain; reward requires sincere intention for Allah.
3
Examine the reasoning for permissibility by istihsan
Khayr al-Din al-Ramli states that the mufta bihi is permissibility by istihsan for teaching the Quran, not for mere recitation. Istihsan allows departure from strict qiyas due to necessity and public benefit.
Istihsan is a distinctive Hanafi principle that considers need and ease.
4
Understand the distinction: teaching vs. recitation
Teaching involves service, effort, and skill; it is akin to other permissible contracts like ijarah or ja'ala. Mere recitation for money does not involve such service and hence remains prohibited.
This distinction is critical for fatwa: hiring a teacher is fine, but paying someone to recite at a funeral is not.
5
Note the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical difference is that in fatwa, teaching Quran for a fee is allowed, while reciting Quran for money without teaching is prohibited. Many contemporary issues, such as paying for online Quran classes or hiring reciters, hinge on this distinction.
The later fatwa overrides earlier strictness to meet community needs.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
[٢] قوله : وتعليم القرآن ; قال تاج الشريعة له في «شرح الهداية»: إن القرآن بالأجرة لا يستحق الثواب لا للميت ولا للقارئ، وقال العيني في «شرح الهداية»: ويمنع القارئ للدنيا، والآخذ والمعطي آثمان.
فالحاصل أن ما شاع في زماننا من قراءة الأجزاء بالأجرة لا يجوز؛ لأن فيه الأمر بالقراءة، وإعطاء الثواب للأمر، والقراءة لأجل المال، فإذا لم يمكن للقارئ ثواب لعدم النية الصحيحة فأين يصلُ الثوابُ إلى المستأجر، ولولا الأجرة ما قرأ أحد لأحد في هذا الزمان، بل جعلوا القرآن العظيم مكسباً ووسيلة إلى جمع ا الدنيا ، ، إنا لله وإنا إليه راجعون. انتهى.
وقال الشيخ خير الدين الرملي في «حاشية البحر» في «كتاب الوقف»: أقول : المفتي به جواز الأخذ استحساناً على تعليم القرآن لا على القراءة المجردة. كما صرح به في «التاتارخانية حيث قال : لا معنى لهذه الوصيّة، ولصلة القارئ بقراءته ؛ لأنَّ هذا
[2] His saying: And teaching the Quran; Taj al-Shari'a said in his commentary on al-Hidayah: Indeed, the Quran with wages does not earn reward, neither for the deceased nor for the reciter. And al-Ayni said in his commentary on al-Hidayah: And it prevents the reciter (from reward) for worldly gain, and the taker and the giver are sinful. Therefore, what has become common in our time of reciting the ajza' (parts of the Quran) for wages is not permissible; because it involves ordering the recitation, giving the reward to the employer, and reciting for money. So if the reciter cannot have reward due to lack of correct intention, then how does the reward reach the employer? And were it not for the wage, no one would recite for anyone in this time; rather, they have made the great Quran a means of earning and a means of accumulating wealth. Inna lillahi wa inna ilayhi raji'un. End. And Shaykh Khayr al-Din al-Ramli said in his Hashiya on al-Bahr in the Book of Waqf: I say: The mufta bihi is the permissibility of taking (wages) by istihsan for teaching the Quran, not for mere recitation. As is stated in al-Tatarkhaniyyah, where he said: There is no meaning to this bequest, and (it is) for the connection of the reciter with his recitation; because this...
Source pages p. 560

Commentary
This passage discusses the ruling on taking wages for teaching or reciting the Quran. It presents two views within the Hanafi school. The earlier view, from Taj al-Shari'a and al-Ayni, holds that taking wages for Quran recitation is impermissible and sinful; the reciter does not earn reward, and both the giver and taker are sinful. They argue that the practice of reciting Quran for money is forbidden because the intention becomes corrupt. However, the later mufta bihi (operative fatwa) from Khayr al-Din al-Ramli permits taking wages by istihsan for teaching the Quran, but not for mere recitation. This distinction is important: teaching involves effort and service, whereas mere recitation for money is a means of worldly gain. The mufta bihi relies on the principle of istihsan, which allows flexibility in certain contracts, such as ja'ala, which is broader than ijarah. Thus, in the Hanafi school, teaching Quran for a fee is permissible, but reciting Quran for hire without teaching is not.

Key Terms
تعليم القرآن (ta'lim al-Qur'an): Teaching the Quran, including instruction in recitation, tajweed, etc.
قراءة مجردة (qira'a mujarrada): Mere recitation of the Quran without teaching or other service.
استحسان (istihsan): Juristic preference; a method of reasoning that allows departure from qiyas for a more suitable ruling.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the later Hanafi fatwa of Khayr al-Din al-Ramli, what is the ruling on taking wages for teaching the Quran?
A) It is absolutely prohibited.
B) It is permissible by istihsan for teaching but not for mere recitation.
C) It is recommended.
D) It is permissible only if the money is given to charity.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school holds that taking wages for teaching the Quran is permissible by istihsan, but mere recitation for money is prohibited.

Wages for Quran Teaching and Recitation: Intra-Hanafi Dispute
Intra-Hanafi dispute on wages for Quran teaching and recitation

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish the Hanafi positions on wages for teaching vs. recitation of the Quran and apply the concept of istihsan to this case.

Core Idea
Teaching the Quran for wages is permissible by istihsan; recitation for wages is generally invalid, but later Hanafis allow it at graves.

This passage from a sharh on al-Hidayah presents an intra-Hanafi dispute about taking wages for Quran-related activities. The commentator navigates between strict early views and later relaxations, showing how necessity (teaching) and changing custom (grave recitation) prompted a shift through istihsan. This lesson will walk you through the positions and the reasoning.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its initial ruling
Distinguish teaching from recitation; note the strict early view: no reward, sinful for both giver and taker.
Al-'Ayni and Taj al-Shari'ah represent this view.
2
Locate the opposing positions within the madhhab
Identify who holds what: early scholars (al-'Ayni, Taj al-Shari'ah) prohibit all wages; later scholars (al-Ramli, al-Tahtawi) allow teaching by istihsan, and some allow grave recitation.
Opposition is intra-Hanafi, not inter-madhhab.
3
Analyze the dalil for each position
Strict: lack of sincere intention, no precedent from caliphs, semblance of hiring the Quran. Permissive: istihsan due to necessity for teaching; for recitation, custom and later consensus allow it.
Istihsan is the key Hanafi tool here.
4
Evaluate the tarjih mechanism
Determine which view is mufta bihi: al-Ramli states teaching is mufta bihi; later fatwas (al-‘Alamkiriyyah, al-Tahtawi) accept grave recitation.
Note the shift over time.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
Practical impact: today paying for Quran teachers is allowed; paying for reciters at graves is controversial but increasingly accepted in Hanafi fatwa.
The dispute remains alive; a mufti must know both views.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : وتعليم القرآن قال تاج الشريعة له في «شرح الهداية»: إن القرآن بالأجرة لا يستحق الثواب لا للميت ولا للقارئ، وقال العيني في «شرح الهداية»: ويمنع القارئ للدنيا، والآخذ والمعطي آثمان. فالحاصل أن ما شاع في زماننا من قراءة الأجزاء بالأجرة لا يجوز؛ لأن فيه الأمر بالقراءة، وإعطاء الثواب للأمر، والقراءة لأجل المال، فإذا لم يمكن للقارئ ثواب لعدم النية الصحيحة فأين يصلُ الثوابُ إلى المستأجر، ولولا الأجرة ما قرأ أحد لأحد في هذا الزمان، بل جعلوا القرآن العظيم مكسباً ووسيلة إلى جمع الدنيا، إنا لله وإنا إليه راجعون. انتهى. وقال الشيخ خير الدين الرملي في «حاشية البحر» في «كتاب الوقف»: أقول : المفتي به جواز الأخذ استحساناً على تعليم القرآن لا على القراءة المجردة. كما صرح به في «التاتارخانية» حيث قال : لا معنى لهذه الوصيّة، ولصلة القارئ بقراءته ؛ لأن هذا بمنزلة الأجرة، والإجارة في ذلك باطلة، وهي بدعة، ولم يفعلها أحد من الخلفاء، وقد ذكرنا مسألة تعليم القرآن على استحسان ؛ أي للضرورة، ولا ضرورة في الاستئجار على القراءة على القبر. انتهى. وفيه رد صاحب «البحر» حيث علل البطلان بأنه مبني على القول بكراهة القرآن على القبر وليس كذلك، بل لما فيه من شبهة الاستئجار على القبر. وقال في «الولوالجيّة»: لو زار قبر صديق أو قريب له وقرأ عنده شيئاً من القرآن فهو حسن، أمّا الوصيّة بذلك فلا معنى لها، ولا معنى أيضاً لصلة القارئ ؛ لأن ذلك يشبه استئجاره على قراءة القرآن وذلك باطل، ولم يفعل ذلك أحد من الخلفاء. انتهى. فلو كانت العلة ما قاله صاحب «البحر» لم يصح قوله هنا، فهو حسن. ونقل العلامة الخلوتي في «حاشية المنتهى الحنبلي» عن شيخ الإسلام تقي الدين ما نصه : ولا يصح الاستئجار على القراءة وإهدائها إلى الميت ؛ لأنه لم ينقل عن أحدٍ من الأئمة الإذن في ذلك، وقد قال العلماء : إنّ القارئ إذا قرأ لأجل المال فلا ثواب له، فأي شيء يهديه إلى الميت، وإنّما يصل إلى الميت العمل، والاستئجار على مجرد التلاوة لم يقل به أحد من الأئمة، وإنّما تنازعوا في الاستئجار على التعليم. انتهى هذا ما التقطته من رد المحتار. وقال في الفتاوى «العالمكيرية»: واختلفوا في الاستئجار على قراءة القرآن على القبر مدة معلومة، قال بعضهم : تجوزُ وهو المختار، كذا في «السراج الوهاج». انتهى. وقال العلامة الطحطاوي في حاشيته على الدر المختار: والمختار جواز الاستئجار على قراءة القرآن على القبور مدة معلومة. وفي «الحَمَوِيّ) ما نصه : ونقل العلامة المقدسي من هامش نسخة من «القنية»: ما نصه وفي «الكواشي»: المستأجر للختم ليس له أن يأخذ الأجر أقل من خمسة وأربعين
His statement: 'and teaching the Quran.' Taj al-Shari'ah said in Sharh al-Hidayah: Indeed, for the Quran with wages, no reward is earned neither for the deceased nor for the reciter. Al-'Ayni said in Sharh al-Hidayah: The reciter for worldly gain is prohibited, and the taker and giver are sinful. The conclusion: what has become common in our time of reciting parts (ajza') for wages is not permissible; because it involves commanding the recitation, giving the reward to the commander, and recitation for wealth. If the reciter cannot have reward due to lack of sincere intention, how will the reward reach the hirer? Were it not for the wage, no one would recite for anyone in this time; rather they have made the great Quran a means of earning and collecting worldly wealth. 'Inna lillahi wa inna ilayhi raji'un.' End. Al-Shaykh Khayr al-Din al-Ramli said in Hashiyat al-Bahr in Kitab al-Waqf: I say: The mufta bihi (relied-upon) opinion is the permissibility of receiving (wages) by istihsan for teaching the Quran, not for mere recitation. As stated in al-Tatarkhaniyyah where he said: There is no meaning to this bequest, nor to the gift to the reciter for his recitation; because this is like wages, and hiring (ijarah) in that is invalid, it is an innovation, and none of the caliphs did it. And we have mentioned the issue of teaching the Quran by istihsan, i.e., due to necessity; and there is no necessity in hiring for recitation at the grave. End. In this is a refutation of the author of al-Bahr who explained the invalidity by saying it is based on the opinion that reciting Quran at the grave is disliked; it is not so, but rather due to the semblance of hiring at the grave. And it is said in al-Walwalijiyyah: If one visits the grave of a friend or relative and recites some Quran there, it is good. As for a bequest for that, it has no meaning, nor does a gift to the reciter; because that resembles hiring him for Quran recitation, and that is invalid, and none of the caliphs did it. End. If the cause were what the author of al-Bahr said, his statement here would not be correct; so it is good. And al-Allamah al-Khalwati in Hashiyat al-Muntaha al-Hanbali narrated from Shaykh al-Islam Taqi al-Din the text: Hiring for recitation and gifting it to the deceased is not valid; because it has not been reported from any of the imams that they permitted that. The scholars have said: When the reciter recites for wealth, he has no reward, so what does he gift to the deceased? Only the action reaches the deceased. Hiring for mere recitation has not been said by any imam; they only disputed over hiring for teaching. End. This is what I extracted from Radd al-Muhtar. And it is said in al-Fatawa al-‘Alamkiriyyah: They differed about hiring for reciting the Quran at the grave for a fixed period. Some said it is permissible, and it is the chosen opinion, as in al-Siraj al-Wahhaj. End. And al-Allamah al-Tahtawi in his Hashiyah on al-Durr al-Mukhtar said: The chosen opinion is the permissibility of hiring for reciting the Quran at graves for a fixed period. And in al-Hamawi there is text: Al-Allamah al-Maqdisi transmitted from the margin of a copy of al-Qunyah: the text: In al-Kawashi: The hirer for a khatm (complete recitation) should not take less than forty-five (dirhams?) as wage.
Source pages p. 560

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute about wages for Quran-related activities. The commentator addresses the matn 'and teaching the Quran.' He first presents a strict view: Taj al-Shari'ah and al-'Ayni from Sharh al-Hidayah state that taking wages for reciting the Quran yields no reward for reciter or deceased, and both giver and taker are sinful. The common practice of reciting portions for pay is invalid because the reciter lacks sincerity and thus no reward can be gifted. However, later Hanafi authorities soften this. Shaykh Khayr al-Din al-Ramli states the mufta bihi is that taking wages for teaching the Quran is permissible by istihsan (juristic preference) due to necessity, but not for mere recitation. Al-Tatarkhaniyyah reiterates that hiring for recitation is invalid, a bid'ah, and not done by the caliphs. The discussion extends to specifically recitation at graves: al-Walwalijiyyah says visiting and reciting voluntarily is fine, but bequests or gifts for it are like hiring. The author of al-Bahr had explained invalidity as based on dislike of Quran at graves, but the text rejects that, saying the real reason is the semblance of hiring. Yet later, al-Fatawa al-‘Alamkiriyyah and al-Tahtawi report that some Hanafis choose the permissibility of hiring for Quran recitation at graves for a fixed period. There is thus a genuine intra-madhhab ikhtilaf. The passage ends with a note from al-Kawashi setting a minimum wage for a full khatm. Throughout, the core distinction is between teaching (permissible by istihsan) and mere recitation (generally not permissible, with some later exceptions for graves).

Key Terms
الاستحسان (al-istiḥsān): Juristic preference; a Hanafi method that departs from strict qiyas for equity or necessity.
القراءة على القبر (al-qirāʾah ʿalā al-qabr): Recitation of Quran at a grave, often for the deceased's benefit.
النيابة (al-niyābah): Acting on behalf of another, as a proxy or agent.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the mufta bihi position mentioned by Shaykh Khayr al-Din al-Ramli, for which activity is taking wages permissible by istihsan?
A) Reciting Quran at the grave
B) Teaching the Quran
C) Reciting Quran for the living
D) Gifting reward of recitation

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school permits wages for Quran teaching by istihsan but generally prohibits wages for recitation, though later fatwas allow it at graves.

Hiring for Quran Recitation at Graves: A Hanafi Intra-Madhhab Dispute
Intra-Hanafi dispute on hiring for Quran recitation at graves

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the two Hanafi positions on hiring for Quran recitation at graves and identify the proofs used by each side.

Core Idea
Hiring for Quran recitation at graves is invalid per the dominant view, but some later Hanafis permit it — the dispute turns on necessity and analogy.

This passage presents a nuanced disagreement within the Hanafi school over whether one can hire a reciter to read Quran at a grave. The author first states the position of invalidity, citing the practice of the caliphs, then acknowledges a permissive view from later authorities. Understanding this dispute requires careful attention to the proofs and the distinction between teaching and recitation.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two positions
Note that the author presents his view (invalid) and later cites authorities who permit it for a fixed period. Locate the statements of each position.
The author leans toward invalidity but does not reject the permissive view.
2
Examine the proof for the invalid position
The key proof is the absence of practice among the Rightly-Guided Caliphs (ijma suknuti) and the argument that reciting for money yields no reward to gift. Also, the resemblance to hiring for worship (shubhat al-isti'jar).
3
Examine the proof for the permissive position
Some later scholars (al-Siraj al-Wahhaj, al-Tahtawi) choose permissibility based on necessity and the fact that the purpose is valid. They also cite that the madhhab has agreed on a minimum wage for khatm.
4
Analyze the author's tarjih
The author argues that the analogy to Hajj Badal is flawed because Hajj is obligatory, while Tarawih khatm is sunnah. He also refutes the claim that invalidity is due to dislike of reciting at graves.
The author does not decisively reject the permissive view, leaving the matter open.
5
Understand the thamarah al-khilaf
If hiring is invalid, the contract is void (batil) and the hirer owes nothing or at most the minimum wage (ujrat al-mithl). If permissible, the contract is valid and the agreed fee must be paid.

«البحر» حيث علل البطلان بأنه مبني على القول بكراهة القرآن على القبر وليس كذلك، بل لما فيه من شبهة الاستئجار على القبر. وقال في «الولوالجيّة»: لو زار قبر صديق أو قريب له وقرأ عنده فهو حسن، وأمّا الوصيّة بذلك فلا معنى لها، ولا معنى أيضاً لصلة القارئ؛ لأنَّ ذلك يشبه استئجاره على قراءة القرآن وذلك باطل، ولم يفعل ذلك أحد من الخلفاء. انتهى. فلو كانت العلة ما قاله صاحب «البحر» لم يصح قوله هنا، فهو حسن. ونقل العلامة الخلوتي في «حاشية المنتهى الحنبلي» عن شيخ الإسلام تقي الدين ما نصه: ولا يصح الاستئجار على القراءة وإهدائها إلى الميت؛ لأنه لم ينقل عن أحدٍ من الأئمة الإذن في ذلك، وقد قال العلماء: إنّ القارئ إذا قرأ لأجل المال فلا ثواب له، فأي شيء يهديه إلى الميت، وإنّما يصل إلى الميت العمل، والاستئجار على مجرد التلاوة لم يقل به أحد من الأئمة، وإنّما تنازعوا في الاستئجار على التعليم. انتهى هذا ما التقطته من رد المحتار). وقال في الفتاوى «العالمكيرية»: واختلفوا في الاستئجار على قراءة القرآن على القبر مدة معلومة، قال بعضهم: تجوزُ وهو المختار، كذا في «السراج الوهاج». انتهى. وقال العلامة الطحطاوي في حاشيته على الدر المختار: والمختار جواز الاستئجار على قراءة القرآن على القبور مدة معلومة. وفي «الحَمَوِيّ» ما نصه: ونقل العلامة المقدسي من هامش نسخة من «القنية»: ما نصه وفي «الكواشي»: المستأجر للختم ليس له أن يأخذ الأجر أقل من خمسة وأربعين درهماً شرعياً، هذا إذا لم يسم شيئاً من الأجر. كما ذكره في «الأصل»: أي «المبسوط» في رجل قال للقارئ: اختم القرآن ولم يسم شيئاً من الأجر وختمه، ليس له أن يأخذ أقل من خمسة وأربعين درهماً بعد العقد عليه، أو شرط أن يكون ثواب ما فوق لنفسه فلا يأثم. وعلى هذا لو قال القارئ: اقرأ ختماً بقدر ما قدرت من الأجر حين أمره المستأجر بالختم بأقل من خمسة وأربعين على ختم القرآن في التراويح كما اعتاده الحفاظ في زماننا فإنّهم يعينون الأجر من قبل، ويجبرون المستأجر عليه، والحال أن الختم في التراويح سنة لا واجبة، والقياس على حج البدل قياس مع الفارق، وحاله ما ذكرنا فتذكر.
In the position of wages, and the hiring for that is invalid, it is an innovation, and none of the caliphs did it. We have mentioned the issue of teaching the Quran by istihsan; that is for necessity, and there is no necessity in hiring for recitation at the grave. End. In it is a refutation of the author of 'al-Bahr' where he attributed the invalidity to the ruling that reciting Quran at the grave is disliked, but it is not so; rather, because of the suspicion of hiring for the grave. It is said in 'al-Walwaljiyyah': If one visits the grave of a friend or relative and recites there, it is good, as for bequest for that, it has no meaning, nor does gifting to the reciter have meaning; because that resembles hiring him for Quran recitation, and that is invalid, and none of the caliphs did that. End. If the cause were as the author of 'al-Bahr' said, his statement here would not be correct; it is good. Al-Allamah al-Khalwati narrated in his Hashiyah on al-Muntaha al-Hanbali from Shaykh al-Islam Taqi al-Din: It is not valid to hire for recitation and gifting to the deceased; because permission for that has not been reported from any of the imams, and the scholars have said: If the reciter recites for the sake of wealth, he has no reward, so what does he gift to the deceased? Only actions reach the deceased, and hiring for mere recitation has not been said by any of the imams; they only disputed about hiring for teaching. End. This is what I extracted from Radd al-Muhtar. It is said in Fatawa al-Alamgiriyyah: They differed about hiring for reciting Quran at the grave for a fixed period; some said it is permissible, and that is the chosen opinion, as in 'al-Siraj al-Wahhaj'. End. Al-Allamah al-Tahtawi said in his Hashiyah on al-Durr al-Mukhtar: The chosen opinion is the permissibility of hiring for reciting Quran at graves for a fixed period. And in 'al-Hamawi': Al-Allamah al-Maqdisi narrated from the margin of a copy of 'al-Qunyah': In 'al-Kawashi': The one hired for khatm should not take less than forty-five shar'i dirhams if no fee was specified. As mentioned in 'al-Asl': i.e. 'al-Mabsut' regarding a man who said to the reciter: Do a khatm of the Quran, and did not specify any fee, and he did so, he should not take less than forty-five dirhams after the contract; or if he stipulated that the reward of what is above is for himself, he does not sin. And on this, if the reciter said: Recite a khatm with as much as you can of the fee when the hirer ordered the khatm with less than forty-five, and he recited that amount of the Quran, a third or a quarter or a half or similar, he does not sin. End summarized. Al-Allamah al-Shami said in Radd al-Muhtar: What is narrated from some margins and attributed to 'Hawi al-Zahidi' that hiring for khatm from forty-five is not permissible is outside what the scholars of the madhhab have agreed upon. End. So reflect and ponder so that the strength of the evidence for impermissibility of hiring for Quran recitation due to the connection of reward to the deceased, whether at the grave or not, becomes clear to you, and hiring for Quran khatm in Tarawih as is the custom of the Huffaz in our time, for they fix the fee beforehand and compel the hirer, whereas khatm in Tarawih is sunnah not obligatory, and analogy to Hajj Badal is an analogy with a difference, and its state is as we mentioned, so remember.
Source pages p. 561

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute on the ruling of hiring someone to recite Quran at graves. The author begins by stating that hiring for recitation at graves is invalid (batil) and an innovation (bid'ah), as none of the caliphs did it. This is contrasted with teaching Quran, which is permissible by istihsan due to necessity. The author refutes the claim of the author of 'al-Bahr' that the invalidity is based on the dislike of reciting at graves; rather, it is because of the resemblance to hiring for the grave. Then the author quotes from 'al-Walwaljiyyah' that visiting graves and reciting is good, but bequest for it is meaningless, and gifting to the reciter is like hiring, which is invalid. A Hanbali source is also quoted asserting that hiring for recitation is impermissible because reciting for money yields no reward to gift. Next, the author cites conflicting opinions from Fatawa al-Alamgiriyyah and al-Tahtawi that the chosen opinion (mukhtar) is permissibility for a fixed period. A minimum wage of 45 dirhams is mentioned for khatm (complete recitation) when no fee is specified. Al-Shami in Radd al-Muhtar states that the prohibition of hiring for khatm from 45 dirhams is outside the consensus of the madhhab. Finally, the author concludes that the evidence for impermissibility is strong, especially since Tarawih khatm is sunnah not obligatory, and analogy to Hajj Badal is flawed. He advises reflection.

Key Terms
الإجارة الفاسدة (al-ijarah al-fasidah): A hire contract that is defective due to an illegality in the subject matter, e.g., hiring for an act of worship or for sin.
الاستئجار على الختم (al-isti'jar ala al-khatm): Hiring someone to complete a full recitation of the Quran (khatm), often in a specified period.
المختار (al-mukhtar): The chosen or preferred opinion in the madhhab for giving fatwa.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school is divided on hiring for Quran recitation at graves: the majority holds it invalid due to lack of caliphal practice and resemblance to hiring for worship, while later scholars permit it for fixed periods by necessity.

Hiring for Teaching and for Sins
Ruling on hire contracts for teaching and sinful acts

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish valid from invalid hire contracts based on the nature of the work (permissible vs. sinful) and explain the reason (ma'siyah cannot be legally owed).

Core Idea
A hire contract for a sinful act is invalid because sin cannot be owed by contract.

Not all hire contracts are valid in Islamic law. The Hanafi school clarifies that while hiring for teaching beneficial sciences and even worldly skills is valid by agreement, hiring for acts considered sinful—such as singing, wailing, or playing musical instruments—is fundamentally invalid. This lesson unpacks the reasoning behind this distinction, focusing on the concept of legal entitlement (istihqaq).

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
First, note the two categories: teaching permissible subjects (e.g., fiqh, writing, medicine) and sinful acts (e.g., singing, wailing). The passage rules the first valid (sahih) and the second invalid (batil).
The ruling on teaching is 'by agreement' (bil-ittifaq) among Hanafis.
2
Understand the key concept: istihqaq
The text explains that sin (ma'siyah) 'cannot be conceptually owed by contract' (la yatasawwaru istihqaquha bi al-'aqd). This means that a contract cannot create a legal entitlement to perform a sinful act.
Istihqaq is the right to demand performance or compensation.
3
Apply the concept to the hire fee
Since the sinful act cannot be legally owed, the hirer is not obligated to pay the wage (ujrah), and the hired worker has no legal claim to it. Mutual exchange requires mutual entitlement.
This nullifies the contract entirely; it is batil, not just fasid.
4
Contrast with permissible teaching
Permissible subjects (religious sciences like fiqh, worldly sciences like medicine) are valid objects of exchange. The contract creates mutual istihqaq: the teacher must teach, and the hirer must pay.
The passage lists 'writing, astronomy, medicine, interpretation' as permissible by agreement.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(1) قوله: والفقه؛ مثله التذكير والتدريس والعمرة مثل الحج، أما لو استأجره لتعليم ولده الكتابة أو النجوم أو الطب أو التعبير جاز بالاتفاق. كذا في «حاشية الطحطاوي على الدر المختار (۳). [٢] قوله: والغناء...الخ؛ يعني ولا يصح الإجارة على المعاصي كالغناء والنوح والملاهي؛ لأنَّ المعصية لا يتصوّر استحقاقها بالعقد، فلا يجب عليها الأجرة من غير أن يستحق هو على الأجير، إذ المبادلة لا تكون إلا بالاستحقاق كل منهما على الآخر.
(1) His saying: and fiqh; likewise tadhkir (reminder), teaching, and umrah like hajj. As for if he hires him to teach his son writing, astronomy, medicine, or interpretation, it is permissible by agreement. Thus in 'Hashiyat al-Tahtawi ala al-Durr al-Mukhtar'. [2] His saying: and singing...etc.; meaning it is not valid to hire for sins like singing, wailing, and musical instruments; because sin cannot be conceptually owed by contract, so the hire fee is not obligatory, and he does not have a right against the hired worker, since exchange only occurs when each has a right against the other.
Source pages p. 562

Commentary
This passage is a ruling statement about the validity of hire contracts. It clarifies that hiring for teaching religious sciences like fiqh (jurisprudence), tadhkir (reminding), tadris (teaching), and even umrah is valid, analogous to hajj. However, hiring for worldly subjects like writing, astronomy, medicine, and ta'bir (dream interpretation) is also permissible by agreement. In contrast, hiring for sins such as singing, wailing (nawh), and musical instruments (malahi) is invalid. The reason given is that a sin cannot be the subject of a valid contract because one cannot legally owe a sinful act. Therefore, the hire fee (ujrah) is not obligatory, and the hirer does not have a claim against the hired worker, as mutual exchange requires mutual legal entitlement.

Key Terms
المعصية (al-ma'siyah): A sinful act, something prohibited by shari'ah, such as singing, wailing, and musical instruments.
الاستحقاق (al-istihqaq): Legal entitlement; the right to demand something from another party through a valid contract.
بالاتفاق (bil-ittifaq): By agreement, i.e., all scholars concur on the ruling.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Because singing is not a useful skill
B) Because sin cannot be legally owed in a contract
C) Because it interferes with worship
D) Because it is not a fixed-term contract

Key Takeaway
A hire contract is valid only if the work is permissible; if the work is sinful, the contract is void because sin cannot be the subject of a legal entitlement.
