Ruling on Hiring for Quran Khatm with Wage Conditions
Ruling on hiring for Quran recitation with wage conditions and intra-madhhab dispute

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on hiring for Quran khatm and identify the minimum wage when unspecified.

Core Idea
Hiring for Quran recitation is valid with a minimum wage of 45 dirhams if unspecified.

This passage examines a common practice: hiring a reciter to complete the Quran for wage. The Hanafi school permits it with clear conditions. The text from al-Mabsut establishes a default minimum wage, allows the reciter to keep the reward for excess recitation, and refutes a minority view that prohibits it entirely. Understanding this ruling helps distinguish between valid contracts and potential sin.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Determine what is being ruled upon: hiring (isti'jar) someone to recite the Quran (khatm). The ruling is that such a contract is valid (sahih) with conditions.
The act is a form of ijarah (hire) for a service (recitation).
2
Analyze the wage condition
If the wage is unspecified, the reciter is entitled to a minimum of 45 dirhams after the contract. The reciter may stipulate that the reward (thawab) for any recitation beyond that minimum is for himself, thereby avoiding sin.
This is based on al-Mabsut (Zahir al-Riwayah).
3
Examine the intra-madhhab dispute
A minority view from Hawi al-Zahidi claims that hiring for khatm at 45 dirhams is impermissible. Allamah al-Shami in Radd al-Muhtar rejects it as outside the consensus of the Hanafi school.
The author cites ijma (consensus) of the madhhab as the proof.
4
Evaluate the ruling in practice
The text criticizes the common practice of hiring huffaz for Tarawih khatm with fixed wages, arguing that khatm in Tarawih is sunnah, not obligatory, and drawing analogy to Hajj al-Badal is invalid.
This highlights the need for clear contractual terms to avoid potential sin.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والفقه، والغناء) درهماً شرعياً، هذا إذا لم يسم شيئاً من الأجر. كما ذكره في «الأصل»: أي «المبسوط» في رجل قال للقارئ : اختم القرآن ولم يسم شيئاً من الأجر وختمه، ليس له أن يأخذ أقل من خمسة وأربعين درهماً بعد العقد عليه، أو شرط أن يكون ثواب ما فوق لنفسه فلا يأثم.
وعلى هذا لو قال القارئ : اقرأ ختماً بقدر ما قدرت من الأجر حين أمره المستأجر بالختم بأقل من خمسة وأربعين فقرأ من القرآن ذلك المقدار من الثلث أو الربع أو النصف أو نحوها فلا يأثم. انتهى ملخصاً.
وقال العلامة الشامي في رد المحتار (۱) : وما نقل عن بعض الهوامش، وعزى لـ«حاوي الزاهدي» من أنه لا يجوز الاستئجار على الختم من خمسة وأربعين فخارج عما اتَّفق عليه أهل المذهب قاطبة. انتهى.
فتفكر وتدبر ليظهر عليك قوّة دليل عدم جواز الاستئجار على قراءة القرآن لاتصال الثواب إلى الميت سواء كان على القبر أو لا، والاستئجار على ختم القرآن في التراويح كما اعتاده الحفاظ في زماننا فإنّهم يعينون الأجر من قبل، ويجبرون المستأجر عليه، والحال أن الختم في التراويح سنة لا واجبة، والقياس على حج البدل قياس مع الفارق، وحاله ما ذكرنا فتذكر.
And jurisprudence and singing. A legal dirham, this is when he did not specify any of the wage. As mentioned in al-Asl: i.e. al-Mabsut, regarding a man who said to the reciter: complete the Quran and did not name any wage, and he completed it: he is not entitled to take less than forty-five dirhams after the contract upon him; or if he stipulated that the reward for what is above (the minimum) be for himself, then he does not sin. And based on this, if the reciter said: read a khatm according to the extent I have power over the wage when the hirer ordered him to complete with less than forty-five, and he read from the Quran that amount (a third, a quarter, a half, or similar), then he does not sin. End of summary. And Allamah al-Shami said in Radd al-Muhtar: What is transmitted from some margins, attributed to Hawi al-Zahidi, that hiring for the khatm of forty-five is not permissible, is outside what the scholars of the madhhab have agreed upon entirely. End. So reflect and ponder so that the strength of the evidence for the impermissibility of hiring for reading the Quran becomes apparent to you, because the reward connects to the deceased whether at the grave or not; and hiring for the khatm of the Quran in Tarawih, as is the custom of the huffaz in our time, for they fix the wage beforehand and compel the hirer upon it, while the khatm in Tarawih is sunnah not obligatory; and the analogy to Hajj al-Badal is an analogy with a difference; its case is as we mentioned, so remember.
Source pages p. 562

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute on the ruling of hiring for Quran recitation (khatm). The text first states the ruling from al-Asl (al-Mabsut): if a person hires a reciter to complete the Quran without specifying a wage, the reciter is entitled to a minimum of forty-five dirhams as compensation. However, if the reciter stipulates that the reward (thawab) for the portion beyond the minimum is intended for himself, then the reciter does not sin. The ruling also applies if the reciter agrees to read only a portion (e.g., a third) for a wage less than forty-five dirhams. Then it mentions a minority view attributed to Hawi al-Zahidi that hiring for the khatm at forty-five dirhams is not permissible. Allamah al-Shami in Radd al-Muhtar rebuts this, stating it contradicts the consensus of the Hanafi school. The text then admonishes the reader to reflect on the strength of the evidence for the impermissibility of hiring for Quran recitation, because the reward reaches the deceased. It then criticizes the common practice of hiring huffaz for Tarawih khatm for a fixed wage, arguing that khatm in Tarawih is sunnah, not obligatory, and comparing it to Hajj al-Badal is an invalid analogy. The author urges careful consideration.

Key Terms
الاستئجار على الختم (al-isti'jar 'ala al-khatm): Hiring someone to recite the complete Quran (khatm) for wage.
ثواب ما فوق (thawab ma fawq): The spiritual reward for the portion of recitation above the minimum required by the wage.
حج البدل (hajj al-badal): Hiring someone to perform Hajj on behalf of another.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the minimum wage a reciter is entitled to if hired to complete the Quran without specifying a wage?
A) 40 dirhams
B) 45 dirhams
C) 50 dirhams
D) The reciter is entitled to nothing

Key Takeaway
Hiring for Quran recitation is valid with a minimum wage of 45 dirhams if unspecified, and the reciter may stipulate the reward for himself to avoid sin.

Prohibition of Hiring for Sinful Acts
Ruling on invalidity of lease for sinful acts

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on hiring for sinful acts and explain why the contract is invalid due to the impossibility of entitlement for sin.

Core Idea
Lease for a sinful act is invalid because entitlement to wage cannot arise from a sin.

This lesson examines the Hanafi position on leasing (ijara) for acts considered sinful, such as singing with instruments, wailing, and playing musical instruments. The text from 'Umdat al-Ri'aya argues that such contracts are void because the subject matter is inherently sinful and cannot be the basis of a valid exchange. We will explore the rationale and the unanimous agreement of the early Hanafi masters.

Guided Path
1
Identify the category of acts prohibited
List the specific sinful acts mentioned: singing (ghina'), wailing (nuh), musical instruments (malahi), and also chants and poetry.
These are considered ma'siyah (sinful) acts.
2
Understand the legal reason (illah)
The text states that sin cannot be 'entitled' by contract. Wage is due only when the hired service is lawful and can be properly owed. Since sin is not permissible, no entitlement arises.
The argument is based on the concept that a valid contract requires mutual entitlement to something permissible.
3
Recognize the unanimity of the Hanafi school
The passage cites Ghayat al-Bayan and Ramz al-Haqaiq confirming this as the position of Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, and Muhammad al-Shaybani.
No difference among the three imams.
4
Apply the ruling to contemporary practices
The author strongly rebukes those who hire qawwals or wailers for religious gatherings, declaring it an innovation. Modern parallels include hiring musicians for events or paid mourners.
The ruling is not limited to the examples given; any hiring for sin is invalid.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
[٢] قوله : والغناء...الخ ؛ يعني ولا يصح الإجارة على المعاصي كالغناء والنوح والملاهي؛ لأنَّ المعصية لا يتصوّر استحقاقها بالعقد، فلا يجب عليها الأجرة من غير أن يستحق هو على الأجير، إذ المبادلة لا تكون إلا بالاستحقاق كل منهما على الآخر.
ولو استحق على المعصية لكان ذلك مضافاً إلى الشارع من حيث أنه شرع عقداً موجباً للمعصية تعالى الله عن ذلك علواً كبيراً؛ ولذا قال في «غاية البيان»: لا تجوز الإجارة على شيء من الغناء والنوح والمزامير والطبل وشيء من اللهو، وعلى هذا الحداء وقراءة الشعر وغيره، ولا أجر في ذلك، هذا كله قول أبي حنيفة وأبي يوسف ومحمد . انتهى. وهكذا في رمز الحقائق»، وغيره من الكتب المعتبرة المعتمدة. فيا أسفاً على من تشيخ وعد نفسه من المتصوفين العارفين واستأجر القوال والمغنيين مشاهرة ومسانهة، وجعلَ هذا الاتفاق من أسباب الخير والسعادة، وزيادة الشوق والعرفان، وأمر عليه فضل نفسه، وأضلّ غيره، وصار من المبتدعين الغافلين ، هداه الله تعالى سواء الطريق، ووفقه خير التوفيق.
ويا حسرة على من عد نفسه من محبي آل الرسول عليه، واستأجر النائحين مسانهةً ومشاهرة لينوحوا على الإمام الهمام سيّد الشهداء المظلـوم في كربلاء له عـنـد ذكـر مصائبه، ويُبكوا أنفسهم ويبكوا غيرهم ممن حضر في ذلك المجلس، فقد أخطأ طريق الحق والصواب، وعدل عن سبيل الأجر والثواب، وخالف السنّة والكتاب، والموفّقُ هو الله التواب، وإليه المرجع والمآب.
[١] قوله : وعسب التيس ؛ العسب - بالفتح - : بكرایه دادن فحل جهت كشني و برجستن بزبر ماده و آب مني بزونسبل واولاد او. كذا في «المنتخب». يقال عسب الفحلُ الناقةَ عسباً من باب ضرب : طرقها، وعسبت الرجل عسباً : أعطيته الكراء على الضراب، ونهى عن عسب الفحل» وهو على حذف مضاف، والأصل عن كراء عسب الفحل ؛ لأنَّ ثمرته المقصودة غير معلومة، فإنّه قد يلقح وقد لا يلقح فهو غرر.
[2] His statement: 'and singing...etc.' means: lease is not valid for sins like singing, wailing, and musical instruments, because sin cannot be conceived as being entitled by contract, so the wage is not obligatory upon him, nor does he become entitled to the wage from the hired person, since exchange only occurs with mutual entitlement. And if entitlement occurred for sin, that would be attributed to the Lawgiver insofar as He legislated a contract giving rise to sin—exalted is Allah above that greatly. Hence it is said in Ghayat al-Bayan: Lease is not permissible for anything of singing, wailing, flutes, drum, or anything of play; and likewise for chants and reciting poetry and so on; and there is no wage for that. This is all the statement of Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, and Muhammad. End. And likewise in Ramz al-Haqaiq and other reliable and authoritative books. Oh regret for one who acts as a shaykh and counts himself among the Sufi knowers of Allah, and hires the qawwals and singers monthly and yearly, making this agreement a cause for good and happiness, increase of desire and gnosis, and thinks well of himself, leads others astray, and becomes one of the heedless innovators—may Allah guide him to the straight path and grant him success. And oh grief for one who counts himself among the lovers of the Prophet's family and hires wailers yearly and monthly to wail for the noble imam, the master of martyrs, the oppressed in Karbala, when his calamities are mentioned, and make themselves and those present in the gathering weep—he has indeed missed the path of truth and right, turned away from the way of reward and recompense, contradicted the Sunnah and the Book; success is from Allah, the Oft-Returning, and to Him is the return and abode. [1] His statement: 'and the sexual service of the he-goat': al-‘asb (with fatha) means: leasing a male animal for copulation, mounting the female, and the water (semen) for procreation and offspring. As in al-Muntakhab. It is said: the stallion covered the she-camel, a verbal noun, and I gave the fee for covering. And the Prophet (PBUH) forbade the sexual service of the stallion; it is with a deleted construct, originally 'for hire of the stallion's service' because its intended outcome is unknown—it may impregnate or may not—so it is gharar (uncertainty).
Source pages p. 562

Commentary
This passage consists of two separate but adjacent rulings on invalid leases. The first part discusses hiring for sinful acts (ma'asi). The commentator explains that lease (ijara) is not valid for actions that are sinful, such as singing (ghina'), wailing (nuh), and musical instruments (malahi). The reason given is that a sin cannot be the subject of a valid contract; entitlement to wage cannot arise from a sinful act, as that would imply the Lawgiver sanctions a contract that necessitates sin. This is the unanimous position of Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, and Muhammad al-Shaybani, as quoted from Ghayat al-Bayan and Ramz al-Haqaiq. The author then delivers a strong rebuke against those who pretend to be pious and yet hire qawwals and singers, and those who hire wailers to mourn the martyrdom of Imam Husain in Karbala, considering such acts as virtuous. The author declares such practices as innovations contrary to the Sunnah.

The second part defines 'casp al-tays' (hire of a male animal for breeding). The term 'asb' means the act of covering or mounting for reproduction. The Prophet (PBUH) forbade hiring a male animal for this purpose. The reason is that the intended outcome (pregnancy) is uncertain (gharar), as the animal may or may not impregnate. Thus, the contract is invalid due to uncertainty.

Key Terms
الغناء (al-ghina'): Singing, especially with musical accompaniment; considered a sinful act in this context.
النوح (al-nuh): Wailing or lamentation over the dead, often with exaggerated grief.
الملاهي (al-malahi): Musical instruments or anything that diverts from remembrance of Allah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the ruling on hiring a person to sing with musical instruments for a wedding?
A) Permissible because it brings joy
B) Permissible if the singer is a Muslim
C) Haram and the contract is invalid
D) Makruh but the contract is valid

Key Takeaway
Any lease whose subject is a sinful act is invalid and creates no obligation to pay, as sin cannot be the basis of a valid exchange.

Prohibition of Hiring for Animal Breeding (Gharar)
Ruling on invalidity of lease for animal breeding due to gharar

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on hiring a male animal for breeding and explain why the contract is invalid due to gharar.

Core Idea
Hiring an animal for breeding is prohibited because the outcome (pregnancy) is uncertain, making it a gharar contract.

This lesson addresses a specific type of lease: hiring a male animal (e.g., a stallion or he-goat) for breeding purposes. The Prophet (PBUH) explicitly forbade this practice. The Hanafi school explains that the prohibition is due to gharar (uncertainty) — the desired result (impregnation) may or may not occur, so the contract lacks certainty of the subject matter. We will examine the hadith and its legal rationale.

Guided Path
1
Understand the term 'asb al-tays'
The term refers to hiring a male animal for copulation, with the fee paid for the service of covering the female.
The author provides a definition from al-Muntakhab.
2
Identify the prophetic prohibition
The text quotes the hadith: 'نهى عن عسب الفحل' (He forbade the sexual service of the stallion).
This is the primary evidence.
3
Analyze the rationale (illah): gharar
The intended outcome (pregnancy) is unknown; the act may or may not result in conception. This uncertainty invalidates the contract.
Gharar is a key principle in Hanafi contract law.
4
Note the deletion in the hadith
The expression 'عسب الفحل' involves a deleted construct (mudaf mahzuf); the full meaning is 'hire of the stallion's service for breeding'.
This clarifies the subject of the contract.
5
Apply to similar modern cases
The ruling extends to any service with uncertain outcome, e.g., hiring a bull for artificial insemination if the fee is conditioned on success.
If the fee is for the act itself (regardless of result), some later scholars may differentiate.

Hiring for Musical Instruments and Singing is Invalid
Ruling on hiring for musical instruments, singing, and wailing

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on hiring for musical instruments, singing, and wailing, and explain why the contract is invalid.

Core Idea
A contract for a prohibited act is itself invalid—no wage is due and the contract is batil.

This passage establishes the Hanafi ruling that hiring for any amusement, including musical instruments, singing, wailing, and related activities, is invalid. The author cites the consensus of Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, and Muhammad al-Shaybani from Ghayat al-Bayan and then offers a strong condemnation of those who engage in such contracts, even for religious purposes. Understanding this ruling clarifies the boundaries of permissible contracts in Hanafi fiqh.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What is the act being judged? It is hiring (ijarah) for singing, musical instruments, wailing, and similar amusements. The ruling is that such a contract is invalid (batil).
2
Locate the evidence
The author quotes Ghayat al-Bayan, stating that hiring for these acts is not permissible and no wage is due. This is the saying of Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, and Muhammad—the three principal imams of the Hanafi school.
This is a citation of a secondary source that transmits the school's position.
3
Understand the rationale
The rationale is that a contract leading to sin cannot be attributed to the Lawgiver, who legislated contracts only for permissible ends. Since the object of the contract (singing, instruments) is itself prohibited, the contract is void.
This is an implicit argument based on the purpose of Shariah.
4
Note the practical consequence
When the contract is invalid, no wage (ujrah) is due for the service performed. The parties are sinful if they proceed.
5
See the application
The author laments those who hire qawwals or wailers for spiritual or mourning purposes, asserting that such actions contradict the Sunnah and Quran. This shows the ruling applies even when the act is religiously motivated.

[1] 563 And if it were worthy of disobedience, that would be attributed to the Lawgiver in that He legislated a contract causing disobedience - exalted is Allah above that greatly. Therefore it is said in Ghayat al-Bayan: Hiring is not permissible for anything of singing, wailing, flutes, drum, or any amusement; and likewise for driving camels with song, reciting poetry, and other things; and no wage is due for that. All this is the saying of Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf (2) and Muhammad. End quote. And likewise in Ramz al-Haqaiq and other relied-upon books. Alas for one who becomes a sheikh and counts himself among the Sufi gnostics, and hires qawwals and singers monthly and yearly, and makes this agreement a cause of good and happiness, increase of longing and gnosis, and passes over his own virtue, leads others astray, and becomes one of the heedless innovators. May Allah guide him to the straight path and grant him success. And regret for one who counts himself among the lovers of the family of the Prophet (peace be upon him) and hires wailers yearly and monthly to wail over the noble leader, the master of martyrs, the oppressed one in Karbala, when his calamities are mentioned, and they make themselves cry and make others cry who attend that gathering. Indeed he has erred from the path of truth and right, deviated from the way of reward and recompense, opposed the Sunnah and the Book. The Granter of success is Allah, the Oft-Relenting, and to Him is the return and destination.
Source pages p. 563

Commentary
This passage is a ruling statement from the chapter of invalid ijarah. The author begins by asserting that a contract involving disobedience cannot be attributed to the Lawgiver. He then quotes from Ghayat al-Bayan that hiring for singing, wailing, playing flutes, drum, or any amusement is not valid, and no wage is due. This is the consensus of the three imams: Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, and Muhammad al-Shaybani (may Allah have mercy on them). The same ruling is found in Ramz al-Haqaiq and other authoritative works. The commentator then expresses deep regret for those who consider themselves pious but engage in such contracts, hiring qawwals and singers, and for those who hire wailers to lament the tragedy of Karbala. He asserts that such actions contradict the Shariah, Sunnah, and Quran. This passage serves as a strong condemnation of these practices and affirms the Hanafi position that such contracts are invalid and sinful.

Key Terms
الملاهي (al-malahī): Musical instruments or amusements that distract from worship.
الغناء (al-ghinā'): Singing that is accompanied by musical instruments or that incites sin.
النوح (al-nawḥ): Wailing or lamentation over the dead with loud voice and tearing of clothes.

Key Terms from Source Passage

B) Makruh but wage is due
C) Invalid and no wage is due
D) Permissible only at weddings

Key Takeaway
Hiring for any amusement, musical instrument, singing, or wailing is invalid in the Hanafi school, and no wage is due.

Prohibition of Hiring a Male Goat for Breeding (ʿAsb al-Tays)
Inter-madhhab dispute on hiring a stud animal with Hanafi proof

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on hiring a male goat for breeding, identify the hadith proof, and evaluate the opposing analogy to wet nursing.

Core Idea
The Prophet forbade hiring a male goat for breeding because the outcome is uncertain — gharar invalidates the contract.

This lesson examines a classical dispute about hiring a male goat for breeding. The Hanafi school holds it is prohibited due to gharar and direct hadith prohibition, while some Hanbalis and Shafi'is analogize it to wet nursing. Understanding the Hanafi proof structure strengthens your ability to weigh textual evidence against analogy.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify the exact ruling: hiring a male goat for breeding (ʿasb al-tays) is prohibited (haram) and the contract is void; no wage is due.
The prohibition extends to any similar contract with gharar.
2
Identify the opposing school and their view
Abu al-Khattab al-Hanbali and some Shafi'is argue it is permissible because it is a beneficial service needed by people.
They compare it to hiring a wet nurse.
3
Follow the opponent's proof
The opposing dalil is qiyas: just as wet nursing is a benefit that can be hired despite some uncertainty, so too is breeding. They also note that lending the animal for breeding is allowed, so hiring should be too.
This is an argument from istihsan based on need.
4
Analyse the Hanafi response
The Hanafi school cites the explicit hadith 'He forbade the hire of a goat' (narrated by Bukhari, Abu Dawud, Tirmidhi, Nasa'i) and argues that the fluid is vile like carrion and blood, and fertilization is uncertain (gharar). Therefore, the analogy fails.
The hadith takes priority over qiyas.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical difference: Under Hanafi ruling, the contract is void and no payment is owed; under the opposing view, the contract is valid and the wage is due.
This affects actual transactions.

Then he said on page 564: And it is said: what is intended is the covering itself; that is weak, because the reproduction of animals is desired for itself; the interests of the servants - so the prohibition is not for itself to avoid contradiction but for an external reason. And in al-Misbah: al-tays is the male goat when a year has passed, and before the year it is al-jady, and the plural is tuyus, like falas and fulus. End. (4) And in Musnad Ahmad: 'from the price of the hire of a stallion'; and because it is taking wealth in exchange for despicable fluid that has no value like carrion and blood; and because this hiring is for impregnation, which is a matter of uncertainty, unknown.
Source pages p. 563

Commentary
This passage is an inter-madhhab dispute concerning the ruling on hiring a male goat for breeding. The commentator first defines 'casp al-tays' as giving a stallion for covering females, and explains the prohibition due to gharar (uncertainty) because fertilization is not guaranteed. This is the Hanafi position. The opposing view comes from Abu al-Khattab al-Hanbali and some Shafi'is, who analogize it to hiring a wet nurse, arguing it is a permissible beneficial contract. The Hanafi response is threefold: (1) a hadith from several authorities (Bukhari, Abu Dawud, Tirmidhi, Nasa'i) where the Prophet forbade 'casp al-tays'; (2) it is taking money for a despicable fluid like carrion or blood, which is unlawful; (3) the object (impregnation) is uncertain, making it gharar. Thus the Hanafi school maintains the prohibition.

Key Terms
عسب التيس (ʿasb al-tays): Hiring a male goat for breeding purposes; the fee for covering.
الغرر (al-gharar): Uncertainty in a contract; here, whether fertilization occurs is unknown.

Key Terms from Source Passage

B) The hadith forbidding 'casp al-tays'
C) Istihsan based on public need
D) Qiyas to hiring a wet nurse

Key Takeaway
Hiring a male goat for breeding is prohibited in the Hanafi school due to explicit hadith and the presence of gharar, regardless of opposing analogical arguments.

Fatwa Change on Hiring for Teaching Quran and Fiqh
Explanation of a fatwa change based on custom and istihsan

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi justification for the fatwa change regarding hiring for teaching Quran and fiqh, and identify the role of istihsan and urf in this change.

Core Idea
Fatwa can change when custom changes: hiring for teaching Quran was once invalid but is now valid to preserve the teaching.

In this passage from the hashia, we see a classic example of fatwa evolution in the Hanafi school. The early ruling prohibited hiring for teaching Quran and fiqh because people freely volunteered. When times changed, so did the fatwa. This lesson examines the reasoning behind this change, focusing on the principle of istihsan (juristic preference) and the role of changing custom (urf).

Guided Path
1
Identify the original ruling and its basis
The original Hanafi position was that hiring for teaching Quran and fiqh is invalid because teaching is an act of worship to be done for Allah's sake without payment.
This ruling was based on the principle that acts of worship should be ihtisaban (voluntarily seeking reward from Allah).
2
Understand the rationale for prohibition
Early scholars prohibited it because people in their time were willing to teach for free out of piety (ihtisaban) and would reward teachers spontaneously without condition.
The contract was seen as unnecessary because the teaching would happen anyway.
3
Recognize the change in circumstances
In later times, people stopped volunteering for free, and the practice of spontaneous reward ceased. If the contract remained invalid, teaching would be abandoned.
This change is a matter of urf (custom) which is a recognized source of law in the Hanafi school.
4
Apply the principle of istihsan
The later scholars applied istihsan (juristic preference) to permit the contract, because preventing harm (loss of teaching) outweighs the original reason for prohibition.
Istihsan allows deviation from qiyas (analogy) in favor of a more suitable ruling.
5
Note the authority level
This ruling is from the later fatwa (fatawa mutakhkhirin) and is the operative position (mufta bihi) today, overriding the earlier position in Zahir al-Riwayah.
The hashia states 'yufata al-yawm' indicating the current fatwa.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
[1] قوله : ويفتى اليوم بصحتها...الخ ; لأنَّ المتقدمين إن منعوا عنها لرغبة الناس في زمانهم في فعلها احتساباً، وفي مجازاة فاعلها بالإحسان بلا شرط ، وفي زماننا قد زال المعنيان، ففي عدم صحة الإجارة عليها تضييعها.
[1] His saying: 'And fatwa is given today on its validity... etc.'; because the early scholars prohibited it due to the desire of people in their time to do it voluntarily, and to reward the doer with goodness without condition; and in our time both reasons have ceased, so in not validating the hiring for it is a waste of it.
Source pages p. 564

Commentary
This is a critical refinement (hashiya) from the supercommentary explaining a fatwa change. The original ruling in the Hanafi school was that hiring for teaching Quran and fiqh was invalid, based on the principle that such acts of worship should be done for Allah's sake without payment. However, the early scholars prohibited the contract because people in their time were willing to teach for free out of piety and would reward teachers spontaneously. In later times, this voluntary practice ceased, and if the contract were not allowed, the teaching would be abandoned. Thus, applying istihsan (juristic preference) due to changed custom, the fatwa shifted to permit such hiring. This illustrates how Hanafi law adapts rulings based on changing circumstances while adhering to core principles.

Key Terms
يفتى اليوم (yufata al-yawm): The current operative fatwa, as opposed to the earlier ruling.
احتساباً (iḥtisāban): Doing something voluntarily seeking reward from Allah, without expecting payment.

Key Terms from Source Passage

C) Because the Quran explicitly forbids taking wages for teaching
D) Because it leads to pride and arrogance

Key Takeaway
Hanafi fatwa on hiring for Quran teaching changed from invalid to valid due to changing custom, applying istihsan to preserve the teaching.

Hiring for Teaching Quran: Original Prohibition and Istihsan Exception
Hanafi ruling on hiring for teaching with hadith proof and later istihsan

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the original Hanafi prohibition on hiring for teaching Quran and Fiqh, cite the hadith of 'asbu al-tays', and apply the istihsan exception to contemporary cases of religious education.

Core Idea
Hiring for teaching Quran was originally prohibited; later Hanafi jurists permitted it by istihsan to prevent loss of religious knowledge.

This passage from 'Umdat al-Ri'aya, a commentary on al-Wiqaya, addresses a critical shift in Hanafi fiqh: the permissibility of hiring teachers for Quran and Fiqh. While the school's foundation (zahir al-riwaya) forbids taking wages for acts of obedience, later scholars recognized a pressing necessity—laxity in religious commitment and the drying up of treasury stipends—and used istihsan (juristic preference) to allow it. This lesson unpacks the original ruling, its proof from the hadith prohibiting 'asbu al-tays' (stud fee), the inter-madhhab dispute, and the scope of the exception.

Guided Path
1
Identify the original Hanafi principle
State the school's default ruling: hiring for acts of obedience (e.g., teaching Quran, leading prayer) is not permissible because these are purely religious duties that should be performed voluntarily.
The ruling applies to acts specific to Islam; hiring for non-Islamic acts (e.g., teaching Torah by a dhimmi) is permissible by consensus.
2
Examine the primary dalil: hadith of 'asbu al-tays'
The Prophet (ﷺ) prohibited taking payment for the mating service of a he-goat. Hanafis extend this by qiyas (analogy) to hiring for teaching, arguing both involve uncertain benefits and lowly consideration.
This hadith is zanni al-thubut (single transmission) and zanni al-dalala (ambiguous meaning), allowing room for istihsan to override the analogy.
3
Understand the necessity that triggered istihsan
In later times, people became lax in religious duties, stipends from the public treasury ceased, and few volunteered to teach. To prevent the extinction of Quranic knowledge, scholars made an exception.
The key phrase is 'zahara al-tawani' (laxity appeared) and 'taharruzan 'an al-indirās' (precaution against extinction).
4
Define the scope of the exception
Al-Hidayah limited the exception to teaching Quran; later authorities extended it to teaching Fiqh, imamah, adhan, iqamah, and wa'z (preaching), but only where there is manifest necessity.
The exception does not cover all acts of obedience—only those essential for preserving religion.
5
Analyze the inter-madhhab dispute
Some Hanbali and Shafi'i scholars analogize hiring a teacher to hiring a wet nurse (ijarat al-za'ir), which is permissible. The Hanafi response distinguishes: teaching is a religious duty, while nursing is a physical need; also, the hadith prohibits uncertain benefits.
The practical difference (thamarah al-khilaf) is that Hanafis originally prohibit, while others permit outright.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

[1] قوله : على الطاعات ؛ أي المختصة بملة الإسلام ، أما إذا كانت غير مختصة بها فيجوز الإجارة عليها بالاتفاق ، كما إذا استأجر ذميّاً على تعليم التوراة فالاستئجار جائز لعدم اختصاص تعليهما بملة الإسلام، كما صرح به الفقهاء الكرام. 
[2] قوله : يفتى بصحتها ... الخ ؛ قال في «الهداية» : وبعض مشايخنا استحسنوا الاستئجار على تعليم القرآن اليوم ؛ لأنه ظهر التواني في الأمور الدينية، ففي الامتناع يضيعُ حفظ القرآن، وعليه الفتوى. انتهى.
وفي «النهاية»: يفتى بجواز الاستئجار على تعليم الفقه أيضاً في زماننا. انتهى. وفي «المجمع»: وقيل : يفتى بجوازِهِ على التعليم والإمامة والفقه. انتهى. فقد اقتصر صاحب الهداية» على استثناء تعليم القرآن، وزاد بعضهم الإمامة والأذان، وبعضهم الإقامة والوعظ والتدريس.
وقد اتفقت كلمتهم على التعليم بالضرورة، وعلى التصريح بأصل المذهب، وهو عدم الجواز، فهذا دليل على أن المفتي به ليس هو جواز الاستئجار على كل طاعة، بل على ما ذكروه فقط مما فيه ضرورة ظاهرة تبيح الخروج عن أصل المذهب من طرق المنع ، فتذكر .
[3] قوله : تحرزاً عن الاندراس ؛ فإنّ العطيات قد انقطعت من بيت المال، وقلّما يعلم حسبة، ولا يتفرغون للتعليم أيضاً ، فإنّ حاجتهم تمنعهم من ذلك، فأفتوا بالجواز ورأوه حسناً.
And today a fatwa is given on its validity for teaching Quran and Fiqh. ... And the principle with us is that hiring for acts of obedience and disobedience is not permissible. But when laxity occurred in religious matters, a fatwa is given on its validity for teaching Quran and Fiqh as a precaution against extinction. [1] He said: Regarding acts of obedience, meaning those specific to the religion of Islam. As for those not specific to it, hiring for them is permissible by consensus, such as when a dhimmi is hired to teach the Torah, the hire is permissible because his teaching is not specific to the religion of Islam, as the noble jurists have stated. [2] He said: A fatwa is given on its validity... He said in al-Hidayah: Some of our mashayikh approved hiring for teaching Quran today because lethargy has appeared in religious matters, and in refusal, the memorization of the Quran would be lost, and upon it is the fatwa. End. And in al-Nihayah: A fatwa is given on the permissibility of hiring for teaching Fiqh also in our time. End. And in al-Mujma': And it is said: A fatwa is given on its permissibility for teaching, imamah, and Fiqh. End. Thus the author of al-Hidayah limited the exception to teaching Quran, and some added imamah and adhan, and some added iqamah, wa'z, and teaching. And they all agreed on teaching by necessity, and on stating the original school position, which is impermissibility. This is evidence that the fatwa position is not the permissibility of hiring for every obedience, but only for what they mentioned, which involves a manifest necessity that permits departing from the original school by way of prevention, so remember. [3] He said: As a precaution against extinction. For the stipends have been cut off from the treasury, and rarely does anyone do it voluntarily, nor do they have leisure for teaching, because their need prevents them from that. So they gave a fatwa of permissibility and considered it good.
Source pages p. 564

Commentary
This passage from the commentary on al-Wiqayah discusses the Hanafi ruling on hiring for teaching Quran and Fiqh. The original principle in the Hanafi school is that hiring for acts of obedience (such as teaching Quran, leading prayer, etc.) is not permissible because it involves taking wages for a purely religious duty that should be performed voluntarily. However, due to changing circumstances—specifically, laxity in religious commitment and the cessation of stipends from the public treasury—later Hanafi scholars (mutakhkhirin) made an exception by istihsan (juristic preference) to allow hiring for teaching Quran and Fiqh to prevent the loss of these sciences. The passage also clarifies that this exception is limited to cases of necessity and does not extend to all acts of obedience. The text includes a comparison with the inter-madhhab dispute regarding the prohibition of stud fee (عسب التيس), citing a hadith to support the original prohibition. The Hanafi response to opponents (like some Hanbalis and Shafi'is) is that the prohibition is due to the uncertainty of the benefit (impregnation) and the lowliness of the consideration (semen).

Key Terms
عسب التيس (asbu al-tays): The stud fee paid for the service of a he-goat to mate with a female goat.
استحسان (istihsan): Juristic preference that allows departing from an established analogy (qiyas) in favor of a more equitable ruling due to necessity or custom.
إجارة (ijarah): A contract of hiring or leasing, where one party provides a benefit in exchange for compensation.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Permissible by consensus
B) Not permissible, but later permitted by istihsan due to necessity
C) Permissible only for teaching Fiqh
D) Prohibited for everyone

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school originally prohibits hiring for teaching Quran, but permits it by istihsan due to necessity; the fatwa today allows it for essential religious education.

Hiring for Teaching Quran: Original Ruling and Later Fatwa
Discusses invalid hire for worship and current fatwa allowing hire for Quran teaching

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the original Hanafi ruling on hiring for teaching Quran and explain the later concession (fatwa) based on necessity (istihsan).

Core Idea
Original Hanafi ruling: hiring for teaching Quran is impermissible; later fatwa permits it due to necessity to prevent loss of Quranic knowledge.

This passage addresses a classic Hanafi ruling: hiring a person to teach the Quran is generally invalid because teaching acts of worship should be done voluntarily. However, over time, circumstances changed: people became lax, voluntary teaching declined, and the religious knowledge faced extinction. To preserve the Quran and Fiqh, later Hanafi masters used istihsan (juristic preference) to permit hiring for teaching, based on necessity. This lesson examines the original ruling, the reasons for the shift, and the limits of the concession.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and original ruling
The act is hiring (ijarah) for teaching the Quran or other acts of worship. The original ruling (asl al-madhhab) is impermissibility (adam al-jawaz) according to the zahir al-riwayah.
The original ruling applies to all acts of worship specific to Islam.
2
Understand the reason for original prohibition
Teaching the Quran is itself an act of worship (ta'ah). In early Islam, those who memorized the Quran were few, so teaching it was wajib (obligatory) on them; accepting payment for an obligatory act was seen as inappropriate.
The principle: one should not be paid for performing an obligation.
3
Recognize the change in circumstances
Over time, lethargy (al-tawani) appeared in religious matters. The number of voluntary teachers decreased, and stipends from the treasury (bayt al-mal) ceased. This created a genuine risk that Quranic knowledge would be lost (al-indiras).
Necessity (darurah) is the key trigger for the concession.
4
Apply istihsan to derive the concession
Later scholars (e.g., in al-Hidayah) used istihsan to depart from the original prohibition. They ruled that hiring for teaching Quran is permitted today because preventing the loss of Quran is a higher interest. This became the relied-upon fatwa (mufta bihi).
Istihsan overrides qiyas (original analogy) in Hanafi usul.
5
Note the limits of the concession
The fatwa is limited to cases of manifest necessity. Some scholars restrict it to teaching Quran; others extend it to teaching Fiqh, leading prayer (imamah), adhan, etc. The concession does not apply to all acts of worship.
The original ruling remains authoritative for non-essential acts.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

Book of Ijarah: Chapter on Invalid Ijarah for Acts of Worship and Sins. But when lethargy occurred in religious matters, fatwa is given for its validity for teaching Quran and Fiqh to guard against extinction. [1] His statement: 'for acts of worship'; i.e., those specific to the religion of Islam. As for that which is not specific to it, then ijarah is permissible by agreement, such as if one hires a dhimmi to teach the Torah, the hire is permissible because its teaching is not specific to the religion of Islam, as the noble jurists have stated. [2] His statement: 'fatwa is given for its validity... etc.'; He said in al-Hidayah: 'Some of our shaykhs deemed it good (istihsan) to hire for teaching Quran today because lethargy has appeared in religious matters, and refusal would cause loss of Quran memorization, and the fatwa is upon it.' End. In al-Nihayah: 'Fatwa is given for the permissibility of hiring for teaching Fiqh also in our time.' End. In al-Majma': 'It is said: fatwa is given for its permissibility for teaching, imamah, and Fiqh.' End. Thus the author of al-Hidayah confined the exception to teaching Quran, and some added imamah and adhan, and some added iqamah, preaching, and teaching. And they all agreed on teaching out of necessity, and on stating the original madhhab, which is impermissibility. This indicates that what is given fatwa upon is not the permissibility of hiring for every act of worship, but only for what they mentioned in which there is manifest necessity permitting departure from the original madhhab from the routes of prohibition, so remember. [3] His statement: 'to guard against extinction'; indeed, stipends have ceased from the treasury, and rarely does one teach voluntarily, nor do they have free time for teaching because their need prevents them from that, so they gave fatwa of permissibility and deemed it good. (1) Some shaykhs deemed it good to hire for teaching Quran today due to the appearance of lethargy in religious matters, so refusal would lead to loss of Quran memorization, and the fatwa is upon it, and its completion is in 'Ihsan al-Istijar ala Ta'lim al-Quran' (p. 227). They said: The teaching of Quran for a fee was disliked in the early period because the carriers of Quran were few, so teaching was obligatory so that the Quran would not be lost. But in our time, carriers of Quran are many, and teaching is no longer obligatory, so hiring for it is permissible. See: al-Muhit (p. 151). (2) al-Hidayah (3:240). (3) See: Radd al-Muhtar (5:34-35).
Source pages p. 565

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof concerning the validity of hiring for acts of worship, specifically discussing the Hanafi position on hiring for teaching Quran and Fiqh. The author begins by stating the general rule: ijarah (hire) for acts of worship (ta'at) that are specific to Islam is invalid, while hiring for acts not specific to Islam, like teaching the Torah to a dhimmi, is permissible by consensus. The key issue is the concession (istihsan) made by later Hanafi scholars regarding hiring for teaching Quran and Fiqh due to changed circumstances. The text quotes al-Hidayah, al-Nihayah, and al-Majma' to show the development: originally, the madhhab ruled that hiring for teaching Quran is not allowed because teaching was an obligation (wajib) on those qualified. However, when Muslims became lax and voluntary teaching declined, scholars feared the loss of Quranic knowledge, so they permitted hiring for it as a necessity. Some extended this to teaching Fiqh, imamah, adhan, etc., but they all agreed that this concession is limited to cases of manifest necessity and does not overturn the original prohibition for other acts of worship. The commentary then explains that the reason for the concession is the discontinuation of stipends from the treasury (bayt al-mal) and the lack of volunteers. The footnote elaborates on the istihsan reasoning: in the early period, Quran carriers were few, making teaching obligatory; later, when carriers increased, the obligation lifted, making hire permissible. This shows the Hanafi principle that legal rulings can change with time and necessity.

Key Terms
الاستحسان (istihsan): A method of reasoning in Hanafi usul al-fiqh where a scholar departs from the obvious analogy (qiyas) in favor of a stronger evidence or public interest.
الفتوى (fatwa): The formal legal opinion given in response to a query, often reflecting the relied-upon position in the madhhab.
الاندراس (al-indiras): Extinction or disappearance, here referring to the potential loss of Quranic and Fiqh knowledge if not taught.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, why did later Hanafi scholars permit hiring for teaching Quran?
A) Because teaching Quran is a recommended act and hiring is always permissible for recommended acts.
B) Because the early prohibition was abrogated by a later Quranic verse.
C) Because necessity arose due to laziness in religious matters and fear of Quran being lost.
D) Because the Sahibayn convinced Abu Hanifa to change his ruling.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school permits hiring for teaching Quran and Fiqh as a necessity-based concession (istihsan), without overturning the original ruling of impermissibility for other acts of worship.

Ijarah — Hire and Lease

Compelling Payment of Wage and Customary Gift (Halwah)
Ruling on compelling payment of wage and halwah.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the obligation of the hirer to pay the agreed wage and customary gift (halwah) and identify when the hirer can be compelled or imprisoned for non-payment.

Core Idea
A hirer must pay the agreed wage and any customary gift; non-payment allows compulsion and imprisonment.

This passage from 'Umdat al-Ri'ayah addresses a practical issue in ijarah: when a hirer fails to pay the agreed wage, the law compels payment and even imprisonment. Additionally, customary gifts like halwah given to teachers are also enforceable. Understanding these obligations is essential for both parties in a hire contract.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What is the ruling? The hirer is compelled (yujbar) to pay the agreed wage and is imprisoned for non-payment. This indicates an obligation (wujub).
2
Extend to customary gift
The same compulsion applies to the customary gift (halwah al-marsumah). Halwah is a gift given to teachers upon completing sections of the Quran, named after sweets (halawi) customarily given.
Halwah is a term from Transoxiana; other regions have similar customs like saraafah in Egypt.
3
Note the legal basis
The wage is obligated by contract, the halwah by established custom ('urf). Hanafi law enforces both.
Custom must be 'marsumah' (established) to be binding.
4
Consider the practical scope
The hirer is compelled whether he is the actual user or his guardian (if minor).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

(ولا إجارة المشاع الإ من الشريك) ، هذا عند أبي حنيفة له وقالوا : الأحكام تختلف باختلاف الزمان ألا ترى أن النساء كن يخرجن إلى الجماعة في زمان الرسول الله فكان ذلك إلى زمان الصديق الأكبر له، حتى منعهم الفاروق الأعظم الله وفق اقتضاء المصالح، وكان ذلك هو الصواب، كما لا يخفى على أولي الباب. [1] قوله : ويجبر ...الخ ؛ أي ويجبر المستأجر سواء كان الصبي أو وليه على دفع ما سماه من الأجر، ويحبس المستأجر بالأجر الذي سماه ، ويجبر على دفع الحلوة المرسومة. [٢] قوله : لأن العادة...الخ ؛ لعلها كانت وبانت، أو هي في بعض البلاد، وقال في «المنح»: وهي المسماة في عرف ديارنا بالصرافة، فإنّ المؤدب يوم يأخذها يصرفُ المتعلمين من عنده في أول النهار، فيفرحون بذلك اليوم رغبة في الراحة والبطالة. انتهى. وهذا غير ما اصطلح عليه أهل مصر، فإنّ الصرافة عندهم تكون إذ ختم الصبي القرآن. ذكره العلامة الطحطاوي (١). [٣] قوله : ولا إجارة المشاع ؛ أي ولا تصح إجارة المشاع سواء كان الشيوع فيما يحتمل القسمة كالعروض، أو فيما لا يحتملها كالعبد، والمراد من الشيوع هو الشيوع الأصلي ؛ لأنّ الطارئ لا يفسد الإجارة في ظاهر الرواية عند الإمام، وفي رواية عنه يفسدها أيضاً. [٤] قوله : إلا من الشريك ; فإنّه يجوز مشاعاً بالإجماع في ظاهر الرواية عـن الإمام ؛ لأنَّ الكل مجتمع على ملكه فلا يلزم الشيوع ، وعنه لا يجوز أيضاً، ثم اختلف (۱) في حاشيته» (٤ : ٣٠).
(And the hirer is compelled to pay what was agreed, and is imprisoned for it, and also for the customary gift (halwah).) Al-halwah - with the vowel fatha on the unpointed ha - is a gift given to teachers upon certain sections of the Quran; it is named thus because the custom is to give sweets (halawi), and it is a term used by the people of Transoxiana. (And there is no ijarah of joint property (musha') except from a co-owner.) This is according to Abu Hanifa. They said: Rulings differ with difference of time. Do you not see that women used to go out for congregational prayer in the time of the Messenger of Allah, and that continued until the time of Abu Bakr al-Siddiq, until Umar al-Faruq prevented them from that due to the requirements of public interest, and that was correct, as is not hidden from people of understanding. [1] His statement: 'And is compelled... etc.'; i.e., the hirer is compelled whether he is a minor or his guardian to pay the wage he specified, and the hirer is imprisoned for the wage he specified, and he is compelled to pay the customary halwah. [2] His statement: 'Because the custom... etc.'; Perhaps it was and became clear, or it is in some lands. He said in al-Minh: 'It is what is called in the custom of our lands as saraafah; indeed, the teacher when he takes it dismisses the students from him early in the morning, and they rejoice on that day desiring rest and idleness.' End. This is different from what the people of Egypt have convention upon, for saraafah with them is when the child finishes the Quran. Mentioned by al-Allamah al-Tahtawi. [3] His statement: 'And there is no ijarah of musha''; i.e., ijarah of musha' is not valid whether the joint ownership is in something divisible like commodities, or in something indivisible like a slave; and the intended meaning of musha' is original joint ownership, because incidental joint ownership does not invalidate the ijarah in the apparent narration from the Imam, and in one narration from him it also invalidates. [4] His statement: 'except from a co-owner'; for it is permitted as musha' by consensus in the apparent narration from the Imam because the entirety is united in his ownership so no joint ownership occurs; and from him it is also not permitted, then they differed. (1) In his Hashiyah (4:30).
Source pages p. 566

Commentary
This passage is a ruling statement with expansion. It covers two distinct legal issues: (1) the hirer's obligation to pay the agreed wage and the customary gift (halwah), and (2) the invalidity of leasing jointly owned property (musha') except to a co-owner. The text first states the ruling that the hirer is compelled to pay the agreed wage and is imprisoned if he does not; additionally, he must pay the halwah, which is a customary gift given to teachers upon completing certain portions of the Quran. The commentary explains that halwah is a term from Transoxiana referring to sweets given as gifts. It distinguishes between the practice in some lands (like Egypt) where a similar gift called saraafah is given upon completion of the entire Quran. The second ruling is that leasing joint property (such as a share of a commodity or a slave) is invalid except when the lessee is a co-owner (sharik). This is the position of Abu Hanifa as per the apparent narration (zahir al-riwayah). The reasoning is that when a co-owner leases his share to another co-owner, the property remains under collective ownership, so the problem of joint ownership is not present. Some narrations from Abu Hanifa even hold that incidental joint ownership (after the contract) does not invalidate ijarah. The commentary also mentions that rulings can change with time, citing the example of women attending congregational prayers: allowed initially but later prohibited by Umar due to changing public interest. This underscores the dynamic nature of fiqh.

Key Terms
الحَلْوَة (al-halwah): A customary gift given to teachers upon completing sections of the Quran; named after sweets (halawi) typically given.
الصرافة (al-saraafah): In Egyptian custom, a gift given to the teacher when a child completes the entire Quran; distinct from halwah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the ruling on the hirer's obligation to pay a customary gift (halwah) in Hanafi fiqh?
A) It is recommended but not enforceable.
B) It is obligatory and the hirer is compelled to pay.
C) It is only obligatory if in writing.
D) It is prohibited to demand it.

Key Takeaway
A hirer must pay both the agreed wage and any customary gift like halwah; non-payment can lead to compulsion and imprisonment.

Ijarah — Hire and Lease

The Ruling on Leasing Joint Property (Musha')
Ruling on leasing joint property (musha').

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on leasing undivided joint property (musha') and identify the exception for leasing to a co-owner.

Core Idea
Leasing an undivided share of joint property is invalid except when the lessee is a co-owner.

This passage addresses a key principle in ijarah: the lease of an undivided share (musha') is generally invalid. However, there is an important exception when the lessee is already a co-owner. Understanding this ruling helps avoid invalid contracts and clarifies the role of possession in ijarah.

Guided Path
1
Identify the general ruling
Ijarah of musha' (undivided joint property) is invalid. The text says 'la ijarah al-musha' (there is no ijarah of musha').
2
Understand the exception
Except when the lessee is a co-owner (sharik). Then it is valid by consensus in the apparent narration.
Because the property remains in the hands of co-owners, possession is not an issue.
3
Explore the reason
In a lease, the lessor must deliver exclusive possession of the leased item. An undivided share cannot be exclusively possessed by a stranger; but a co-owner already shares possession.
4
Note intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf
There is a narration from Abu Hanifa that incidental joint ownership (after contract) also invalidates the lease. But the apparent narration says incidental does not invalidate.
Similarly, some narrations say even leasing to a co-owner is not allowed, but the relied-upon position is that it is allowed.
5
Observe the principle of changing rulings
The passage mentions that rulings can change with time, citing the example of women attending congregational prayers.
This underscores the dynamic nature of fiqh.

It distinguishes between the practice in some lands (like Egypt) where a similar gift called saraafah is given upon completion of the entire Quran. The second ruling is that leasing joint property (such as a share of a commodity or a slave) is invalid except when the lessee is a co-owner (sharik). This is the position of Abu Hanifa as per the apparent narration (zahir al-riwayah). The reasoning is that when a co-owner leases his share to another co-owner, the property remains under collective ownership, so the problem of joint ownership is not present. Some narrations from Abu Hanifa even hold that incidental joint ownership (after the contract) does not invalidate ijarah. The commentary also mentions that rulings can change with time, citing the example of women attending congregational prayers: allowed initially but later prohibited by Umar due to changing public interest. This underscores the dynamic nature of fiqh.

Key Terms
المشاع (al-musha'): Jointly owned or undivided property; a share of a common property that is not physically partitioned.
الشريك (al-sharik): Co-owner; a partner in the joint property.
الشيوع الأصلي (al-shuyu' al-asli): Original joint ownership; the state of being jointly owned at the time of the contract.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Under what circumstance does Abu Hanifa permit leasing of joint property (musha')?
A) When the property is divisible.
B) When the lessee is a co-owner (sharik).
C) When the lease is for a short period.
D) When the property is an immovable.

Key Takeaway
Leasing an undivided share of joint property is invalid except to a co-owner; this is due to the impossibility of delivering exclusive possession.

Compulsory Payment of Rent and Customary Halwa
Ruling on compulsory payment of rental wage and customary halwa

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling that a lessee is compelled to pay both the agreed wage and the customary halwa, and explain that non-payment may lead to imprisonment.

Core Idea
A lessee must pay both the agreed wage and the customary halwa; the law compels payment and may imprison for default.

This passage from 'Umdat al-Ri'aya addresses the enforcement of rental obligations. It clarifies that beyond the fixed wage, customary gifts like halwa are also legally binding if they are established by custom. The commentary connects this to the broader principle that rulings adapt to custom and time, using the example of women's mosque attendance.

Guided Path
1
Identify the parties and the obligation
Determine who the lessee (musta'jir) is and what he is required to pay: the specified wage and any customary halwa.
The lessee may be an adult or minor (guardian pays for minor).
2
Distinguish between fixed wage and custom-based halwa
Note that the wage is agreed in the contract, while halwa is a customary gift not originally stipulated. Both are enforceable.
Halwa means sweets, but it refers to any customary gift to teachers.
3
Understand the enforcement mechanism
The text states the lessee can be imprisoned for non-payment of both wage and halwa.
Imprisonment is a coercive measure, not a punishment for debt.
4
Observe the commentary on changing customs
The commentator uses the example of Umar banning women from mosques to illustrate that rulings can change with time and custom.
This supports the enforcement of halwa as a current custom.

Commentary
This passage begins by stating a ruling: the lessee (mu'ajjir) is compelled to pay the wage he agreed upon, and he can be imprisoned for non-payment. The passage ends with a commentary on the custom of halwa, noting regional variations—in some lands it is a day off for students, while in Egypt it refers to a celebration upon completing the Quran. This is a pure ruling statement with no proof cited; the commentary merely expands on the meaning.

Leasing Shared Property (Musha') – Intra-Hanafi Dispute
Intra-Hanafi dispute on validity of leasing undivided shares

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the positions of Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn on leasing musha', identify the key proof (taslim), and explain why the relied-upon view is fasid.

Core Idea
Leasing an undivided share is invalid unless its benefit can be exclusively delivered – a dispute over delivery of the non-deliverable.

This lesson examines a classic intra-Hanafi dispute: can you lease an undivided share (musha') in a property to someone who is not a co-owner? Abu Hanifa says no – because you cannot deliver a share you cannot specify. Abu Yusuf and Muhammad say yes – because vacating (takhliyah) or mutual division (tahayu') can make delivery possible. The passage you'll read lays out Abu Hanifa's proof and his rebuttals to the Sahibayn's arguments. Understanding this dispute will sharpen your ability to analyse contractual validity debates within the school.

Guided Path
1
State the two Hanafi positions
Identify Abu Hanifa's ruling (invalid except to a partner) and the Sahibayn's ruling (valid to anyone). Note that the disagreement is about the lessee being a non-partner.
2
Analyse Abu Hanifa's central proof
Abu Hanifa argues that leasing requires delivery (taslim) of the leased item, but a musha' share cannot be physically delivered because possession (qabd) requires a specified object (mu'ayyan). A musha' share is unspecified.
This is a classic example of a hukm based on impossibility of delivery.
3
Examine the Sahibayn's counter-proofs and Abu Hanifa's responses
The Sahibayn claim delivery is possible via takhliyah (vacating) or tahayu' (mutual division). Abu Hanifa rebuts: takhliyah does not actually enable benefit unless benefit occurs, and tahayu' is a post-contract arrangement that cannot retroactively validate the contract.
4
Evaluate the qiyas (analogy) to leasing to a partner
The Sahibayn analogise to leasing from a partner, where the lease is valid. Abu Hanifa distinguishes: in that case, the lessee already possesses his share, so the newly arising benefits are exclusively owned by him – no sharing issue.
This is a tanqih al-manat: the illa is exclusive benefit, not mere delivery.
5
Determine the mufta bihi (operative ruling)
Later scholars combined the views: the contract is not batil (void) but fasid (defective), requiring ujr al-mithl (like wage). This is the relied-upon position.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(ولا إجارة المشاع الإ من الشريك) ، هذا عند أبي حنيفة له ... (وقالا : تصح إجارة المشاع من الشريك ومن غيره). ... ولأبي حنيفة : إنّ هذا إجارة ما لا يقدر على تسليمه، فإن تسليم المشاع وحده غير متصوّر ؛ لأن التسليم إنّما يتم بالقبض، والقبض أمر حسي، وهو لا يرد إلا على المعين، والمشاع غير معين، وما لا يتصوّر تسليمه لا يصح إجارتُه لعدم الانتفاع به، والإجارة عقد على المنفعة. والجواب عن إمكان التسليم بالتخلية : إنّ التخلية اعتبرت تسليماً إذا كان تمكيناً من الانتفاع ، وإنما يكون تمكيناً إذا حصل، أما التمكن وهو غير حاصل بها ، فلم يعتبر فعله تمكيناً بخلاف البيع، فإنَّ التمكن من البيع والإعتاق وغير ذلك حاصل فيه. والجواب عن إمكان التسليم بالتهايؤ : إنّ التهايؤ من أحكام العقد بواسطة الملك، فهو متأخر عن العقد الموجب للملك، وهو منتف، والانتفاع شرطه، وهو القدرة على التسليم ، ولا يمكن إثباته بالتهايؤ ؛ لأنه لا يمكن أن يكون ثبوت الشيء مما يتأخر عنه ثبوتاً. والجواب عن قياسهما على ما إذا اجر من شريكه، فهو أنَّ جملة المنافع حادثة حينئذ على ملكه ، فإنَّ البعض له بحكم الملك، والبعض له بحكم الإجارة فلا شيوع.
(And the leasing of shared property is not valid except from a partner), this according to Abu Hanifa... (And they two said: The leasing of shared property is valid from a partner and from others). ... And for Abu Hanifa: This is a lease of something that cannot be delivered, because delivery of the shared part alone is inconceivable; for delivery is only complete by taking possession (qabd), and possession is a sensory matter that applies only to specified things, and a shared share is unspecified. That which cannot be delivered cannot be validly leased because one cannot benefit from it, and leasing is a contract for benefit. The response to the possibility of delivery by vacating (takhliyah) is that vacating is considered delivery if it enables benefit, but it is only enabling if benefit actually occurs; mere potential is not considered enabling, unlike sale, where potential for transfer, manumission, etc. is present. The response to the possibility of delivery by mutual division (tahayu') is that mutual division is a consequence of the contract via ownership; it is subsequent to the contract that establishes ownership, and such ownership is absent here. Benefit requires the ability to deliver, and this cannot be established by mutual division because something cannot be established by what comes after it. The response to their analogy to the case where one leases from his partner is that in that case all the newly arising benefits belong to him by ownership in part and by lease in part, so there is no sharing.
Source pages p. 566

Commentary
This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the validity of leasing undivided shares (musha') in property. Abu Hanifa holds that leasing musha' is invalid except when the lessee is a co-owner (sharik). Abu Yusuf and Muhammad (the Sahibayn) hold that it is valid even to a non-partner. The passage then details Abu Hanifa's proof: leasing requires the ability to deliver the property, but a musha' share cannot be physically delivered because possession (qabd) requires a specific, identified object. Mere vacating (takhliyah) of the property by the lessor does not enable benefit because the lessee cannot exclusively use the share. Similarly, mutual division (tahayu') is a subsequent arrangement that cannot retroactively validate the contract. The Sahibayn respond that delivery is possible through vacating or mutual division, and analogize to leasing from a partner where the share is effectively delivered. Abu Hanifa rebuts these analogies. The commentary explains that the relied-upon position (mufta bihi) is that the contract is valid but fasid (defective), requiring payment of the like wage (ujr al-mithl).

Key Terms
مشاع (musha'): An undivided share in a property held in common.
تخلية (takhliyah): Vacating the property by the lessor to enable the lessee's possession.
تهايؤ (tahayu'): Mutual division or arrangement among co-owners to allocate use.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is Abu Hanifa's main reason for invalidating the lease of musha' to a non-partner?
A) The rent is unknown (gharar)
B) Delivery (taslim) is impossible because the share is unspecified
C) The co-owner must consent
D) Leasing benefits that are not yet created

Key Takeaway
Leasing an undivided share to a non-partner is invalid according to Abu Hanifa because delivery is impossible; the later relied-upon view rules it fasid (defective), requiring the lessee to pay ujr al-mithl.

Dispute on Hiring Undivided Property (Ijārat al-Mushā‘)
Debate on hiring undivided property (musha‘)

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi positions on hiring undivided property, explain the proofs of Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn, and apply the mufta bihi ruling with the given legal stratagem.

Core Idea
Hiring undivided property: Sahibayn validate it; Abu Hanifa invalidates it; fatwa follows Sahibayn.

This lesson examines an important intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the validity of hiring out undivided property (musha‘). While Imam Abu Hanifa holds that such a contract cannot be valid due to the impossibility of delivery, his two disciples, Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani (the Sahibayn), argue that benefit exists and delivery can be effected either by vacating (takhliya) or by mutual division (tihayi‘). The text presents both arguments in detail and concludes that the relied-upon fatwa is with the Sahibayn, even including a legal stratagem (hila) for those who wish to follow Imam Abu Hanifa.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Two Positions
State the ruling of Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn on hiring undivided property. Determine the thamarah al-khilaf: what changes in outcome between the two views.
Abu Hanifa: invalid (either void or corrupt). Sahibayn: valid with full agreed wage.
2
Understand the Sahibayn’s Proof
Follow their reasoning: undivided property has benefit; delivery is possible via takhliya or tihayi‘; analogies to hiring from a partner or from two persons. Identify the key qiyas they use.
The principle is that hire is a contract on benefit, and benefit exists in musha‘.
3
Analyse Abu Hanifa’s Objection and Rebuttal
Abu Hanifa argues that delivery of undivided property is impossible because qabd (taking possession) requires specificity. Then examine his responses to the Sahibayn’s points: takhliya does not create tamakkun (actual ability), tihayi‘ is a post-contract consequence, and the analogies are distinguishable.
Pay attention to the distinction between tamkin and tamakkun.
4
Determine the Mufta Bihi and the Hila
Identify that the fatwa is according to the Sahibayn, as transmitted from al-Mughni. Then explain the hila: take the contract before a judge, or if impossible, rescind part of it to eliminate undividedness.
The hila allows permissibility according to all views.

فاسداً حتى يجب أجر المثل، وهو الصحيح. كذا في «مجمع الأنهر».

فعله تمكيناً بخلاف البيع، فإنَّ التمكن من البيع والإعتاق وغير ذلك حاصل فيه. والجواب عن إمكان التسليم بالتهايؤ : إنّ التهايؤ من أحكام العقد بواسطة الملك، فهو متأخر عن العقد الموجب للملك، وهو منتف، والانتفاع شرطه، وهو القدرة على التسليم ، ولا يمكن إثباته بالتهايؤ ؛ لأنه لا يمكن أن يكون ثبوت الشيء مما يتأخر عنه ثبوتاً. والجواب عن قياسهما على ما إذا اجر من شريكه، فهو أنَّ جملة المنافع حادثة حينئذ على ملكه ، فإنَّ البعض له بحكم الملك، والبعض له بحكم الإجارة فلا شيوع.  زبدة النهاية لعمدة الرعاية
ولو دفع إلى آخر غزلاً لينسجه بنصفه، أو استأجر حماراً يحمل عليه زاداً (ولو دفع إلى آخر غزلاً لينسجه بنصفه ، أو استأجر حماراً يحمل عليه زاداً فإن قيل : سلمنا أنّ جملة المنافع حادثة على ملكه، لكن مع اختلاف النسبة ؛ لأن الشريك منتفع بنصيبه بنسبة الملك ، وبنصيب شريكه بالاستئجار، فالشيوع موجود. أجيب : بأن الاختلاف في النسبة غير مضر ؛ لأنه لا عبرة لاختلاف الأسباب مع
اتحاد الحكم. وأما الجواب عن قياسهما على ما إذا أجر من رجلين : فهو أنَّ التسليم يقعُ جملة ؛ لأن العقد أضيف إلى كلّ الدار ، ثم الشيوع بتفرق الملك فيما بينهما طارئ ، وتوضيحه : إنَّ تسليم المعقود عليه كما أوجبه العقد مقدور عليه للمؤاجر، ثم المهاياة ذلك يكون بين المستأجرين بحكم ملكهما ، وهو نظير الرهن من رجلين فهو جائز ؛ لوجود المعقود عليه. كذا في شروح «الهداية)) ومع ذلك ذكر العيني (۳) ، والشمني (۳) ، وغيرهما نقلاً عن «المغني»: إن الفتوى في
إجارة المشاع على قولهما. انتهى. والحيلة في جوازها على قول الكلِّ أن يرفع العقد إلى قاض يحكم به، فإن تعذر الرفع لفقدان الإجارة في الكلّ، ثم يفسخان العقد في بعضه بقدر ما يتفقان عليه ؛ لأنّ الشيوع الطارئ لا يمنعُ الجواز بالاتفاق في ظاهر الرواية. كما ذكرنا.
And they (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) said: The hire of undivided property is valid from the partner and from others. The later scholars (mashayikh) follow the saying of Imam (Abu Hanifa). Some said: It does not conclude at all, so no hire is due. Others said: It concludes corruptly, so the equivalent hire is due, and that is correct. Thus in Majma' al-Anhur. [Commentary]: His saying: 'And they said: The hire of undivided property is valid from the partner and from others' — because undivided property has a benefit; do you not see that equivalent hire becomes obligatory according to Imam if the tenant is lodged therein? This indicates that undivided property has a benefit; otherwise nothing would be obligatory. The basis of hire is benefit, so it is permissible. If it is said: This is a hire that cannot be delivered, how is it valid? The answer: Delivery is possible by vacating (takhliya) or by division (tihayi'). As for vacating: the partner-lessor removes his belongings from the house and leaves it to the tenant. As for division: they agree on a matter and are content with it. Since benefit of undivided property is established and delivery is possible, it becomes like the case where one hires from his partner or from two persons, and that is permissible. So too this, and it becomes like sale. According to Abu Hanifa: This is a hire of something that cannot be delivered, for delivery of undivided property alone is inconceivable because delivery is completed by taking possession, and taking possession is a sensory matter, and it only applies to specified property, whereas undivided property is unspecified. Whatever cannot be delivered cannot be validly hired due to lack of benefit, and hire is a contract for benefit. The answer regarding the possibility of delivery by vacating: Vacating is considered delivery if it enables benefit. It only becomes enabling if actual ability is attained, but ability (tamakkun) is not attained by this, so his act is not considered enabling, unlike sale where ability for sale, manumission, etc. is present. The answer about delivery by division: Division is among the consequences of the contract through ownership; it is subsequent to the contract that establishes ownership, and is absent. Benefit requires ability to deliver, and it cannot be established by division because something cannot be established by something that comes after it. The answer to their analogy of hiring from his partner: In that case all benefits arise at that time on his ownership; part is by ownership, part by hire, so no undividedness. Then if it is said: We grant that all benefits arise on his ownership, but with differing proportion because the partner benefits from his share proportionally to ownership and from his partner's share by hire, so undividedness exists. Answer: The difference in proportion is harmless because differing causes with a single ruling are disregarded. As for the answer to their analogy of hiring from two persons: Delivery takes place as a whole because the contract pertains to the entire house; then the undividedness due to division of ownership between them is incidental. Explanation: Delivery of the contracted object as required by the contract is within the lessor's ability; then the division (muhaya) takes place between the lessees by virtue of their ownership, akin to a pledge from two persons—it is valid due to the existence of the contracted object. Thus in the commentaries of al-Hidayah. Nevertheless, al-Ayni, al-Shumnuni, and others transmitted from al-Mughni that the fatwa on hire of undivided property is according to their saying. The stratagem (hila) for its permissibility according to all sayings is to bring the contract before a judge who rules on it. If that is not possible due to lack of a judge, then they rescind (yafsakhan) the contract in part to the extent they agree upon, because incidental undividedness does not prevent validity by agreement in the apparent riwaya, as we mentioned.
Source pages p. 567

Commentary
This passage is an inter-madhhab dispute between Abu Hanifa and his two disciples (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani) regarding the validity of hiring out undivided property (musha'). The text first states the position of the Sahibayn: the hire of undivided property is valid whether the lessee is a partner or a stranger. Their reasoning is that undivided property has a benefit—even Abu Hanifa acknowledges that if the tenant is allowed to occupy, equivalent hire is due. Since the essence of a hire contract is benefit, it is permissible. As for the objection that delivery is impossible because the property is undivided, they respond that delivery can be effected either by vacating (takhliya) or by mutual division (tihayi'). By vacating, the partner-lessor removes his belongings and leaves the property to the tenant; by division, the parties agree to use portions on different days. Both methods make delivery possible. They analogize to the validity of hiring from a partner or from two persons. Abu Hanifa argues that this is a hire of something that cannot be delivered, because delivery requires taking possession (qabd), which is a sensory act that can only apply to specific, determined property. Undivided property is unspecified, so delivery is inconceivable. Without delivery, the tenant cannot benefit, and hire is a contract for benefit. He refutes the possibility of delivery by vacating: vacating only becomes a valid delivery if it enables benefit (tamkin), but mere vacating does not create actual ability (tamakkun) to benefit because the other partner's share remains. In sale, the buyer has ability immediately; here it is lacking. Delivery by division is also invalid because division (tihayi') is a consequence of the contract that establishes ownership, so it cannot be a precondition. The contract cannot be validated by something that comes after it. As for the analogy of hiring from a partner: there, the benefits all arise on the lessor's ownership—part by ownership, part by hire—so no undividedness exists. If it is argued that undividedness still exists in proportion, the response is that differing causes do not affect the unified ruling. As for hiring from two persons: delivery is of the whole, and the subsequent division among the lessees is incidental, like a pledge from two persons. The text then notes that despite Abu Hanifa's position, the fatwa (relied-upon ruling) is according to the Sahibayn, as transmitted from al-Mughni. Finally, a legal stratagem (hila) is given: to take the contract before a judge who can enforce it, or if no judge, to rescind part of the contract to eliminate undividedness, because incidental undividedness does not prevent validity in the apparent riwaya.

Key Terms
المشاع (al-mushā‘): Undivided property (shares in a common property not physically separated).
التخلية (al-takhliya): Vacating the premises by the lessor (removing his belongings) to enable the lessee to take possession.
التهيؤ (al-tihāyu’): Mutual division (partition) of usage among partners by agreement on times or portions.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the relied-upon fatwa regarding the hire of undivided property (musha') according to the text?
A) It is invalid according to all Hanafi imams.
B) It is valid only if the lessee is a partner.
C) It is valid according to Sahibayn, and the fatwa is upon their view.
D) It is valid only if the contract is taken before a judge.

Key Takeaway
The relied-upon Hanafi position is that hiring undivided property is valid, with a hila for those who wish to follow Abu Hanifa's view.
