Corrupt Hire: Paying with Part of the Output
Ruling on hire with wage as part of output

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling for a hire contract where the wage is part of the produced item, and apply the rule of equivalent wage (ajr al-mithl) with the cap of the named wage.

Core Idea
A hire where the wage is part of the output is corrupt (fasid), not void; the worker gets the market wage, capped by the agreed amount.

In Hanafi fiqh, not every invalid contract leaves the worker uncompensated. This lesson examines three scenarios where a person hires a weaver, a donkey, or an ox, paying them with a portion of what they produce or transport. The Prophet ﷺ forbade such arrangements in the form of 'qafiz al-tahhan' (miller's measure). The Hanafi school classifies these contracts as corrupt (fasid), meaning they are not fully valid but still obligate payment of the equivalent wage. Understanding this distinction is crucial for distinguishing between void (batil) and corrupt (fasid) contracts and for knowing the worker's entitlement.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three examples
The passage gives three cases: weaver paid with half the cloth, donkey hired for a measure of the food it carries, and ox hired for a measure of the flour it grinds. Note that in each, the wage is a part of the very thing produced or carried.
These are all instances of 'qafiz al-tahhan' type transactions.
2
Determine the ruling on the contract
The text says 'these hires are corrupt (fasida)'. In Hanafi terminology, 'fasid' means the contract is defective but not void. The worker has performed the work, so the contract is not completely without effect.
Contrast with 'batil' which is void ab initio and gives no compensation.
3
Identify the financial consequence
The worker is entitled to ajr al-mithl (equivalent wage) for the work done, but not exceeding the named wage (the agreed amount). This caps the liability.
This prevents the employer from being forced to pay more than originally agreed, even though the contract is corrupt.
4
Understand the reason for corruption
The wage is made part of the output of the work. This resembles the prohibited 'qafiz al-tahhan'. The prohibition indicates that such uncertainty (gharar) in the wage makes the contract defective.
The hadith is used as dalil that such arrangements are not permissible; the Hanafi school interprets it as making the contract fasid, not batil.
5
Apply the ruling to new cases
Any hire where the wage is a share of the thing produced or carried falls under this rule. For example, hiring a farmer to cultivate land for a portion of the harvest is similarly fasid.
The key is that the wage is uncertain and part of the subject matter.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : ولو دفع ..الخ ؛ يعني ولو دفع رجل إلى حائك غزلاً ؛ لينسجه بأجر هو نصف الثوب المنسوج مثلاً ، أو استأجر حماراً يحمل عليه طعاماً إلى بيته بقفيز من ذلك الطعام، أو استأجر ثوراً ليطحن له برّ القفيز من دقيق ذلك البر، فهذه الإجارة فاسدة، ويجب أجر المثل في الكل، لا يجاوز المسمى.
أما كون الإجارة فاسدة ؛ فلأنّ في المسألة الأولى والثانية جعل الأجر بعض ما يخرج من عمله، فيصير في معنى قفيز الطحان، وهو منهي عنه كما أشار إليه الشارح بقوله : وقد نهى النبي ﷺ عنه.
His saying: 'And if one hands over...' etc.: meaning if a man gives yarn to a weaver to weave it for a wage which is half of the woven cloth, for example, or hires a donkey to carry food to his house for a qafiz (measure) of that food, or hires an ox to grind for him wheat for a qafiz of the flour of that wheat — then these hires are corrupt (fasida), and the equivalent wage (ajr al-mithl) is due in all, not exceeding the named wage. As for why the hire is corrupt: because in the first and second cases, the wage is made part of what comes out of his work, so it falls under the same meaning as 'qafiz of the miller' (qafiz al-tahhan), which is prohibited, as the commentator indicated by his saying: 'And the Prophet ﷺ forbade it.'
Source pages p. 568

Commentary
This passage is a ruling statement with a proof from hadith. It explains a corrupt hire (ijarah fasida) where the wage is specified as a portion of the very thing produced or transported. Three examples are given: (1) giving yarn to a weaver to weave it for half the finished cloth; (2) hiring a donkey to carry food to one's house for a qafiz measure of that same food; (3) hiring an ox to grind wheat for a qafiz of the flour from that wheat. In all these cases, the hire is corrupt (fasid). The reason is that the wage is part of the object of the contract itself (the output of the worker's effort), which resembles the prohibited 'qafiz al-tahhan' (miller's qafiz). The Prophet ﷺ forbade such transactions because they involve uncertainty (gharar) and potential exploitation. The ruling: the hire contract is not valid, but since the work has been performed, the worker is entitled to the equivalent wage (ajr al-mithl) for the market value of his labor, but not exceeding the named wage (the agreed amount, even if corrupt, serves as a cap). This protects the worker from overpayment while preventing the contract from being enforced as agreed.

Key Terms
الإجارة الفاسدة (al-ijārah al-fāsida): A hire contract that is corrupt due to a defect in the wage or object, but not void; the worker still earns the equivalent wage.
قفيز الطحان (qafīz al-ṭaḥḥān): A transaction where a miller is paid with a measure of the grain he grinds; prohibited by the Prophet.
أجر المثل (ajr al-mithl): The prevailing market wage for similar work; owed in corrupt hire contracts.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the case of hiring a weaver with half the woven cloth as wage, what is the ruling?
A) The contract is valid and the weaver gets half the cloth.
B) The contract is void (batil) and the weaver gets nothing.
C) The contract is corrupt (fasid) and the weaver gets the equivalent wage up to the named wage.
D) The contract is valid only if the weaver is a partner.

Key Takeaway
When the wage is part of the output, the hire is corrupt (fasid), but the worker still receives the market wage (ajr al-mithl) capped by the named wage.

Ruling on Invalid Ijarah: Payment from Output (Qafiz al-Tahhan)
Explaining the ruling and reasoning for voidable hire with payment from output

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on ijarah when the wage is taken from the output (qafiz al-tahhan) and explain why it is fasid, applying the rule that the hirer must pay ujr al-mithl not exceeding the named wage.

Core Idea
Hiring a worker with a share of the output is invalid—the wage must be certain and independent of the worker's labor.

This lesson examines a specific type of voidable hire contract (ijarah fasidah) known as qafiz al-tahhan, where the wage is a portion of the very thing produced by the worker. The Hanafi school declares such contracts invalid due to uncertainty and the hirer's inability to deliver the wage independently. We will explore the scenarios, the evidence from the Prophet's prohibition, the reasoning behind the ruling, and the remedy of paying the equivalent wage (ujr al-mithl).

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenarios and the ruling
The passage presents three examples: hiring a weaver with half the cloth, hiring a donkey with a measure of the carried food, and hiring an ox with part of the flour. In each, the wage is part of the output. The ruling is that the hire is fasid (voidable), not batil (null).
Third case is said to be obviously void.
2
Locate the primary evidence
The commentator cites the Prophet's prohibition of 'qafiz al-tahhan' (the miller's measure). This is the direct dalil (Sunnah ahad) that establishes the prohibition.
The hadith is mentioned but not quoted fully; it is considered zanni al-thubut but qat'i al-dalalah.
3
Analyze the legal reasoning (ta'lil)
The reasoning is that the hirer cannot deliver the wage independently because its existence depends on the worker's own action, which is itself the subject of the contract. This creates circularity and makes the wage uncertain (gharar).
The condition of capability to deliver is essential for a valid wage.
4
Determine the remedy for a fasid contract
Even though the contract is voidable, if the worker has performed, the hirer must pay the equivalent wage (ujr al-mithl), but not exceeding the named wage. This compensates the worker while respecting the hirer's consent to forgo the excess.
This is consistent with Hanafi rules for fasid contracts: the act is recognized but the defect is remedied by fair compensation.
5
Address the objections from al-Zayla'i
Al-Zayla'i raises two problems: how the wage is owned immediately without delivery, and the seeming contradiction between ownership and not deserving the wage. The answer from al-Minh clarifies that in the specific case where the wage is paid immediately (bi al-ta'jil), ownership is by prompt payment, not by the contract's validity.
This preserves the principle that a void contract does not transfer ownership of the wage.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
11 ] قوله : ولو دفع ..الخ ؛ يعني ولو دفع رجل إلى حائك غزلاً ؛ لينسجه بأجر هو نصف الثوب المنسوج مثلاً ، أو استأجر حماراً يحمل عليه طعاماً إلى بيته بقفيز من ذلك الطعام، أو استأجر ثوراً ليطحن له برّ القفيز من دقيق ذلك البر، فهذه الإجارة فاسدة، ويجب أجر المثل في الكل، لا يجاوز المسمى. أما كون الإجارة فاسدة ؛ فلأنّ في المسألة الأولى والثانية جعل الأجر بعض ما يخرج من عمله، فيصير في معنى قفيز الطحان، وهو منهي عنه كما أشار إليه الشارح بقوله : وقد نهى النبي عنه. هذا يسمى قفيز الطحان والمعنى فيه : إن المستأجر عاجز عن تسليم الأجر ؛ لأن حصوله بفعل الأجير، ولا يعد أحد قادراً بفعل غيره ؛ ولأنه جعل الأجر شيئاً لا يمكن تسليمه إلا بعمل للأجير، وهو العمل الذي يجب عليه بحكم العقد، فيكون القدرة التي هي شراء العقد قائمة بحكم العقد، فتصير بمنزلة حكم العقد، والشرط لا يصلح حكماً، فكذا لا يصلح قائماً به. وأما في المسألة الثالثة ؛ فالفساد ظاهر غير محتاج إلى البيان. وأما وجوب أجر المثل ؛ فلأنّه سَلّمَ له المعقود عليه ؛ لأنّ العامل لم يصر شريكاً في العين، بخلاف ما إذا استأجر ليحمل نصف طعامه بالنصف الآخر، حيث لا يجب الأجر ؛ لأنّ المستأجر ثم ملكه بالأجر في الحال بالتعجيل فصار حاملاً طعاماً مشتركاً بينهما، وبحمل طعام مشترك بينهما لا يجب الأجر إذما من جزء يحمله إلا وهو عامل لنفسه، فلا يتحقق تسليم المعقود عليه. وأما أنه لا يجاوز بالأجر المسمّى ؛ فلان الإجارة لما فسدت وجب الأقل من المسمّى ومن أجر المثل لرضاه بحطّ الزيادة. قال الزَّيْلَعِي : في «شرح الكنز ) : وفيه إشكالان : أحدهما : إن الإجارة فاسدة، والأجرة لا تملك بالصحيحة منها بالعقد عندنا ، سواء كان عيناً أو ديناً على ما بيناه، فكيف ملكه هاهنا من غير تسليم، ومن غير شرط التعجيل. والثاني : إنّه قال ملكه في الحال، وقوله : لا يستحق الأجرة ينافي الملك ؛ لأنه لا يملكه إذا ملكه إلا بطريق الأجرة ، فإذا لم يستحق شيئاً فكيف يملكه. وأجاب صاحب «المنح» عن هذين الإشكالين بقوله : يمكن الجواب عنه : أما عن الأوّل ؛ فلان صورة المسألة أنه عَجَلَ له الأجرة، فإنَّه قال : ملك النصف في الحال بالتعجيل، وهي تملك به كما تملك بشرطه.
11] His saying: 'And if one gives ... etc.' means: If a man gives yarn to a weaver to weave it for a wage which is half of the woven cloth, or hires a donkey to carry food to his house for a qafiz of that food, or hires an ox to grind wheat for him for some of its flour, then this hire is void (fasid), and the equivalent wage (ajr al-mithl) is obligatory in all, not exceeding the named wage. As for why the hire is void: because in the first and second cases, he made the wage part of what results from his work, so it falls under the meaning of the miller's measure (qafiz al-tahhan), which is prohibited, as the commentator indicated by his saying: 'The Prophet prohibited it.' This is called the miller's measure, and the reasoning is that the hirer is incapable of delivering the wage because its acquisition depends on the action of the worker, and no one is considered capable through another's action; also because he made the wage something that cannot be delivered except through the worker's action, which is the action obligatory on him by the contract, so the capability that is a condition of the contract stands by the contract itself, and thus becomes like a ruling of the contract, and a condition cannot be a ruling, so likewise it cannot stand by it. As for the third case, the voidness is apparent and needs no explanation. As for the obligation of the equivalent wage: because he delivered the contracted object; since the worker did not become a partner in the property, unlike the case where one hires to carry half his food for the other half, where no wage is due because the hirer there owns it immediately through the wage due to prompt payment, so he becomes a carrier of food shared between them, and for carrying shared food no wage is due, as no part he carries is except that he is working for himself, so delivery of the contracted object is not realized. As for not exceeding the named wage: because when the hire is void, the lesser of the named wage and the equivalent wage is due, due to his satisfaction with forgoing the excess. Al-Zayla'i said in Sharh al-Kanz: 'There are two problems in it: First, the hire is void, and the wage is not owned by a valid contract in our school, whether it is a specific thing or a debt, as we explained, so how did he own it here without delivery and without a condition of prompt payment? Second, he said he owns it immediately, and his saying 'he does not deserve the wage' contradicts ownership, because he does not own it when he owns it except as a wage, so if he does not deserve anything, how does he own it?' The author of al-Minh answered these two problems by saying: 'It can be answered: As for the first, because the scenario of the issue is that he paid the wage promptly, for he said: 'He owns half immediately due to prompt payment,' and it is owned by it as it is owned by its condition.'
Source pages p. 568

Commentary
This passage is an expansion (sharh) on the ruling of voidable hire (al-ijarah al-fasidah) where the wage is taken from the output of the hired work. The commentator explains the scenario: giving yarn to a weaver to weave for half the cloth, or hiring a donkey to carry food for a measure of that food, or hiring an ox to grind wheat for part of its flour. All three are void (fasid) because they fall under 'qafiz al-tahhan' (the miller's measure), which the Prophet prohibited. The reasoning (ta'lil) is that the hirer cannot deliver the wage securely, as its existence depends on the worker's action, which is itself the subject of the contract. This creates circularity and renders the contract void. The third case (grinding) is void by obvious analogy. Despite voidness, if the hirer has benefited from the work, the worker is entitled to the equivalent wage (ajr al-mithl), but not exceeding the named wage. The text then addresses two problems raised by al-Zayla'i: how the wage is owned immediately without delivery, and the seeming contradiction between ownership and not deserving the wage. The answer from the author of al-Minh clarifies that in this specific scenario, the wage is paid immediately (bi al-ta'jil), so ownership is by prompt payment, not by the contract itself. Thus, the worker owns the wage at the moment of agreement, but if the contract is void, he is not entitled to the named wage as a contractual right; rather, he receives the lesser of the named wage and the equivalent wage as a fair compensation. This maintains consistency with Hanafi principles where a void contract does not transfer ownership of the wage, but here the ownership is due to immediate delivery, not the contract's validity.

Key Terms
قفيز الطحان (qafiz al-tahhan): A measure of grain given as wage to a miller; used here as a term for any hire where the wage is taken from the output of the hired work.
إجارة فاسدة (ijarah fasidah): A voidable hire contract that is defective in its conditions but can be rectified by paying the equivalent wage.
أجر المثل (ajr al-mithl): The fair market wage for similar work, used as compensation when a contract is fasid but the worker has performed.

Key Takeaway
A hire contract where the wage is taken from the output of the work (qafiz al-tahhan) is fasid, requiring payment of the equivalent wage up to the named wage.

Invalid Ijarah with Payment from Work Output: Qafiz al-Tahhan
Inter-madhhab dispute over ijarah with wage from output

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why the Hanafi school invalidates ijarah paid from the work output (qafiz al-tahhan) and evaluate the counter-argument based on custom.

Core Idea
Paying wages from the worker's own output creates uncertainty; Hanafis deem it invalid unless the wage is a clear debt.

The famous case of qafiz al-tahhan tests the limits of ijarah. When a miller is paid from the flour he grinds, the wage is contingent on his own effort, making delivery impossible. This lesson unpacks the reasoning behind invalidity and the intra-Hanafi dispute over local custom, along with a legal trick to accommodate practice.

Guided Path
1
Identify the core problematic contract
Examine the contract where the wage is part of the work output (e.g., paying a miller with some of the flour, or a carrier with some of the carried goods). Recognise it as a form of qafiz al-tahhan.
This is prohibited by hadith and considered invalid (fasid) in the Hanafi school.
2
Understand the Hanafi rationale for invalidity
The hirer cannot deliver the wage because its acquisition depends on the worker's action. Since the wage is contingent on the worker fulfilling the contract, the condition of capacity is not met, making the contract invalid.
The wage must be deliverable independently of the worker's performance.
3
Distinguish between two scenarios of payment from output
In one scenario, the hirer makes the entire output his own and stipulates wage from it → invalid, worker deserves fair wage. In another, the output is shared as wage → void, worker gets nothing because he owns his share by the contract.
The distinction lies in how ownership of the output is allocated.
4
Follow al-Zayla'i's objections and al-Manh's responses
Al-Zayla'i raises two problems: how can the wage be owned without delivery in an invalid contract? And how can immediate ownership coexist with not deserving the wage? Al-Manh answers that the wage was accelerated (set as immediate ownership), and later it becomes clear that the worker deserves nothing, similar to a case of accelerated wage reclaimed.
This resolves the apparent contradiction about ownership and entitlement.
5
Analyze the Balkh/Nasaf position and the legal trick
Some Hanafi scholars of Balkh and Nasaf permit such contracts based on local custom, analogising to istisna'. The majority rejects this because custom must be widespread. A legal trick: stipulate the wage as an absolute debt (qafiz) in the hirer's liability, not tied to the output, then pay from it.
The trick avoids the prohibition by making the wage a distinct debt.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ببعضه، أو ثوراً ليطحن بُرا له ببعض دقيقه) هذا يسمى قفيز الطحان والمعنى فيه : إن المستأجر عاجز عن تسليم الأجر ؛ لأن حصوله بفعل الأجير، ولا يعد أحد قادراً بفعل غيره ؛ ولأنه جعل الأجر شيئاً لا يمكن تسليمه إلا بعمل للأجير، وهو العمل الذي يجب عليه بحكم العقد، فيكون القدرة التي هي شراء العقد قائمة بحكم العقد، فتصير بمنزلة حكم العقد، والشرط لا يصلح حكماً، فكذا لا يصلح قائماً به. وأما في المسألة الثالثة ؛ فالفساد ظاهر غير محتاج إلى البيان. وأما وجوب أجر المثل ؛ فلأنّه سَلّمَ له المعقود عليه ؛ لأنّ العامل لم يصر شريكاً في العين، بخلاف ما إذا استأجر ليحمل نصف طعامه بالنصف الآخر، حيث لا يجب الأجر ؛ لأنّ المستأجر ثم ملكه بالأجر في الحال بالتعجيل فصار حاملاً طعاماً مشتركاً بينهما، وبحمل طعام مشترك بينهما لا يجب الأجر إذما من جزء يحمله إلا وهو عامل لنفسه، فلا يتحقق تسليم المعقود عليه. وأما أنه لا يجاوز بالأجر المسمّى ؛ فلان الإجارة لما فسدت وجب الأقل من المسمّى ومن أجر المثل لرضاه بحطّ الزيادة. قال الزَّيْلَعِي : في «شرح الكنز ) : وفيه إشكالان : أحدهما : إن الإجارة فاسدة، والأجرة لا تملك بالصحيحة منها بالعقد عندنا ، سواء كان عيناً أو ديناً على ما بيناه، فكيف ملكه هاهنا من غير تسليم، ومن غير شرط التعجيل. والثاني : إنّه قال ملكه في الحال، وقوله : لا يستحق الأجرة ينافي الملك ؛ لأنه لا يملكه إذا ملكه إلا بطريق الأجرة ، فإذا لم يستحق شيئاً فكيف يملكه. وأجاب صاحب «المنح» عن هذين الإشكالين بقوله : يمكن الجواب عنه : أما عن الأوّل ؛ فلان صورة المسألة أنه عَجَلَ له الأجرة، فإنَّه قال : ملك النصف في الحال بالتعجيل، وهي تملك به كما تملك بشرطه. تبيين الحقائق (۵ : ۱۳۰). وقد نهى النبي عنه (۱۱) ؛ لأنه جعل الأجر بعض ما يخرج من عمله، والصورتان الأوليان في معنى قفيز الطحان. وأما عن الثاني ؛ فلأنّه لما ملكه بالتعجيل كما ذكرنا وعمل تبين بعد ذلك عدم استحقاقه لشيء من الأجرة، فصار كما لو عَجَلَ له الأجرة في عقد الإجارة، فإنه يحكم بكونها مالكاً لها ، فإذا استحقها مستحق تبين كونه ليس بمالك. انتهى. فتدبر. وقال الزيلعي (٢) : وكان مشايخ بلخ والنسف يجوزون حمل الطعام ببعض المحمول أو نسج الثوب ببعض المنسوج ؛ لتعامل أهل بلادهم بذلك، وقالوا : من لم يجوزه إنما لم يجوزه بالقياس على قفيز الطحان والقياس يترك بالتعارف. ولئن قلنا : إنّ النص يتناوله دلالة، فالنص يختص بالتعامل، ألا ترى أن الاستصناع تُرِكَ القياسُ فيه، وخص عن القواعد الشرعية بالتعامل، ومشايخنا له لم يجوزوا هذا التخصيص ؛ لأنّ ذلك تعامل أهل بلدة واحدة وبه لا يختص الأثر، بخلاف الاستصناع، فإنّ التعامل به جرى في كل البلاد، وبمثله يترك القياس ويخص الأثر، والحيلة في جوازه أن يشترط قفيزا مطلقاً من غير أن يشترط أنه من المحمول أو من المطحون، فيجب في ذمّة المستأجر ، ثمّ يعطيه منه، ثمّ الأصل فيه : إنه متى ما جعل المستأجر المحمول كلّه لنفسه وشرط له الأجر من المحمول فسدت الإجارة، فإذا عمل الأجير استحق أجر المثل، كمسألة الكتاب المذكورة، ومتى ما جعل المحمول بعضه له والبعض الباقي أجرة بطلت الإجارة، وإن حمل لا يستحق شيئاً ؛ لأنه ملكه بالعقد، وفي الأول لم يملكه على ما بينا انتهى. فاحفظه. [١] قوله : وقد نهى النبي الله عنه ؛ روى الدَّارَ قُطْنِيُّ والبَيْهَقِيُّ في «سننهما»، وأبو يعلى الموصلي في مسنده»: عن أبي سعيد الخدري الله قال : «نهى رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم عن عسب الفحل ، وعن قفيز الطحان». كذا في كمال الدراية.
With part of it, or an ox to grind his wheat with part of its flour. This is called qafiz al-tahhan. The meaning is: The hirer is unable to deliver the wage because its acquisition depends on the worker's action, and no one is considered capable through another's action. Also because he made the wage something that cannot be delivered except by the worker's work, which is the work obligatory by the contract. Thus the capacity that is a condition of the contract is established by the contract, so it becomes like a ruling of the contract, and a condition cannot serve as a ruling, so likewise it cannot stand. As for the third case: the invalidity is apparent and needs no explanation. As for the obligation of the fair wage: because he delivered the subject matter of the contract, since the worker did not become a partner in the property, unlike the case where he hires to carry half his food with the other half, where the wage is not obligatory because the hirer then owns it by the wage immediately by acceleration, so he becomes a carrier of food shared between them, and for carrying shared food no wage is obligatory because no part he carries is except while he works for himself, so delivery of the subject matter is not realized. As for not exceeding the named wage: because when the ijarah is invalid, the lesser of the named wage and the fair wage is obligatory due to his consent to reduction of the excess. Al-Zayla'i said in Sharh al-Kanz: There are two problems: First, the ijarah is invalid, and the wage is not owned by a valid contract according to us, whether it is a specific thing or a debt as we explained, so how is it owned here without delivery and without condition of acceleration? Second, he said he owned it immediately, and his saying he does not deserve the wage contradicts ownership because he does not own it except by way of wage, so if he does not deserve anything, how does he own it? The author of al-Manh answered these two problems by saying: It can be answered: As for the first, because the form of the matter is that he accelerated the wage, for he said he owned half immediately by acceleration, and it is owned by it as it is owned by its condition. Tabyin al-Haqa'iq (5:130). And the Prophet forbade it (11) because he made the wage part of what comes out of his work, and the first two cases are similar to qafiz al-tahhan. As for the second: because when he owned it by acceleration as we mentioned, and he worked, it then became clear that he does not deserve any of the wage, so it becomes like if he had accelerated the wage in an ijarah contract, then it is ruled that he is the owner of it, and if a claimant claims it, it becomes clear that he is not the owner. End. So reflect. Al-Zayla'i said: The scholars of Balkh and Nasaf permitted carrying food with part of what is carried or weaving cloth with part of what is woven, due to the custom of the people of their land, and they said: Those who do not permit it only do so by analogy to qafiz al-tahhan, and analogy is abandoned due to custom. And if we say that the text includes it by implication, the text is specific to the custom. Do you not see that istisna' (manufacturing contract) had analogy abandoned in it, and it was excepted from the legal rules due to custom? But our scholars did not permit this exception because that is the custom of a single town, and by it the established ruling is not excepted, unlike istisna', for its custom occurred in all lands, and by such, analogy is abandoned and the ruling is excepted. The trick to permit it is that he stipulates an absolute qafiz without stipulating that it is from the carried or the ground, so it becomes a debt on the hirer, then he gives him from it. Then the principle: Whenever the hirer makes all the carried goods for himself and stipulates the wage from the carried goods, the ijarah is invalid, so when the worker works, he deserves the fair wage, like the mentioned case in the book. And whenever he makes part of the carried goods for himself and the remaining part as wage, the ijarah is void, and if he carries he does not deserve anything because he owns it by the contract, and in the first he did not own it as we explained. End. So memorize it. [1] His saying: And the Prophet forbade it; al-Daraqutni and al-Bayhaqi narrated in their Sunans, and Abu Ya'la al-Mawsili in his Musnad, from Abu Sa'id al-Khudri that he said: 'The Messenger of Allah forbade the stud fee of the stallion and qafiz al-tahhan.' This is in Kamal al-Dirayah.
Source pages p. 569

Commentary
This passage is an expansion on the chapter of invalid ijarah, specifically regarding contracts where the wage is part of the work output, known as qafiz al-tahhan. The author begins by explaining the reason for invalidity: the hirer cannot deliver the wage because it depends on the worker's action, and a condition cannot become a ruling. He then discusses three cases. In the third case, invalidity is obvious. For the obligation of fair wage (ujr al-mithl), it is because the subject matter was delivered to the hirer, unlike a scenario where hiring to carry half one's food for the other half, where no wage is due because the hirer becomes a partner. The named wage sets a limit; since the contract is invalid, the lesser of the named wage and fair wage is owed. Al-Zayla'i raises two objections: (1) how can the wage be owned without delivery or acceleration in an invalid contract? (2) how can immediate ownership coexist with not deserving the wage? The author of al-Manh answers: the wage was accelerated; ownership by acceleration is possible, and later it becomes clear that the worker deserves nothing, similar to a case where a wage is accelerated then reclaimed. The discussion then shifts to a dispute between the majority Hanafi scholars and some Hanafis from Balkh and Nasaf, who allowed such transactions based on their local custom, drawing an analogy to istisna' (manufacturing contract), which is permitted despite analogy due to custom. The responding scholars reject this, arguing that custom must be widespread, not limited to one town. However, they offer a legal trick (hila): stipulate an absolute qafiz as a debt in the hirer's liability, not specifying it from the output. The passage also records the hadith prohibition of qafiz al-tahhan and the stud fee, confirming the underlying ruling.

Key Terms
قفيز الطحان (qafiz al-tahhan): A transaction where a miller takes a portion of the flour as payment for grinding.
أجر المثل (ujr al-mithl): The fair market wage for similar work.
تعامل (ta'amul): Common practice or custom of the people in transactions.
حيلة (hila): A legal stratagem to achieve a permissible outcome while avoiding prohibition.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the majority Hanafi position, what is the ruling when a hirer pays the worker with part of the carried goods (e.g., carrying food with part of it as wage)?
A) The contract is valid and the named wage is due.
B) The contract is invalid and the worker deserves the fair wage.
C) The contract is void and the worker gets nothing.
D) The contract is valid if customary in that town.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school invalidates ijarah where the wage is part of the work output due to uncertainty, but permits a legal trick (hila) to make the wage a clear debt.

The Prohibition of Paying Wages from the Product (Qafiz al-Tahhan) and the Role of Custom
Ruling on paying wages from the product, with hadith proof and exception by custom

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the prohibition of paying wages from the product, explain the Hanafi proof, and apply the mufta bihi ruling including the legal stratagem.

Core Idea
Paying wages from the labor's output is haram because it is akin to gambling; only widespread custom can override the prohibition.

This lesson examines a classic prohibition in Hanafi fiqh: paying a worker from the very product he produces (e.g., giving the miller a measure of flour as his wage). The source provides a hadith proof and then discusses a dispute among Hanafi scholars about whether local custom can permit such transactions. Finally, it presents a lawful stratagem (hila) to achieve a similar result without violating the prohibition. Understanding this passage sharpens your ability to navigate between textual evidence and customary practice.

Guided Path
1
Identify the prohibited transaction
The passage discusses 'qafiz al-tahhan' – the miller's qafiz. This is paying a worker (miller) with a fixed measure of flour from the grain he grinds. The Prophet prohibited this. We need to understand why this specific transaction is problematic.
The prohibition is not just for millers; it extends to any case where the wage is part of the product (e.g., carrying food for part of the load, weaving cloth for part of the cloth).
2
Locate the textual evidence
The passage cites a hadith: 'The Messenger of Allah prohibited the stud fee of a stallion and the miller's qafiz.' This is the primary proof. The prohibition is explicit (al-nahy).
The hadith is ahad (zanni al-thubut) but nonetheless legally binding in Hanafi usul.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah (how the proof yields the ruling)
The prohibition (nahy) indicates haram. The 'miller's qafiz' is interpretively extended by analogy (qiyas) to any wage that is part of the output because the effective cause (illa) is the uncertainty and the worker being paid from the same thing he produces, which is akin to gambling (gharar).
The passage explicitly says: 'because he made the wage part of what comes out of his work.'
4
Examine the intra-Hanafi dispute: Balkh and Nasaf
Some Hanafi scholars (from Balkh and Nasaf) permitted similar transactions based on local custom. They argued that analogy should be abandoned for custom (ta'amul), just as istisna' (commission to manufacture) is allowed despite lacking precise specification.
The mainstream Hanafi position rejects this because the custom is only local, not widespread. Only widespread custom can override a text.
5
Identify the mufta bihi position and the hila
The mainstream ruling is: the direct transaction is fasid (void). However, a legal stratagem (hila) is permitted: stipulate an absolute qafiz as a debt in the hirer's liability, then give from the product. This avoids tying the wage to the output and makes the contract valid.
The hila is a recommended way to achieve practical needs while staying within the Shari'ah.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وقد نهى النبي عنه (۱۱) ؛ لأنه جعل الأجر بعض ما يخرج من عمله، والصورتان الأوليان في معنى قفيز الطحان.
وأما عن الثاني؛ فلأنّه لما ملكه بالتعجيل كما ذكرنا وعمل تبين بعد ذلك عدم استحقاقه لشيء من الأجرة، فصار كما لو عَجَلَ له الأجرة في عقد الإجارة، فإنه يحكم بكونها مالكاً لها، فإذا استحقها مستحق تبين كونه ليس بمالك. انتهى. فتدبر.
(۲)
وقال الزيلعي (٢) : وكان مشايخ بلخ والنسف يجوزون حمل الطعام ببعض المحمول أو نسج الثوب ببعض المنسوج؛ لتعامل أهل بلادهم بذلك، وقالوا : من لم يجوزه إنما لم يجوزه بالقياس على قفيز الطحان والقياس يترك بالتعارف. ولئن قلنا : إنّ النص يتناوله دلالة، فالنص يختص بالتعامل، ألا ترى أن الاستصناع تُرِكَ القياسُ فيه، وخص عن القواعد الشرعية بالتعامل، ومشايخنا له لم يجوزوا هذا التخصيص؛ لأنّ ذلك تعامل أهل بلدة واحدة وبه لا يختص الأثر، بخلاف الاستصناع، فإنّ التعامل به جرى في كل البلاد، وبمثله يترك القياس ويخص الأثر، والحيلة في جوازه أن يشترط قفيزا مطلقاً من غير أن يشترط أنه من المحمول أو من المطحون، فيجب في ذمّة المستأجر، ثمّ يعطيه منه، ثمّ الأصل فيه : إنه متى ما جعل المستأجر المحمول كلّه لنفسه وشرط له الأجر من المحمول فسدت الإجارة، فإذا عمل الأجير استحق أجر المثل، كمسألة الكتاب المذكورة، ومتى ما جعل المحمول بعضه له والبعض الباقي أجرة بطلت الإجارة، وإن حمل لا يستحق شيئاً؛ لأنه ملكه بالعقد، وفي الأول لم يملكه على ما بينا انتهى. فاحفظه. [١] قوله : وقد نهى النبي الله عنه؛ روى الدَّارَ قُطْنِيُّ والبَيْهَقِيُّ في «سننهما»، وأبو يعلى الموصلي في مسنده»: عن أبي سعيد الخدري الله قال : «نهى رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم عن عسب الفحل، وعن قفيز الطحان». كذا في كمال الدراية
And the Prophet prohibited it (11) because he made the wage part of what comes out of his work, and the first two cases are similar to the miller's qafiz. As for the second: because when he possessed it through advance payment as we mentioned and worked, it became clear afterwards that he was not entitled to any wage, so it is as if he advanced him the wage in a hire contract, then he is judged to be the owner of it, and when a rightful claimant claims it, it becomes clear that he is not an owner. End. Reflect. (2) Al-Zayla'i said: The scholars of Balkh and Nasaf allowed carrying food with part of what is carried or weaving cloth with part of what is woven, due to the practice of the people of their lands. They said: whoever does not permit it only does not permit it by analogy with the miller's qafiz, and analogy is abandoned for custom. And if we say that the text includes it by implication, then the text is specific to that transaction. Do you not see that istisna' (commission to manufacture) was exempted from analogy and set apart from the legal rules because of custom? Our scholars (the later ones) did not allow this specification because that is the practice of one town, and by it the effect is not specified, unlike istisna', because the practice of it occurred in all lands. By such practice analogy is abandoned and effect is specified. The legal trick (hila) to permit it is that he stipulates an absolute qafiz without stipulating that it is from the carried or the ground, so it becomes a debt in the hirer's liability, then he gives him from it. Then the principle in it: Whenever the hirer takes all the carried goods for himself and stipulates the wage from the carried goods, the hire becomes fasid. When the worker works, he is entitled to ujrat al-mithl, as in the mentioned book's issue. And whenever part of the carried goods is given to him and the remaining part is the wage, the hire is void, and if he carries, he gets nothing because he possessed it by the contract. In the first, he did not possess it as we explained. End. Memorize it. [1] His statement: 'And the Prophet prohibited it'; narrated by al-Daraqutni and al-Bayhaqi in their Sunan, and Abu Ya'la al-Mawsili in his Musnad, from Abu Sa'id al-Khudri (may Allah be pleased with him) who said: 'The Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) prohibited the stud fee of a stallion and the miller's qafiz.' Thus in Kamil al-Diraya.
Source pages p. 570

Commentary
This passage combines a ruling with proof and a discussion of customary exceptions. It begins by explaining the prohibition of paying wages from the product of labor, as in the case of the miller's qafiz (a fixed measure of flour given as wage for grinding). The Prophet explicitly prohibited this because it makes the wage a part of the very thing being produced, leading to uncertainty (gharar). The text distinguishes between two scenarios: one where the employee receives the product in advance (as wage) and then works, and another where the wage is specified from the output. The parallel is drawn with advancing wages in a hire contract—if the employee later loses the right, it becomes clear he did not truly own it. Al-Zayla'i then reports that some Hanafi scholars (from Balkh and Nasaf) allowed similar transactions (like paying for carrying food with part of the carried load, or weaving cloth with part of the woven cloth) based on local custom. They argued that the analogy to the prohibited qafiz should be abandoned in favor of customary practice, just as istisna' (commission to manufacture) is permitted despite lacking precise specification. However, other Hanafi scholars rejected this because the practice of one city is insufficient to override a textual prohibition; only widespread custom (as with istisna') can do so. A hila (legal stratagem) is then presented: instead of specifying that the wage is from the product, one can stipulate an absolute qafiz as a debt in the hirer's liability, and then the hirer can give from the product. This avoids the prohibition because the wage is not directly tied to the output. The passage concludes with the hadith evidence for the prohibition.

Key Terms
قفيز الطحان (qafiz al-tahhan): A fixed measure (qafiz) of flour given as wage to a miller for grinding grain; prohibited by hadith.
تعامل (ta'amul): Mutual practice or customary transaction among people; here, the basis for allowing certain contracts despite analogy.
حيلة (hila): A legal stratagem to achieve a permissible outcome while avoiding a prohibition; here, stipulating an absolute qafiz as a debt.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the mainstream Hanafi position, why is the custom of Balkh and Nasaf not sufficient to permit paying wages from the product?
A) Because the custom is not widespread across all lands.
B) Because the hadith is mutawatir and cannot be overridden.
C) Because the scholars of Balkh and Nasaf were weak in hadith.
D) Because the qafiz al-tahhan is explicitly mentioned in the Quran.

Key Takeaway
Paying wages from the product of labour is prohibited by hadith; only a widespread custom can override it, but a legal stratagem (hila) allows for a similar valid transaction.

Hiring a Baker for Specified Output per Day: Intra-Hanafi Dispute
Intra-Hanafi dispute on validity of hiring with work and time specifications

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish the positions of Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn on mixed-object hire contracts and apply the mufta bihi view.

Core Idea
When work and time both appear, Sahibayn prioritize work to validate the contract; Abu Hanifa sees ambiguity.

This passage presents a classical dispute within the Hanafi school: a baker is hired to bake a fixed quantity in a single day. The disagreement turns on whether the mention of time makes the contract ambiguous or merely serves as a deadline. We will examine both proofs and the practical outcome.

Guided Path
1
Identify the contract scenario
Understand the case: hiring a baker to bake ten maunds today for a dirham.
The ma'qud 'alayh (object of contract) is disputed.
2
State Abu Hanifa's ruling and reasoning
Abu Hanifa rules the contract fasid because both work and time are considered objects, leading to uncertainty.
His proof: combining work and time creates conflicting benefits.
3
State the Sahibayn's ruling and reasoning
Abu Yusuf and Muhammad rule it valid: the object is work alone, time is for acceleration (ta'jil).
They analogize to a hire where work is the focus.
4
Compare the two proofs
Identify the exact point of disagreement: whether mention of time necessarily makes it part of the object.
Abu Hanifa sees no preponderance; Sahibayn prioritize work as the purpose.
5
Determine the mufta bihi position
The relied-upon view is that of the Sahibayn, as it validates common commercial practice.
This is the operative ruling for fatwa today.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
أو رجلاً ليخبز له كذا اليوم بكذا : أي استأجر رجلاً ليخبز له عشرة أمناء اليوم بدرهم، فإن هذا فاسد عند أبي حنيفة ، وعندهما يصح، والمعقود عليه العمل، وذكر الوقت للتعجيل.
[۲]- - -
له : أَنه جَمَعَ بينَ العمل والوقت، والأوَّلُ : أي العمل يوجب كونَ العمل معقوداً عليه ، وفيه نفع للمستأجر ، والثَّاني : أي الوقت يوجب كون تسليم النَّفْسِ في هذا اليوم معقودا عليه وفيه نفعُ الأجير، فيفضي إلى المنازعة)، ولو كان المعقود عليه كليهما : أي يعملُ هذا العمل مستغرقاً ؛ لهذا اليوم فذلك مما لا قدرة عليه لأحدٍ عادة، حتى لو قال : ليخبز له عشرة أمناء في اليوم، فعن أبي حنيفة أنه يصح
[١] قوله : وعندهما يصح ؛ أي عقد الإجارة ؛ لأنه جعل المعقود عملاً دون اليوم، فإذا فرغ عنه نصف النهار فله الأجر كاملاً ، وإن لم يفرغه في اليوم فعليه أن يعمله في الغد ؛ لأنّ المعقود عليه هو العمل ؛ لأنه هو المقصود، وهو معلوم وذكر اليوم للتعجيل.
فكأنه استأجره للعمل على أن يفرغ منه في أوّل أوقات الإمكان، فيحمل عليه تصحيحاً للعقد عند تعذر الجمع بينهما، ويرجّح بكون العمل مقصوداً دون الوقت وتقدير المعمول يدلُّ عليه ؛ لأنّ الإجارة إذا وقعت على المنفعة لا تقدر بالعمل، وإنما تقدر بالوقت.
[٢]قوله : إنه جمع ... الخ ؛ هذا دليل على ما ذهب إليه الإمام، وتوضيحه: إنّ ذكر الوقت دليل على كون المنفعة معقوداً عليها ، وذكر العمل دليل على كونه معقوداً عليه ونفع المستأجر في الثاني ، ونفعُ الأجير في الأوّل، ولا ترجيح لأحدهما على الآخر.
Or a man to bake for him such and such a day for such and such: i.e., he hired a man to bake ten maunds today for a dirham. This is fasid according to Abu Hanifa, but according to the two (Sahibayn) it is valid. The object of contract is the work, and mention of time is for acceleration. [2] For him (Abu Hanifa): He combined work and time. The first (work) makes the work the object of contract, and in it there is benefit for the employer. The second (time) makes the delivery of the self in this day the object of contract, and in it there is benefit for the employee, leading to dispute. And if both were the object of contract, i.e., he does this work occupying the whole day, that is not within anyone's capacity normally. So if he said: 'Bake ten maunds in the day,' then from Abu Hanifa it is valid. [1] His statement: 'According to the two it is valid' i.e., the contract of hire is valid because he made the object the work, not the day. So if he finishes in half the day, he gets full wages, and if he does not finish in the day, he must do it the next day. Because the object of contract is the work, as it is the intended purpose, and it is known, and mention of day is for acceleration. So it is as if he hired him for the work on condition that he finish it at the earliest possible time, and this construction is adopted to validate the contract when combining both is impossible; and it is reinforced that work is the purpose, not time, and the specification of the worked product indicates that. Because hire contract when on a benefit is not measured by work but by time. [2] His statement: 'He combined...' etc. This is evidence for the Imam's position. Its clarification: Mention of time indicates that the benefit is the object of contract, and mention of work indicates that work is the object of contract. The employer benefits from the second, the employee from the first, and there is no preponderance of one over the other.
Source pages p. 571

Commentary
This is an intra-Hanafi dispute. The passage presents a case: a person hires a baker to bake a specified amount (ten maunds) in one day for a dirham. Abu Hanifa rules this contract fasid (void) because it combines both work and time as objects of the contract, leading to uncertainty and potential dispute. The Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) rule it valid by considering work alone as the object, with time merely for acceleration. The commentary explains both positions. Abu Hanifa argues that mentioning work and time creates ambiguity: work benefits the employer, time benefits the employee, and they conflict. The Sahibayn prioritize work as the real purpose, interpreting the time specification as a deadline for completion. They analogize to a contract where the work is the focus, and time is only to urge promptness. The commentary also notes that if the contract was for work occupying the whole day, it would be impossible normally. A variant from Abu Hanifa allows validity if phrased as 'in the day' (using 'fi' for container) rather than 'the day' (for duration).

Key Terms
معقود عليه (ma'qud 'alayh): The object or subject matter of a contract; what is agreed upon and for which the contract is concluded.
فاسد (fasid): A contract that is void due to a defect in its substance, such as ambiguity in the object; it is not wholly void but does not produce legal effects unless rectified.
التعجيل (al-ta'jil): Acceleration or urging promptness; here, mentioning time is interpreted as a deadline to expedite work, not as a condition of hire.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Sahibayn, why is the contract to bake ten maunds in a day valid despite specifying a time?
A) Because the time is considered part of the object of contract.
B) Because the time is only for acceleration, and the real object is the work.
C) Because Abu Hanifa later retracted his view.
D) Because the contract involves an impossibility.

Key Takeaway
The relied-upon Hanafi position validates contracts specifying both work and a deadline by treating time as a mere acceleration clause.

Ijarah — Hire and Lease
intermediate
12 min
Conditions Invalidating Ijarah: Time vs. Work and Double Plowing
Commentary on conditions rendering ijarah fasid.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on ijarah contracts that specify both time and work, and evaluate the validity of conditions like double plowing based on necessity and persistence of benefit.

Core Idea
When both time and work are equally intended in ijarah, the contract is fasid due to uncertainty; a condition benefiting the lessor alone invalidates unless required for the work.

In this lesson, we examine two connected issues in Hanafi ijarah law: the effect of specifying both time and work as objects of the contract, and the condition of plowing land twice. The commentary from 'Umdat al-Riayah clarifies when such specifications render the contract invalid (fasid) and when they are permissible. Understanding these distinctions is crucial for drafting valid hire contracts.

Guided Path
1
Identify the issue: both time and work specified
Locate the part of the passage where the contract specifies both a time (e.g., 'in this day') and a specific work (e.g., baking a quantity of flour). Note that the commentary analyzes whether this creates uncertainty.
The key phrase is 'في اليوم' (in the day) used with a specific work.
2
Analyze the linguistic ruling on 'fi'
Understand that the preposition 'fi' indicates a container, not full duration. Therefore, specifying 'in the day' does not require the entire day's work; the work itself is the primary object.
This is contrasted with omitting 'fi', which would require full duration.
3
Understand the distinction between descriptive and intended conditions
Learn Abu Hanifa's distinction: if a condition (like finishing today) is merely descriptive of the work, it does not become an object of the contract. But if time and work are equally intended, neither is primary, leading to uncertainty.
Example: buying a slave described as a baker is valid; time as an intended object invalidates.
4
Apply to the double plowing scenarios
The passage presents three scenarios: (1) condition to return land plowed (benefit to lessor) → fasid; (2) land requires double plowing → valid (necessity); (3) land does not require it but effect persists → fasid; effect does not persist → valid.
Focus on the concept of 'benefit to lessor post-contract'.
5
Evaluate the conditions based on necessity and persistence of benefit
Summarize the Hanafi rule: a condition that benefits the lessor alone outside the contract invalidates; if it is necessary for the work or its benefit does not outlast the contract, it is valid.
This is derived from the prohibition of 'two transactions in one'.

Source pages p. 572

Commentary
This passage is a commentary from 'Umdat al-Ri'ayah on Al-Wiqayah, discussing conditions that invalidate an ijarah (hire) contract. The commentary begins by explaining the ruling on the word 'fi' (in) when specifying time. If one says 'I hire you to work in this day,' the word 'fi' does not imply that the entire day must be used for work; it only indicates the time frame. However, if both the time (e.g., the day) and the specific work (e.g., baking a certain amount of flour) are mentioned equally as intended objects of the contract, the contract becomes fasid (invalid) because the subject matter is uncertain—each party could claim different entitlements, leading to dispute. Abu Hanifa distinguishes this from the case where time is merely descriptive (e.g., buying a slave described as a baker), where the description does not become part of the contract. The commentary then moves to the condition of plowing a field twice (tathniya). It analyzes three scenarios: (1) If the condition is to return the land plowed (benefit to lessor), it invalidates the contract as it is a condition benefiting one party without being required by the contract. (2) If the land requires double plowing to produce yield, then the condition is inherent to the contract and valid. (3) If the land produces without double plowing but the effect of plowing remains after the contract ends, the condition invalidates because it benefits the lessor post-contract. If the effect does not remain, the condition is permissible. The commentary also touches on leasing rivers ('anhar'), noting it is similar to the plowing condition.

Key Terms
في (fi): A preposition meaning 'in', used for containment, not for measuring duration. Here it does not imply that the entire time must be used.
التثنية (al-tathniyah): Doubling or doing twice; here specifically plowing the land twice.
الإجارة الفاسدة (al-ijarah al-fasidah): A hire contract that is invalid due to a defect such as uncertainty in the subject matter or an improper condition.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi position in this passage, what happens if a person hires a worker to bake flour 'on condition that he finishes today'?
A) The contract is valid by consensus.
B) The contract is invalid because today is mentioned as an intended object.
C) The contract is invalid because the condition benefits the lessor.
D) The contract is valid only if the worker agrees.

Key Takeaway
The validity of an ijarah contract depends on whether specified conditions are descriptive or equally intended, and whether a condition benefits one party beyond the contract's scope.

Ijarah — Hire and Lease
intermediate
8 min
Condition to Return Land Plowed: When It Invalidates the Lease
Explaining when stipulating plowing invalidates the lease

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on a condition to return land plowed in an ijarah contract, identify when it invalidates the lease, and explain the proof from Hadith.

Core Idea
A condition benefiting only the lessor after the lease ends invalidates the contract; essential conditions do not.

In Hanafi fiqh, ijarah contracts are for the benefit of the lessee. A condition that returns a benefit to the lessor beyond the lease term is not required by the contract and may invalidate it. However, if the land cannot yield without plowing, the condition is considered necessary and valid. This lesson examines the rule, its exceptions, and the prophetic proof.

Guided Path
1
Identify the condition and its legal status
The condition is that the land be returned plowed (makrūbah). First, determine whether the plowing benefits the lessor or the lessee.
Benefit to lessor after term ends suggests invalidity.
2
Apply the necessity exception
If the land cannot produce a crop without plowing (especially double plowing), the condition is deemed necessary for the contract and does not invalidate it.
Necessity is judged by whether the land yields without the plowing.
3
Examine the duration of benefit
If the plowing's effect remains after the lease ends (e.g., improved soil), it benefits the lessor and invalidates the lease.
Transient effects that vanish do not invalidate.
4
Connect to the Hadith proof
A condition that creates an extra benefit for the lessor is akin to 'two transactions in one' (safqatāni fī safqah), which the Prophet (ﷺ) forbade.
This Hadith is cited as the proof of invalidity.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
أو يكري أنهارها فإن كان المراد أن يردها مكروبة فلا شك في فساده ، فإنه شرط لا يقتضيه العقد، وفيه نفع لأحد العاقدين، وهو المؤجر ، وإن لم يكن المراد هذا فإن كانت الأرض لا يخرج الربع إلا بالكراب مرتين لا يفسد العقد، لأن الشرط مما يقتضيه العقد، وإن كانت تخرجُ الرَّيع بدونه ، فإن كان أثره يبقى بعد انتهاء العقدِ يفسد إذ فيه منفعة ربِّ الأرض ، وإن كانَ أثره لا يبقى ، لا يفسد.
(أو يكري أنهارها)
قوله : فإن كان المراد.... الخ؛ يعني قال بعضُهم : إنّ المراد بالتثنية في هذه المسألة أن يرد الأرض ربّها مكروبة، وقال بعضُهم : إنّ المراد بها هاهنا أن يكربها مرتين، فإنّ المراد أن يردها ... الخ. قوله : فلا يشك في فساده، فإنّه... الخ، حاصله : إنّ الإجارة تفسد حينئذ ؛ لبقاء نفع الكراب بعد انقضاء المدّة، وهذا شرط لا يقتضيه العقد، وسبب الفساد وبقاء النفع لربّ الأرض ، فتوجد صفقتان في صفقة واحدة، وهي مما نهى عنه رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم. وتوضيح المقام : إنّ ما كان ملائماً للعقد ليكون مفسداً له وللأراضي إنما تستأجر لمنفعة المستأجر خاصة، فكل فعل ينتفع به المستأجر خاصة، كالكراب والزراعة والسقي يكون ملائماً للعقد، وكل فعل ينتفع به المؤجر خاصة يكون مخالفاً للعقد مفسداً له ؛ كشرط إبقاء السرقين ورد الأرض مكروبة.
قوله : الربع - بالفتح - : الزيادة والنماء، وراعت الحنطة وغيرها ريعاً من باب باع : إذا أدركت ونمت كذا في «المصباح»، وقال في «المنتخب»: دخلى كراز كشت حاصل شود. انتهى.
قوله : لأنّ الشرط مما يقتضيه العقد ؛ فإنّ الزراعة لا يتأتى إلا بالكراب، ولما لم تخرج الأرض الريع إلا بالكراب مرتين، فكان شرط الكراب مرتين من مقتضيات العقد، فذكره لا يوجب الفساد كما لا يخفى على صاحب الطبع الوقاد.
Or he leases its rivers. If the intent is that he return it plowed, there is no doubt in its invalidity, because it is a condition not required by the contract, and it contains benefit for one of the contracting parties, which is the lessor. And if the intent is not this, then if the land does not produce yield except with plowing twice, the contract is not invalid, because the condition is among what the contract requires. And if it produces yield without it, then if its effect remains after the termination of the contract, it invalidates, since it contains benefit for the landlord; and if its effect does not remain, it does not invalidate. (Or he leases its rivers) His statement: 'As for the intent... etc.'; meaning some said: the intent of 'tathniyah' in this issue is that the landlord return the land plowed, and some said: the intent here is that he plow it twice, then the intent is to return it... etc. His statement: 'So there is no doubt in its invalidity, because... etc.'; its summary: the lease is invalid then due to the benefit of plowing remaining after the term ends, and this is a condition not required by the contract, and the cause of invalidity is the remaining benefit for the landlord, so there occur two transactions in one transaction, and that is what the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) forbade. And clarification of the matter: What is compatible with the contract to invalidate it, and lands are leased only for the benefit of the lessee specifically, so every act from which the lessee specifically benefits, like plowing, planting, and watering, is compatible with the contract, and every act from which the lessor specifically benefits is contrary to the contract and invalidates it, like the condition of keeping manure and returning the land plowed. His statement: 'ar-rib'' - with fatha - is increase and growth, and wheat and others yield ri'y from the conjugation of ba'a: when it ripens and grows, as in al-Misbah, and he said in al-Muntakhab: 'dakhlī karāz kasht hāsil shavad'. End. His statement: 'Because the condition is among what the contract requires'; for planting is not achieved except with plowing, and when the land does not produce yield except with plowing twice, then the condition of plowing twice is from the requirements of the contract, so mentioning it does not cause invalidity, as is not hidden from the possessor of a burning nature.
Source pages p. 573

Commentary
This passage discusses the ruling on a condition in an ijarah (lease) contract where the lessor stipulates that the land be returned plowed (makrūbah). The passage type is a ruling with proof, expanding on the matn of al-Wiqāyah. The author first states the general rule: if the condition is that the land be returned plowed, the lease is invalid because it is a condition not required by the contract and it benefits only the lessor. However, if the land cannot produce a crop without double plowing, the condition is considered necessary for the contract (muqtadā al-‘aqd) and thus does not invalidate. The commentary explains that the difference hinges on whether the benefit of plowing remains after the lease ends. If the effect remains (e.g., improved soil for future seasons), the lease is invalid as it creates a benefit for the lessor beyond the term, analogous to 'two sales in one' which is prohibited by Hadith. The author also examines the linguistic meaning of 'rib‘' (yield) and provides a Persian gloss from al-Muntakhab. Finally, the principle is reinforced: any condition that solely benefits the lessor invalidates the lease, whereas conditions benefiting the lessee (like plowing necessary for planting) are compatible.

Key Terms
الكراب (al-kirāb): Plowing or tilling the land to prepare it for cultivation.
الربع (ar-rib‘): Increase and growth; the yield or produce of the land.
صفقتان في صفقة (safqatāni fī safqah): Two transactions in one; a prohibited practice where a single contract includes two separate exchanges.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In Hanafi fiqh, if a lessor stipulates that the land must be returned plowed, when does this condition NOT invalidate the ijarah contract?
A) When the plowing is the lessor's responsibility.
B) When the land cannot produce a crop without double plowing.
C) When the plowing benefits the lessee.
D) When the lease term is less than one year.

Key Takeaway
A condition to plow land in an ijarah contract invalidates the lease if it solely benefits the lessor beyond the term; it is valid if necessary for the land to yield.

Digging Canals in Ijarah: Large vs. Small
Expands on ijarah conditions: large vs. small canals.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on stipulating to dig canals in an ijarah contract, distinguishing large canals from small streams, and evaluate the intra-Hanafi dispute.

Core Idea
A condition benefiting the lessor beyond the lease term invalidates the contract; small streams do not.

When a lessee agrees to dig waterways as part of a land lease, does the condition make the contract invalid? The Hanafi school distinguishes between large canals, whose benefit persists after the lease, and small streams, whose benefit does not. This passage from 'Umdat al-Ri'āyah explains the ruling and an internal disagreement among Hanafi authorities.

Guided Path
1
Identify the disputed condition
The passage addresses a stipulation in an ijarah contract requiring the lessee to dig water channels. Determine whether the channel is large (anhār ‘izām) or small (jawāwil).
The text explicitly differentiates between the two categories.
2
State the ruling for each category
For large canals, the lease is invalid; for small streams, it is valid. Note the reason given: the benefit of large canals remains after the lease term, benefiting the lessor, while small streams do not leave a lasting effect.
The distinction hinges on persistence of benefit.
3
Identify the opposing view
Some Hanafis (e.g., Khwāhar Zādah, based on a general statement of Imam Muhammad) rule that all digging conditions invalidate the lease, regardless of size. This is an intra-Hanafi ikhtilāf.
The opponent relies on the absolute wording of Imam Muhammad.
4
Analyze the Hanafi response
The majority (al-Hidāyah, al-Sadr al-Shahid) qualify the absolute statement by the principle that only conditions yielding lasting benefit to the lessor invalidate. Small streams do not, so the condition is valid.
This is an application of istihsān based on the nature of the benefit.
5
Determine the mufta bihi
The relied-upon position for fatwa is the distinction: large canals invalidate, small streams do not. This is the view chosen by Burhān al-A’immah and supported in al-Hidāyah.
The authority weight is ẓāhir al-riwāyah.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : أو يكري أنهارها عطف على قوله : يثنيها ؛ أي لو استأجر رجلٌ أرضاً بشرط أن يحفر أنهارها العظام تفسد الإجارة ؛ لبقاء منفعته في العام القابل. قوله : بخلاف الجداول ؛ فالإجارة بشرط كريها صحيحة؛ لأنه يجب على المستأجر بدون شرطه وإنه لا يبقى أثره بعد العام فلا تفسده، وهو الصحيح. قال الصدر الشهيد : واختاره الوالد برهان الأئمة ، وإليه ذهب في «الهداية»، وسوّى بعضهم بين الكبار والصغار في الفساد ؛ لإطلاق محمد ه ، وصححه في «الذخيرة»، واختاره خُواهر زاده له و به كان يفتي ، ذكره العلامة الحموي
His statement: 'Or he leases its rivers' is conjuncted to his statement: 'he plows it'; that is, if a man leases land with the condition that he dig its large canals, the lease is invalid due to the benefit remaining in the coming year. His statement: 'Unlike the streams'; so the lease with the condition of digging them is valid, because it is obligatory upon the lessee without his condition, and its effect does not remain after the year, so it does not invalidate it, and that is the correct view. Al-Sadr al-Shahid said: and al-Walid Burhān al-A'immah chose it, and to it went in al-Hidāyah, and some equated the large and small in invalidity due to the absolute statement of Muhammad, and he corrected it in al-Dhakhīrah, and Khwāhar Zādah chose it and used to give fatwa accordingly, mentioned by al-‘Allāmah al-Hamawī.
Source pages p. 574

Commentary
This passage deals with a condition in an ijarah contract requiring the lessee to dig canals. The ruling differentiates between large canals (anhār ‘izām) and small streams (jawāwil). Digging large canals invalidates the lease because the benefit (improved irrigation) lasts beyond the lease term, benefiting the lessor. Small streams, however, do not leave a lasting effect after the year, and the lessee is already obligated to maintain them, so such a condition is valid. The author notes an intra-Hanafi dispute: the majority, including al-Hidāyah, uphold the distinction, while some (like Khwāhar Zādah) equate them in invalidity based on the general statement of Imam Muhammad. The correct (sahīh) position is the distinction, as it aligns with istihsān (juristic preference) based on the nature of the benefit.

Key Terms
الأنهار العظام (al-anhār al-‘izām): Large canals or rivers that require significant digging and provide enduring irrigation benefits.
الجداول (al-jawāwil): Small streams or ditches for irrigation that do not leave a lasting structural benefit.
الكرى (al-kary): Digging or dredging of waterways.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Because the lessee is not required to dig canals at all.
B) Because the benefit remains after the lease term, benefiting the lessor.
C) Because digging is a form of labor that must be compensated separately.
D) Because the contract becomes a contract of hire for labor, not land.

Key Takeaway
A condition in an ijarah lease that gives lasting benefit to the lessor invalidates the contract; small streams do not provide such benefit, so their digging condition is valid.

Stipulating Manure in Land Lease: Invalid Unless Necessary or Long-Term
Ruling on manure condition in ijarah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi ruling on stipulating manure in an ijarah contract by distinguishing between invalid and valid conditions.

Core Idea
The condition to fertilize is invalid if it benefits the lessor, but valid if indispensable for the crop or the lease is long-term.

In Hanafi ijarah, the lessee cannot be required to permanently improve the lessor's land without compensation. Stipulating manure (sarqīn) permanently enriches the soil, benefiting the lessor. This lesson examines the default invalidity of such a condition and the two exceptions when it becomes valid.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Act and Condition
The act is leasing agricultural land with a condition that the lessee must apply manure (sarqīn) to stimulate crop growth. Identify the parties: lessor (landowner) and lessee (farmer).
2
State the Default Ruling and Reason
The default ruling is fasid (invalid) because the manure improves the land permanently, benefiting the lessor at no cost, which is analogous to an unauthorized loan (qard) in the lease.
3
Recognize the Two Exceptions
The lease is valid: (1) if the land cannot yield any crop without manure – then it is necessary for the purpose of the lease; (2) if the lease term is long (e.g., several years) – then the manure becomes part of normal farming and does not give extra benefit to the lessor.
These exceptions are established in the school; 'as they have stated' indicates consensus among early Hanafis.
4
Apply to a New Scenario
Given a lease of barren land for one year with a condition to add manure to enable any harvest. Determine validity using the exceptions: if the land cannot yield at all without manure, the condition is valid; if the land can produce without it but manure is just to increase yield, the condition is invalid.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : أو يُسرقنها ؛ عطف على قوله : يثنيها؛ أي لو استأجر رجل أرضاً بشرط أن يضع فيها السرقين وهو الزبل ليتهيج الزرع، فالإجارة فاسدة، إلا إذا كان الريع لا يخرج من الأرض إلا بوضع السرقين فيها ، أو كانت المدة طويلة. كما صرحوا
His statement: 'or he manures it' is conjuncted to his statement: 'he plows it'; that is, if a man leases land with the condition that he put in it sarqīn (manure) to stimulate the crop, then the lease is invalid, except if the yield does not come out of the land except by putting manure in it, or if the term is long, as they have stated.
Source pages p. 574

Commentary
This passage addresses a condition in an ijarah contract where the lessee must put manure (sarqīn) on the land. The general ruling is that such a condition invalidates the lease because the manure improves the land for the lessor's future benefit. However, there are two exceptions: (1) if the land cannot produce any yield without manure, then the condition is necessary for the purpose of the lease and does not invalidate; (2) if the lease term is long (e.g., years), the lessee naturally uses manure during the term, so it becomes part of normal farming. The commentary cites 'as they have stated' indicating this is established in the school. This ruling is consistent with the principle that conditions solely benefiting the lessor invalidate the lease unless they are required for the land's basic functionality.

Key Terms
السرقين (as-sarqīn): Manure or dung used to fertilize soil for crop growth.
الزبل (az-zibl): Synonym for manure, same ruling.
يتيهج الزرع (yatahayyaj az-zar‘): To stimulate or make the crop thrive.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In Hanafi fiqh, when does stipulating manure in an ijarah contract NOT invalidate the lease?
A) When the manure is provided by the lessor.
B) When the land cannot yield without the manure.
C) When the manure increases the land value.
D) When the lessee pays extra for the manure.

Key Takeaway
A condition to put manure in a land lease is invalid unless the land cannot yield without it or the term is long.

The Invalidity of Bartering Usufruct for Usufruct in Ijarah
Ruling on the invalidity of ijarah with rent being a benefit of the same kind.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on leasing an asset with the rent being another similar asset, and explain why it is fasid.

Core Idea
Ijarah with rent of the same type (e.g., land for land) is invalid due to gharar and lack of quantifiable value.

This passage presents a key Hanafi principle: the rent in ijarah must be known and distinct from the subject matter. When the rent is a benefit of the same genus (e.g., planting another land in exchange for land), the contract becomes invalid due to uncertainty. The text provides four concrete examples to illustrate the rule.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Act and Its Ruling
The act is leasing land with the condition that the rent is planting another land. The ruling is fasid (invalid).
2
Extract the General Principle
The author states: 'إجارة نوع بنوع آخر لا قدر فيهما فاسدة' (Ijarah of one type for another type with no specific value is invalid). This is the operative rule.
The phrase 'لا قدر فيهما' indicates that both the subject and the rent lack a determined measure or value.
3
Recognize the Expansion through Examples
The author expands the ruling to analogous cases: hiring an animal for riding another animal, hiring a house for residing in another house, hiring a garment for wearing another garment.
Each example involves exchanging a benefit (manfa‘a) for a benefit of the same category without quantification.
4
Understand the Rationale (Gharar)
The invalidity stems from gharar (uncertainty): the rent is unquantified and of the same nature as the leased object, making the contract resemble a barter of usufructs with no fixed value.
Hanafi fiqh requires the rent (ujra) to be known (ma‘lūm) – either in amount or description – to prevent disputes.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : أو يزرعها ... الخ ؛ عطف على قوله : يثنيها أي لو استأجر رجل أرضاً بشرط أن يزرعها بزراعة أرض أخرى بأن جعلت زراعة الأرض الأخرى أجرة لها ، فهذه الإجارة فاسدة. وكذا استئجار دابة ليركبها بركوب دابة أخرى يركبها الآخر بمقابلتها. وكذا استئجار دار ليسكنها بسكنى دار أخرى ليسكنها الآخر بمقابلتها. وكذا استئجار ثوب ليلبسه بلبس ثوب آخر يلبسه الآخر بمقابلته. فالحاصل أن إجارة نوع بنوع آخر لا قدر فيهما فاسدة.
His statement: 'or he plants it... etc.' is conjuncted to his statement: 'he plows it'; that is, if a man leases land with the condition that he plant it by planting another land, making the planting of the other land the rent for it, then this ijarah is invalid. Likewise, hiring a riding animal to ride it by the riding of another animal that the other rides in exchange. Likewise, hiring a house to reside in it by the residence of another house that the other resides in exchange. Likewise, hiring a garment to wear it by the wearing of another garment that the other wears in exchange. So the conclusion is that ijarah of one type for another type with no specific value in both is invalid.
Source pages p. 574

Commentary
This passage explains the ruling on a barter-like ijarah contract where the rent is not a fixed monetary amount but rather the use of another asset of the same category. The example given is leasing land with the agreement that the lessee will plant another land of the lessor as payment. This is invalid because the rent (the planting of another land) is unquantified and of the same genus as the subject matter (benefits of land), leading to uncertainty (gharar) and resembling a prohibited exchange of benefits without determined value. The commentary extends the ruling to other cases: hiring an animal in exchange for riding another animal, hiring a house in exchange for residing in another house, and hiring a garment in exchange for wearing another garment. The general principle is that ijarah where the compensation is a benefit of the same type (e.g., usufruct for usufruct) without specified value is invalid. This is consistent with the Hanafi prohibition of barter contracts that lack precise measure (kayl, wazn, etc.) in things that are not fungible.

Key Terms
إجارة نوع بنوع آخر (ijārat naw‘ binaw‘ ākhar): Leasing one type of asset for a rental consisting of another asset of the same genus (e.g., land for land, animal for animal).
لا قدر فيهما (lā qadr fīhimā): No specific value or measure in both (the subject matter and the rent).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why is an ijarah contract invalid when the rent is the use of another similar asset (e.g., land for land)?
A) Because the rent is not monetary.
B) Because the rent is uncertain and unquantified, leading to gharar.
C) Because both parties must benefit equally.
D) Because the contract becomes a sale, not a lease.

Key Takeaway
Ijarah with rent being a benefit of the same genus is invalid because the rent is unquantified, leading to gharar.
